# 重阳全真集

**The Complete Works of Zhongyang (Chongyang Quan Zhen Ji)**

**Title:** *The Complete Works of Zhongyang (Chongyang Quan Zhen Ji)*
**Author:** *Jin Wang Zhe (Master Zhongyang of the Complete Way)*
**Volume:** *Thirteen*
**Source of the Base Text:** *The Canon of the Orthodox Dao (正统道藏), Taiping Section (太平部)*

**Preface to the Complete Works of Zhongyang (Chongyang Quan Zhen Ji Xu)**

The Complete Way of Truth is vast indeed!

By *Truth (真)*, I mean the utmost purity without admixture, enduring through the eons, the primordial ancestor of the One, and the great lineage of all things.

In the earliest antiquity, humans possessed pure *virtue/power (德)*, their nature as innocent as a babe, self-governed without need of herding, self-ordered without need of transformation. Dwelling in ease, they found contentment naturally, all enjoying longevity and tranquility—this was their harmony with the Dao/Way in its true essence.

Yet in later ages, human nature grew corrupted, the Dao/Way vanished and *virtue/power (德)* was lost. The original simplicity scattered, the pure became defiled. Lust and desire gnawed within like maggots, sorrow and grief assailed without like spectral flames. Nature swayed with passions, passions were led astray by external influences—dispersed and never gathered, lost and never returned. The pristine essence was exhausted, souls wandered through life and death, chasing fleeting realms and transient causes, trapped in endless suffering with no hope of escape. Truly, this calls for a long sigh of lamentation!

Master Zhongyang pitied the *Miaoxing (妙行) True Person*, who was well-versed in the Three Teachings (三教), penetrating the wisdom of a hundred schools. He encountered a sage at Ganhé River (甘河), found a kindred spirit in the East Sea (东海), transformed the virtuous men of three prefectures, and bound the five communities (五社) in harmonious ties. His teachings saved and guided beings, benefiting all sentient life and embracing all things.

Those who heard of his ways held him in reverence and awe. Wherever his staff and sandals passed, people gathered like mist, seeking his instruction. He never refused any who came. His verses, songs, and miscellaneous writings flowed effortlessly from nature, composed spontaneously for every occasion.

His teachings, broadly speaking, led beings back to sincerity and simplicity, to stillness and emptiness, nurturing the eternal soul’s essence, revealing the wondrous nature of *Suchness (真如)*, recognizing the original face of existence, and restoring them to the eternal constancy of the Dao/Way, returning them to its ineffable mystery.

Someone once asked the True Person: *"Among all beings in heaven and earth, though humans are said to be the most refined, are they not just one thing among myriad things? Who can escape the cycles of yin and yang? Who can transcend the workings of creation? All that begins must end, all that lives must die—this is the natural order of things. Without cultivating extraordinary *qi (气)*, immortality cannot be sought. Without aligning with one’s predestined fate, the Dao/Way cannot be learned. How can one exhaust oneself in rigid asceticism, chasing shadows or grasping wind, carving ice or sculpting rotten wood, for something that is inevitably unattainable, striving for an impossible result?"*

The True Person sighed deeply and said: *"The mysteries of eternal life are within all people. Who cannot seek the immortal groves? Those who fail from neglect are indeed numerous and obvious; those who succeed through diligence are few and hidden. The world believes what it sees and doubts what it does not see, thus deeming immortality a distant, unattainable dream.

Let us test this with natural principles: iron can be forged from ore, gold refined from copper. Fish that leap beyond Lüliang (吕梁) become dragons, wildfowl that enter great waters transform into *fenghuang (凤凰)*. Even ice, which melts easily, can endure the summer if concealed; grass, which withers quickly, can survive the winter if covered.

If humans can sever attachment and abandon greed, maintain humility and hold fast to the One, wander their hearts in serenity, and blend their *qi (气)* with the void, they too can ascend to lofty heights, tread upon the light, ride the breezes of the *Killer Wind (寇)*, and traverse the paths of the *True Person’s blessings (真)*. They can ride the whale across the boundless seas, soar with the phoenix to the azure void, living a thousand years like the crane of Liaodong (辽东), or aging in reverse like the teal of Yè County (叶县). Such beings would stand alongside Anqi (安期) and Xiànmén (羡门), the masters of Hongya (洪崖) and Dongxuan (洞玄), as equals in the ranks of immortals—this would not be difficult.

Across the ages, those who attained the Dao/Way and moved with ease are countless. Yet I say this without evidence: like the deaf who hear no music, or the blind who see no colors, those with shallow insight and narrow hearing cannot truly speak of the Dao/Way."*

The questioner, humbled and awestruck, fell silent and withdrew.

The True Person then opened the gates of flexibility, revealed the boundless ocean of compassion, and rescued beings from the burning house of suffering, guiding them across the vast mire of delusion. He showed them the primordial roots of life and death, the harmonious interplay of *qi (气)* and spirit, the unity of existence and non-existence, the merging of emptiness and form in the realm of dual forgetting.

For those who entered this path, it was as if awakening from the *Southern Grove Dream (南柯梦)*; for those who walked its way, it was like sobering from the *wine of Zhongshan (中山)*. They returned to their original truth, complete and without deficiency, and re-entered the undifferentiated unity; they restored their ancestral Dao/Way, unfallen and unlost, and aligned once more with the primordial beginning.

The nature of the True One is profound and luminous, ever-adapting through transformation and resonance—nowhere does it fail to harmonize.

After the True Person’s ascension, his disciples gathered his remaining works, numbering over a thousand pieces. Their language is vast and profound, their meanings vast and deep, steeped in the true winds of the Dao/Way, containing the wondrous essence of existence. They are the very foundation of true cultivation, the ladder by which others are guided across.

The Daoist communities of Jingzhao (京兆) raised funds and had them printed, though many in the Eastern Prefectures (东州) who followed the Dao/Way found the journey to obtain them too distant. Master Siu (刘), the *Longevity Sage (长生)*, was a beacon of the teaching, a model of the immortal lineage, the foremost master of his age, and the guide for all four directions.

It is said that the Complete Way’s teachings arose in the West, flourished in the East, and spread throughout the world—vast and profound indeed! Thus, he commissioned *Lingyun (灵玉)* Cao, *Lingyun (灵玉)* Lái, *Shoudao (守道)* Xú, *Zhenyi (真一)* Liú, *Tongzhen (通真)* Liáng, and *Daoqing (道清)* Zháì, all virtuous masters, to journey specially to my homeland and request this preface from me.

The *True Person’s* (真人) literary collection is divided into nine volumes, which were then printed and widely disseminated to all directions.

Thus, those who come after may obtain this collection and delve deeply into its words, as one who digs a well and finds mud—knowing water is not far—
or who bores wood and sees smoke—knowing fire must be near.
So that all may awaken early and swiftly attain the Dao/Way,
this is indeed the benevolent one’s (仁者) intent.

Alas! From ancient times, those who cultivated the Dao/Way—
some sought teachers by foot only to find them absent,
others severed their arms to inquire of the dharma (法) yet failed to grasp it,
and in the end, even after years of white-headed toil,
they knew not where to turn,
wasting their lives in vain—
how deeply regrettable!

Now, the *Complete Dao/Way’s* (全真) literary collection
scatters among the people,
its subtle applications and profound mechanisms
clearly visible and easily understood.
Those who study and follow it
will find great efficacy if they earnestly pursue it,
and small gains if they seek modestly.

For those who aspire to the Dao/Way,
to encounter such a time is indeed fortunate!

On the first day of *Great Clarity* (清明) in the year *Great Stability* (大定) *Wuxin* (戊申),
*Fàn Zé Dé* (范择德), the *Learning Officer* (学正) of *Nínghǎi Prefecture* (宁海州),
respectfully composed this preface.

The *First Volume of the Complete Dao/Way’s* (全真集卷之一) *Chóngyáng* (重阳) Collection
Composed by *Master Chóngyáng* (重阳子) *Wáng Zhé* (王哲) of *Zhòngnán Mountain* (终南山)

「A *Seven-Character Regulated Verse* on *The Bond Beyond the Material World*

**One nephew, two sons, and a mountain recluse**—
Together with me, five in heart’s bold quest.
*Six Bright Ones* join the moon of distant skies,
*Seven Pure Ones* call the winds from ocean’s breast.

The *True Marvel* wraps the head in secrets deep,
Upon the *Clear Sky* treads the *Void’s* expanse.
East, west, south, north all turn in perfect round,
Here alone do I know the *Way*’s vast command.

**One brother, one nephew**, two more in this band,
With me, five *Leisurely Ones* seek the *Dao/Way*’s grand.
Bound as *True Kin* beyond the world’s embrace,
We cast off dusty forms, these hollow, fleeting shapes.

A *Pure Quiet* landscape planted all around,
The *Purple Lingzhi* passed from hand to hand.
To *Longhua’s* gathering on the mountain’s height,
I first pay homage to *Penglai’s* lofty guide.

*Master* in *Ninghai* donned in military garb,
With his brother, begging on the streets.
A vast scroll he bore, upon it wrote these two,
To lure *Mǎ Yǔ* along in search and quest.

*Mǎ Sān*, squint-eyed, begged in those days,
Called by others *Harmful to the Wind*.
Five hues of fortune on his body seen,
One spark of *Dao/Way’s* light only he has known.

Eight lines he gathered—*one* swift glance to seize—
Seven-character verses promised, clear as day.
On both sides of the street, the wealthy thronged,
Yet none knew who the silkworm sought.

White for bones, red for flesh, they say,
Red and white together form a hollow clay.
Yesterday they called him *Master Chongyang*,
Today they see him with his brother, begging.

Bodies differ, minds are strange—none grasp the truth,
Faces change, yet none perceive the *Dao/Way’s* proof.
A thousand years of worldly toil in vain,
A hundred years but like a fleeting glance.

*Na Sūn*’s Inquiry
On your own body, speak not of worth or low,
But match the *Three Lights* to *Primordial Tao/Way*’s glow.
Rectify the *Four Gates*, let teaching spread,
One *Nature*’s essence opens wide and free.
In *Cool Tranquility*, you dwell with ease,
At leisure, time itself obeys your decree.

*Elixir of Immortality* stolen from fate’s hand,
True joy unfolds when all desires stand.
To *Master Bàn*’s Question—First Clarity, Then the *Way*
*Release* and *Dao/Way* share one ancient root,
Two forms yet one in essence, never askew.
*True Awakening* sees the heart’s own light,
*Mercury* and *Lead* unite—good seeds take flight.

*Mǎ Zǐ*, do not let rivers shift your oar,
Nor monkeys mimic sands, forever more.
The *Lamp of Wisdom* blazes past the clouds,
Piercing mist to reveal the *Five Colors*’ shrouds.

*Lǚ Gōng*’s Desire to Retire and Seek the *Dao/Way*
With *Three Paths*’ law, he walks with care,
Like ice beneath his feet, the abyss laid bare.
To *Three Paths*’ retreat, he turns with grace,
In *One Marvel*’s essence, he becomes *Pure Clarity*.

Within stillness, he refines the heart’s bright moon,
Where he finds light, his wisdom’s lamp is spun.
A *True Teacher* comes to guide his way,
To *Yùfēng Peak*’s summit, he ascends to play.

*Wáng Gōng*’s Inquiry on the *Five Gates*
At *Five Aggregates*’ mountain, the *Five Gates* unfold,
*Qi* and *Shen* entwined like *Peach of Jade*’s gold.
With *One Decision*, his nature’s light takes flight,
In *True Stillness*, his essence shines—no dimness in sight.

Beyond the world, the *Blue Sky*’s eternal stay,
The *Bright Moon* lingers in the void’s array.
*Blue Boy* presents *Golden Elixir*’s art,
Only *Primordial Tao/Way*’s seekers may impart.

*Mǎ Gōng*’s Inquiry on *Equality*
Come and go must recognize the *Fixed Star*’s span,
Exit and enter still discern the *Luminous One*’s plan.
His transgressions match my own in kind,
May all beings share my heart’s pure mind.

I’ve communed with *Heaven’s* and *Earth’s* spirits bright,
Now I glimpse *Uchang*’s nature—fragrant, clear, and light.
This is the *True Marvel*’s secret key,
If you follow, you’ll reach *Heaven’s* lofty decree.

*Zhāng Gū*’s Inquiry
The *Nine-Leaf Golden Flower* blooms in endless grace,
*Eight Channels of Jade Water* flow at will’s embrace.
The *Seven Gates* open wide—all paths revealed,
The *Four Symbols* shine, yet all dissolve in *Void*’s veil.

One grain of *Divine Elixir* returns to right,
Two strands of *Silver Threads* bind *Primordial Tao/Way*’s light.
Brilliant hues know their own true share,
When fruit is ripe, no lack—only joy remains.

*Grinding the Mirror*
Grinding mirrors strives to polish *my* own heart,
Its depths reflect far, yet still they part.
*Mirror’s* return strips name and gain away,
Revealing *Void*’s truth—no trace to stay.

One spark of *Dao/Way’s* light ignites the *Fire Path*,
A million hues of *Pure Clarity* rise from lofty height.
*Master Jiào* takes the *Mystic Treasure* true,
Hangs it in *Bright Hall* to pierce through ages’ hue.

*In Harmony with the Falling Flowers’ Rhythm*
No need to scheme for lofty flight,
*Blue Cave*’s pearl requires no lock in sight.
Long weary of the world’s vain chase,
I scorn the name and profit, false and base.

How best to guard the heart’s own ground,
Why cling to robes of street and town?
Flowers fall beyond the gates—let winds and rains take sway,
Who will awaken to *Xīyí*’s hidden way?

*Inscribed on the Red and White Peonies*
Red and white silk twisted into clusters tight,
On *Blue Silk* screens they stand in orderly flight.
Fragrance drifts far, no difference known,
Though forms diverge, each holds its proper throne.

Long ago, the world forgot the *Three Islands*’ seed,
Now men mistake these two as one, indeed.
I pluck them now to join their *Tao/Way*’s return,
Each step through clouds and mists, the *Rainbow Crane*’s turn.

*Master Chí*’s Annotation on the *Dao/Way’s* and *Virtue’s* *Classic*
In *Five Thousand Words* of *Tao/Way’s* *Great Sage*’s might,
The *Dao/Way* nameless shines with marvel’s light.
One *Qi* enfolds *Heaven* and *Earth*’s core,
Four seasons guide the *Year’s* *Primordial Mystery*’s lore.

The *Five Phases* unfold *Yin* and *Yang*’s place,
Two *Luminaries* first divide *Creation’s* grace.
Obscure and dim, no words can say,
Yet *Nature’s* secrets hide the *Dao/Way’s* array.

*Sù Xiān*’s Inquiry
Awakening to *Shàohuá*’s six *Ji*’s embrace,
He unites his *One Self* with *Floating Bamboo’s* grace.
No need for incense’s fire to burn,
No need to seek the *Teaching Wind*’s turn.

He opens *Lingming*’s light both near and far,
Lets *Xīngyào*’s radiance pierce east and west afar.
*True* and *False* exchanged—now brilliance gleams,
Each step a *Lotus Flower* leads to *Heaven’s* dreams.

*Xíng Gōng*’s Inquiry on *Seventy-Two Years* of Practice
Even at a hundred, practice is not late,
Only the heart must shift its fate.
This life cannot reach the *Tao/Way*’s full height,
Next life’s promise grants the path of light.

At parting’s hour, one spark must be refined,
The *Three Lights* gathered—none will be left behind.
Cast off the new, abandon the old,
Remove the new—*Lingzhi*’s essence unfolds.

*To Master Xué Dào* Who Seeks the *Dao/Way*
Practice is hindered by a clever mind,
Yet *Golden Adamantine* calls—what’s left behind?
Before men, he boasts of outward grace,
Within, his eyes grow dim—his steps astray.

*True Alchemy*’s key lies hard to find,
*Dao/Way’s* essence rare—*Jade Science*’s mind.
He leaves his wife and sons, what will he say?
Future sins will weigh how light or heavy they’ll sway.»

**To Master Liu Jiang Zhang Yizhong**
Upon receiving Zhang Liang’s *Dao/Way* scripture,
He wanders through fair scenes, finding cool clarity.
His feet tread paths where water and stone merge,
His gaze sweeps clouds and mountains—like a painted screen.
Ten thousand households gleam with three dark birds,
A hundred flowers and grasses share one fragrant breath.

Now I turn back—do not blame my public face,
Yet I ride the southern *Bi*’s emerald *Dongting* lake.

**Spring Rain**
A spring rain nourishes the marsh like butter—
A blessing for the *Tai Ping* age.
Heaven bestows its *qi* to aid the people’s harmony.
The wandering clouds form a canopy—*Three Lights* shine,
Harmonious *qi* brings auspicious signs, nurturing all things.
His enlightened heart grows ever still,
His *Dao/Way*-eyes clearer with each wash.
With staff in hand, he treads the cloud-paths high,
Seeking leisure—his jade carriage overturned.

**Instructing the Simple and Unrefined**
A scholar of *Dao/Way* meets his match—
His crude nature demands harsh refining.
To awaken the blind, fan the fire within his heart,
To open the ignorant, wield the sword of laughter.
If he heeds my teaching and returns,
Let him join our ranks—his fate will turn.

*Ji-ji-ji*—the sage-king’s decree,
Without thought, without care, in blissful *Tao/Way*.

**Alchemy of the Iron Pot**
If black *qi* is destroyed in the body,
On *Badu* Mountain, recognize the *Three Fields*.
Stillness is the return to *Xu*’s emptiness,
In chaos, where shall you seek the *Mystic Dao*?
On wood, seek gold; on water, nurture fire-lotus.
Gentlemen, recognize the *Sword-and-Cinnabar* method,
And aid the *Kingly Wind* with iron-pot coinage.

**Inscription for the *Xiaoyao* Pavilion**
*Xiaoyao*, *Xiaoyao*—this *Xiaoyao*!
Laughing at pines and bamboo, trusting their knocks.
From now on, white clouds come to the cave’s mouth,
No need for green waters or distant mountains.
The *Du* River scholar sighs in vain at filth,
The *Ge* Hall poet mocks in empty wit.
Still, who knows this truth?
Cast aside tortoise hair and hare’s horn alike.

**Master Yang’s Inquiry**
Seven feet tall, his frame a borrowed guise,
His robes and meals surpass three men’s share.
Do not boast of his ordinary bones,
For his golden form stands six *zhang* high.
Awakened, he unites the four directions’ mysteries,
Enlightened, he binds the eastern *Du*’s perfect cause.
His transformed body spans a thousand feet—unobstructed,
Turning the *Dharma* Wheel in the mortal realm.

**Sending Military Judge Brother to Seek the *Anle* Method**
To seek true joy, cultivate the root cause,
Open your heart and leave behind defilement.
In noise, do not let *qi* be wasted,
In stillness, let your spirit be fully nourished.
Naturally, you will recognize the *Three Lights*’ brilliance,
Decisively harmonize the four seasons’ spring.
Externally, your form gleams with clarity,
Internally, your true joy shines—
Mortals unaware, you become an immortal.

**To My Elder Brother**
Who among kin understands the gold in water?
In *Ji Mao* and *Ren Chen*, we each seek our path.
I have already returned to the old *Yunshui* recluse,
Urging you: abandon ambition and name.
The *En* Mountain’s love, the *Hai*’s depths—when will they be crossed?
The *Fire House*’s snares encroach daily.
Do not be ensnared by earthly slopes,
For *Penglai* holds higher, finer peaks.

**Three Essentials for Practice**
Begging for the *Upper* (alchemical substances),
Walking the *Middle* (talismans),
Setting the *Lower* (medicines).
Empty without purpose—this is not the way.
Begging for those who walk talismans and set medicines—
These are the three true practices.
Internally, without purpose, *qi* cannot be refined,
Externally, labor damages the spirit.
If not sought from the origin’s deepest mystery,
Where else shall you find the primal cause?
Here, the *Changshun* scene is uncovered—
Thus, *Xiaoyao* emerges from the six defilements.

**Master Wang’s Request for Release of Life**
Knowing you can observe your own self,
All life is equal—no distinction between us.
Only the form differs, yet all may fly and be whole.
Your virtue matches mountains and rivers’ boundless grace,
Your *virtue/power* flows like streams of blessing.
The *yin* principles are fulfilled—all debts repaid,
His immortal years are offered on the celestial altar.

**Inscription for Master Ma’s True Person’s Hall**
In person, I seek the *True Sage* at *Kunlun*’s peak,
Where ridges and mist lock the *Taihu* void.
Sharp *qi* draws the idle guest,
Harmful winds welcome the colored clouds to dwell.
Golden *qi* forges the true spirit’s nature,
White jade contains the original beginning.
Do not praise *Zhongnan*’s fine scenery—
Wherever the immortals gather, it is as such.

**On the Copulation of Dragon and Tiger**
Do not ask of Dragon’s child or Tiger’s kin—
The single point in your heart is the true teacher.
Adjust the *qi*, steady the spirit, and call for union,
With upright heart and devout essence, nurture warmth.
Equality is the *Great Dao*’s way,
Purity and non-retreat bring true compassion.
Each manifestation reveals the round light,
Guiding the *Golden Elixir* to gather *Jade Grass*.

**Master Sun’s Inquiry on the Three Teachings**
The *Ru*’s gate, the *Release*’s household, and the *Dao*’s path all communicate,
The Three Teachings share one ancestral wind.
Awakened, you know the entering and exiting,
Enlightened, you perceive the vast and boundless.
Spirit and *qi* surpass comparison—
Sun, moon, stars, and constellations may align.
Understanding principles, discerning texts clears disputes,
Above the clear sky, you observe the empty sky.

**Master Ren’s Inquiry on Original Nature**
Like gold, like jade, like pearl—
Vivid, five-colored, spread wide.
Ten thousand rays of light remain unseen,
A clump of dust obscures it all.
Wash and polish to reveal its round form,
Grind and refine to show its original state.
Neither extinction nor birth—leisurely radiant,
Only then do you reclaim its ancient measure.

**The Wooden Fish**
Hollow, heartless, hung in the hall’s courtyard,
Its own strikes echo *dang-ding*.
Its cultivation bears fruit—it draws offerings,
Awakens monks and nuns to chant the scriptures.
Water cannot contain its baited line,
Fire cannot free it from its wooden form.
Suddenly, moonlit wind arrives at dawn,
Blowing apart its clinging vines—its fragrance lingers.

**Ode to Laziness**
I laugh at my own laziness, though called "diligent,"
In dreams, I record the root cause with a brush.
Returning greetings, I keep my mouth shut,
Seeing food, though hungry, I do not speak.
Paper robes, hemp clothes cover my body,
Unkempt hair, filthy face—yet I preserve the *True*.
Nine years in one sleep before I wake,
For fear of toil’s weariness, my spirit dims.

**The Bell**
Cast in the west wind’s likeness,
Suspended in the void, its form honored.
Eighty-one strikes mark the *Yang*’s *Yao* number,
One hundred and eight tolls the *Yin*’s *De* name.
Thus, *Dao* families divide *Zi* and *Wu*,
And *Release*’s children distinguish *Xu* and *Ying*.
If those beside you will long endure its service,
It is the one who truly knows its own voice.

**Congee of Barley**
Honeyed clouds, whiter than frost,
Called *Yazheng*—its fragrance distinct and pure.

**The Jade Scepter**
A precious blade splits jade with light ease,
A silver spoon swirls to pour the nectar’s flow.
The Golden Boy presents fragrant, luminous elixir,
The Celestial Guest chews open light like snow’s hue.
All five *zàng* organs now corrected stand,
Henceforth eternal coolness ever prevails.

**The Drum Tower**
At dusk and dawn, the horn’s mournful cry,
With rapid drums dispels pestilence and calamity.
Water droplets fall in measured time, their rhythm true,
Each clang and toll aligns with fate’s precise decree.
A hundred years pass in relentless nightly pressure,
A lifetime’s bloom fades as each night hastens near.
I urge the poet to awaken early,
Lest the fifth watch’s call steal your clarity.

**Jiang Gong’s Drum Tower**
Its *jīng* blue form holds the Three *Treasures*’ essence,
A towering structure built with solemn intent.
To let its sound resound beyond the void,
And let its pure tones permeate the world.
A single strike of true gold’s thunder,
Shakes the Ten Directions to their own accord.
Great and small alike bow in reverence,
Each one attaining *Perfect Enlightenment*.

**On the Zen and Dao**
In Zen, the *Dao* is glimpsed yet powerless to act,
In *Dao*, Zen’s depths are known—no love nor hate.
The adept who masters both is highest of all,
While the one who gains but one is truly a sage.
Where *Dao*-emotion deepens, clarity stills the mind,
When Zen’s flavor is pure, the heart’s chaos finds peace.
Now cease your Zen and *Dao*—both rise as one,
And naturally ascend to that which transcends them.

**Attending the Governor of Dengzhou at the Qingbai Hall**
Within the Qingbai Hall, a spring of crystal clear,
Its depths profound, its waves both limpid and bright.
Endless it rolls, its flow never ceases,
Splashing forth to nourish those with destiny’s grace.
Through lattice windows, light filters like jade’s essence,
At the door, gusts scatter shadows—golden lotus in flight.
Fragrant mist fills the hall, the spirit’s waves converge,
A pearl of clarity lifted to the azure sky.

**Dawn Awakening**
I seek the original source—its truth is self-evident,
Release its radiance to extinguish all passions.
The Three *Treasures* now pierce through *Right Awareness*,
One mind—why fear it not attain *Perfect Enlightenment*?
Mastering subtle applications, clarity’s depths are known,
Recognizing profound mysteries, purity’s light is shown.
The mortal form dissolves as guest beyond the clouds,
On the Path of Eternal Life, I stride with steady tread.

**Strolling at Xingqing Pool**
With carefree step, I wander through Xingqing’s embrace,
Yet find it but these fleeting illusions’ trace.
Rain flips lotus leaves—pearls burst in splendor,
Wind rolls bamboo tips—jewels cling to branches.
Spring’s verdant green, summer’s crimson lotus bloom,
Autumn’s chill clarity, winter’s jade-like gem.
Through jade’s transparent depths, the source is sought,
But asking of its flow—none know its path.

**At the Zen Gate: The First Rain’s Invitation**
To seek the formless, first distinguish east and west,
To pierce the mundane, see all as one.
On Snowy Peak, I search for *Right Awareness*,
On Crimson Cliffs, I play with emptiness.
These messages are wrapped in spring’s light,
These causes hidden in the moon’s reflection.
Do not cling to the courtyard’s pine’s shadow,
Your true nature is your own ancestral wind.

**The Old Monk on Life and Death**
All my life, I’ve grasped the *Great Vehicle’s* truth,
In harmony with jade’s tones and gold’s voice.
On the path of *Right Awareness*, I climb the lofty ridge,
Toward *Bodhi*, I step beyond the mortal slope.
With wisdom’s fruit, I taste the white lotus’s bloom,
My true nature soars past the *Sacred Tree’s* bough.
From this point, no birth nor death shall bind,
Fixed in *Prajñā* and *Bodhisattva*’s light.

**A Virtuous Friend Asks of Cultivation and the Dao**
Do not entangle yourself in worldly affairs,
For *Qinglián*—purity—begins with stillness.
With wisdom’s lamp, I often prune and polish,
In the heart’s field, I daily till and weed.
Let not the incense of fortune ever fade,
Cut down the thorns of vexation—clear the path.
When the seeds of *Lingyīng* flourish, the work is done,
Carry them forth to offer at *Potalaka’s* gate.

**Master Su Seeks Resignation from Office**
All speak of *Qinglián*—purity’s ease,
Yet none but the *Penglai* Sage attain it.
Beyond the *Wuji*, clouds and mists are my companions,
In half the sky, wind and moon my causes.
To master *Miaoyuan*—effortless transcendence,
Wisdom must shift as swiftly as it flows.
The Master sheds his mortal form,
And here, we speak of years beyond time.

**The Dream**
In joyful play, the outer world draws near,
Yet in the midnight slumber, truth reveals itself clear.
The Seven *Po* spirits dance with demons’ guile,
The Three *Shi* delight in draining life’s vital tide.
The mind-monkey is bound—no defilement clings,
The thought-horse is captured—no nocturnal wanderings.
The four false forms trade in daylight’s fleeting market,
Yet in truth, how different from those who sleep in darkness?

**Master Lü Asks for a *Gold Justified* Verse from the *Diamond Sutra***
The *Diamond Sutra’s* first four lines begin with *Mahā*,
Then seek the six-character hymn’s pure path.
With wisdom’s blade, I sever *Prajñā*’s veil,
To cross the shore and prove *Bodhisattva*’s worth.
To know the heart, to see true nature—this is *Perfect Enlightenment*,
To grasp the *Mercury* and *Lead* of alchemy’s art—*Mìdū*’s sweetness revealed.
From this core, the *orthodox* meaning is found,
Ascending to the *Pure Realm*, leaving *Sahā*’s dust behind.

**Master Yu Asks of Master Su’s Childhood Abstinence**
This cause lies not in mortal feasts,
Nor in fasting’s guise to shape the face.
To nourish *qi*, I drink the elixir’s essence,
To sustain the spirit, I rest like clouds at ease.
When cultivation’s merit fills the measure,
The *Mercury* and *Lead* unite—this world is left behind.
Only when the outer dross is purged away,
Shall radiance return in its full, eternal round.

**On *Qinglián* (Purity and Tranquility)**
Let not the mind’s clarity be strained by turmoil,
On nature’s stillness, raise the wisdom’s blade.
Crush the dust of red passions—find what’s truly gained,
Split the void of black ignorance—know the potter’s wheel.
Through peaks, the moon’s light is my companion,
Beyond ridges, lone clouds are my kin.
As neighbors in retreat, we part in joy,
To wander the Three Isles, seeking peaches of immortality.

**A Layman Jokes of Stealing My Feet**
Fortunate indeed to meet a *Count of My Native Land*,
Would I dare steal your feet to add to my own?
You’ve not yet suffered the Three *Poisons’* anguish,
I’ve already escaped the *Nine Abysses’* bond.
My heart is like the moon—bright and boundless,
My nature flows with *Dao*—pure and unfettered.
Though short my step, long strides shall soon be mine,
And teach the *Eastern Sea’s* soul to circle the world.

**The Inspector of Yandu Asks of Eternal Life**
Your Excellency’s loyalty shines in your question,
Yet even now, the hour’s struck—one toll to reckon.
The five *qi* are clear, their cycles marked,
The *Jia* and *Gēng* days reversed—refine the Three *Péng*.
I seek the golden vessel of ancient lore,
To emerge from the fiery furnace of this age’s test.
Now grasp the *Penglai’s* true path,
And sit firm on *Youtai*—sipping jade wine with zest.

**Master Song Asks of Cultivation**
Polish the mind’s core—let wisdom flow,
And from its depths, jade blossoms shall grow.
In the Three *Fields*, treasures rare await the morning dew,
A single grain of cinnabar withers as the twilight’s hue.
Its crimson glow fades to pale mist,
Its radiance shifts—from white to fiery red.

**The Essence of the Dao: Formless and Void**

From the void’s true display of empty form,
Empty wrapped in emptiness—its nature, void’s own norm.
**Cultivation**—this path so hard to trace,
Turns out to be but the mind’s true, boundless grace.

The crimson-clad noble roams the hills and streams,
The black-hatted sage dives into the furnace’s gleam.
When the white steed snorts, gold echoes in its cry,
Where the green ox plows, jade’s luster never dies.
Heaven-high pillars, earth-rooted radiance gleam,
The *Dragon Embrace* and *Terhapa*’s smallest flame.

Great alchemy’s path knows no end to refinement,
The *Cold Furnace*’s folly belongs to my kin.
Pure winds veil the face—*True Qi*’s breath,
Bright moon’s glow reveals the *Cinnabar*’s wealth.
Ever check the old form, ever polish anew,
And pluck fresh likeness from the void’s hue.

A single spark cast into the azure sky,
Pierces the void—its image begins to rise.
Dragon’s roar stirs the tiger’s wrath,
Snow-waves and winds swirl, tossing in wrath.
Purifying one soul, adding to its glow,
Harmonizing two *qi*—their union does bestow.

The tortoise strides through the waves’ play,
The crimson phoenix alights on the peak’s sway.
One bright moon wheel, its light so grand,
Illuminates the *Sanmao*’s peak, where it stands.
Since first I’ve glimpsed the Dao’s true face,
Today I know the old self’s embrace.

Detached from the world, a guest of the clouds,
Free from the dust, no earthly bounds.
For once I’ve seized the *Cinnabar*’s core,
It’s all been the *Mercury*’s lore.

A spark of clarity returns to the still,
A rounded light wraps the face—*Golden Wheel*’s thrill.
The *Mysterious Pass*’s secret I’ve claimed,
Refined for *Chongyang*—all darkness tamed.

From now on, flames multiply on the wood,
And gold is boiled in the river’s flood.
What god responds to these wonders seen?
One *True Soul*—its awe is mine.

Gathered as form, dispersed as *qi*,
In clear skies, it travels—eternally free.
The *Fetal Immortal* dances, becoming divine,
All from the right path, the ancient design.

Why circle the *Dan Field* with gold and tiger’s might?
No need for the *Treasure Cauldron*—let the dragon ignite.
Scold the *Lead-Mercury* pair—calm is their due,
Swap *Yin-Yang*—they’ll grow ever anew.

A streak of red dawn on the mountain’s crest,
The returning light shines on the *Azure Crane*’s nest.
Clouds severed, the moon’s radiance is clear,
The *Divine Vessel* glides beside the shore’s sheer.

When water and fire meet, the path opens wide,
Wood and gold parted—eternal life’s guide.
*Lead* black, *Mercury* red—south and north divide,
*White Tiger* and *Green Dragon* shift with *Jia* and *Geng*’s stride.

Hold fast to this method—its truth is refined,
In the void, a *Jade Silk Pavilion* defined.
Since the light’s clear, no need for search’s toil,
No petty debate on shallow or deep—avoil.

Seated true, the *Child of Midday*’s seen,
The *Ding-Ren*’s head reveals the path’s keen.
Five hues in steps, one *Dao Mystery*’s tide,
Grasp the void’s marvel—let it be your guide.

Inhale and exhale, subtle and fine,
Nurture the *Pearl*—its origin divine.
*Mother-Child*’s pair follow, hues intertwined,
*Qi* and *Spirit* converge—lights uniquely aligned.

Upside-down union, secrets revealed,
Top and bottom’s clash—*Pivot Axis*’s healed.
To the deep mountain’s highest peak,
Alone, I bloom—*Moon Wheel*’s sleek.

From the start, I’ve learned to twist the winds,
Scatter them in the *Yao Pool*—*Jade Lotus*’s seeds.
One branch grows, its brilliance unmatched,
Five leaves unfurl—each perfect, each matched.

Once I’ve seen the Dao’s profound art,
Now I know its natural heart.
No longer bound by the four seasons’ rush,
In *Eternal Spring*’s realm, years lose their crush.

Cultivate with the *Nine Suns*’ chart,
Know the *Suns*’ lore—all things shall part.
The wise shall transcend the *造化*’s* fate,
The fool wastes effort—his toil’s in vain.

Gained, it’s seen through—void within has form,
Completed, how’s it like—form within the void’s norm?
Void has form, form has void, void’s no void,
Form’s within void—*Heaven’s Path*’s employed.

Know the hand’s start—avoid the *Three Realms*’’ snare,
Scold the past self—this mortal’s affair.
Into the fire, dare to dive and blaze,
Cross the river—no need to drown or sway.

At noon, the *Essence*’s brilliance gleams,
In the moon’s embrace, the *Jade Forest*’s dreams.
This *Great Cinnabar* returns to the world’s beyond,
Free and unfettered—its journey’s unbound.

**The Eternal Student of the Dao**
Empty boasts of cultivation—what’s ever been?
Only to show off before men’s eyes, then.

Hard to grasp the scholar’s void, yet they fear the test,
Unfamiliar with the *Buddha’s Path*—they scorn the quest.
Amidst wealth and desires, they seek to rise,
In wine and flesh’s depths, they hope to prize.

In the world, no sin’s ever been,
Yet Dao’s pursuit adds burdens ten.
Keep the heart upright—no evil’s bred,
The *Three Teachings*’ truths merge as one thread.

When principles shine, what’s left to differ?
After *Mystic Dao*’s grasp, no need to stir.
All things are set aside, pure and clear,
The *Eternal Person*’s rebirth draws near.

Truly longing for the Dao’s way,
No ties remain—my body stays.
In stillness, stillness grows—its grace refined,
In leisure, leisure’s peak—no need to find.

Then I’ll act free, yet know peace’s art,
Days pass with coolness, wisdom’s my part.
No need to seek the *Immortal’s* lot,
Just sit on the *White Flower Lotus*—my spot.

Last year in *Ninghai*’s army I stayed,
This year in *Wéndēng*’s county I roamed.
Two years past, cold to warmth’s sway,
Two seasons through—darkness to light’s play.

This reversal, who else understands?
This *Yin-Yang*’s shift—I alone command.
A single ounce of true gold emerges bright,
No need to forge—it’s already right.

Like this, know the Dao’s outer hold,
The heart and spirit—your guides, your gold.
Ancient cases must be sought and found,
Your own *Dao Wind*—let it be unbound.

Refined, the *Awakened Mind*’s clear,
Filled, the *Old Compassion*’s sheer.
Compassion and purity stand side by side,
Sudden enlightenment—no things can bind.

Know the *Heart’s Flower*—it breeds the wind,
*Mercury-Lead*’s secrets, pure and refined.
Within the *Three Thousand*, use the *Thousand Dawn*’s law,
In ten years’ span, pass the *Nine Transformations*’ flaw.

Hues layered, white’s purity spread,
A single light—red’s brilliance shed.
Void’s reflection returns to the void’s face,
Illuminating true void—void’s not empty space.

How many follow the stream’s flow?
I stand alone—fools’ company’s woe.
When hunger comes, I feast on *oyster rice*,
Cold returns—I wear coarse clothes, no vice.

Poetry cannot split the profound subtlety,
The heart’s *incense-scent* (*xīnsū*) hard to discern.

Not only must one guard it when gained,
But return it to its source—no taxing claim.

---
**A Tea Ode (1–7 characters per line)**
Tea, tea.
Jade cups, gem buds.
Born of void wisdom, blooming void splendor.
Clears the spirit’s *qi*, summons clouds and mist.
Precisely my heart’s affair—
Do not boast of worldly tastes.

One cup stirs Li Bai’s joy,
Seven bowls belong to Lu Quan’s kin.
Only gold can brew jade buds,
Releasing *golden blossoms* through the strainer.

---
**Alcohol, alcohol, alcohol.**
Filthy lips, foul mouth.
Dulls the nature, dulls the spirit.
Diminishes true *qi*, erodes lifespan’s thread.
Half-drunk, the gut aches with sorrow;
Drunk deep, the mind collapses.
To oneself, it invites reckless rage;
To others, no shame remains.
Better never drink—eternally awake,
No harm, no calamity—cultivate the *Nine Nines*.

---
**Desire, desire, desire.**
Brings misfortune, drains virtue.
Diminishes *jin* essence, harms *yè* fluid.
Shatters *qi* and spirit, ruins benevolence.
Can leave the *Three Fields* barren,
Confuse the *Five Viscera*.
Extinguishes the luminous soul,
Exhausts the limbs’ sinew and strength.
Better abstain—enduringly boundless,
No harm, no calamity—eternally flourishing.

---
**Wealth, wealth, wealth.**
Sows sin, acts as matchmaker.
Buys desire, invites the cup.
Further corrupts virtue, invites disaster.
Accumulates the *Three Realms’* suffering,
Makes escape from *Nine Abysses* hard.
Though it swells the family’s fortune,
How can one avoid *samsara*’s wheel?
Better not seek it—constantly content,
No harm, no calamity—ever abundant.

---
**Qi, qi.**

**Qi, qi.**

Destroys the spirit, harms the stomach.
Summons **xīng** (猩) and **líng** (狞)—how foul the taste!
Seven orifices still unobstructed,
Two eyes bright as boiling water.
Dao/Way’s sentiment cannot be turned,
The king’s law—who dares to fear?
Street after street, the **lǚo** (偻罗) vie for victory,
Contesting strength only brings dissipation and waste.
Better not indulge—then all is well,
No harm, no calamity—all is noble and refined.

---
**Seven-line Long Poem: Praising Alcohol**
Cloud-friends and mist-companions always draw near,
Smooth and spicy light nourishes **qi** and spirit.
A full hall discusses the three teachings’ lore,
One cup spreads the freshness of four seasons’ spring.
If you know the scene at the **Zìzài** (自在) Pavilion,
Then you are the **xiāoyáo** (逍遥) one beyond worldly ties.
Silent and drunken, the wind is my companion,
Dark and deep, the moon is my neighbor.
Fragrant vapors swirl through empty space,
Emerald mists layer above and below.
Pure and serene—no thought of life’s affections,
When drunk, I dance in sleeves, seeking truth’s embrace.

---
**Hall of Full Truth**
Its name resounds—**Quánzhēn** (全真)!
**Jìzhèng** (寂正) and **xiāoyáo** (逍遥) expound its essence.
Why use grass huts to shield from rain and dew?
Nor need I dwell in tiled roofs to pass the autumn and spring.
A single idle abode is hard to find,
Yet my **sān jiǎ** (三假) mortal form is its cause.
Ever built, ever maintained, it rests upon the earth,
Sleep and wake—never leaving my body.
Sometimes, after waking, my heart feels vast,
Each time I rouse, my love grows deeper.
**Qi** and blood flow without leakage,
Spirit and essence intertwine—endless and boundless.
The wisdom-lamp shines within, illuminating the **sān yào** (三曜),
Fortune bestows eternal life beyond the **liù chén** (六尘).
Here, the **Zìzài** (自在) Sage returns to the **Yuèdǐng** (岳顶),
Holding **zhīcǎo** (芝草) and stepping toward the **Lián guān** (莲官).
Tea-talk and broth-chatter are my **fēng gē** (风哥),
**Zhīcǎo** (芝草) idly shared—what fruit does it bear?
Do not boast before mortals,
Know that beyond things, laughter is sincere.

---
**The Red Dragon stirs the sea, adding to the fire of separation (离水),
The Purple Flame rests in the furnace, nurturing the **kǎn hé** (坎河).
The Wooden Horse can still follow the Water Tiger,
The Golden Master must wed the Yellow Mother (黄婆).
Mercury and lead have long been mingled—
Now sons and daughters are born in abundance.
Guests depart together, looking back at the crossing,
Teaching you to climb the high slope as well.

---
**Sharing Tea with the Venerable Long Elder**
The gathering is always Daoist/Sagely guests,
Today, celestial **língzhī** (灵芝) is obtained.
Only I recognize its roots when plucked,
No one knows its essence when ground.
Dust scatters—**qióngyáo** (琼瑶) fragrant beyond measure,
Broth pours—**xuělàng** (雪浪) white within.
My mind is clear, beyond life and death,
My **shuǎngqì** (爽气) scorns the narrowness of heaven and earth.
Seven cups of Dao/Way’s sentiment reveal old ties,
One sip of **chán wèi** (禅味) opens the heart’s special path.
Washing away delusion, attaining true emptiness,
From now on, no worldly dust shall intervene.

---
**In Harmony with the Venerable Jade Long Elder’s Ancient Tune**
Wisdom’s gaze is rooted in emptiness—no rise or fall,
Auspicious **qi** drifts faintly, opening distant peaks.
Here, the **Sānshān** (三山) guests often pass,
Birds of the **Jiǔgāo** (九皋) come and go with them.
The lofty towers coolly shower sweet rain,
Washing away all worldly dust’s intrusion.
Divine water surges through the **Zǐjīn kū** (紫金窟),
The luminous **bǎodòng** (宝洞) is even more profound.
Before the cave, ancient **gǔwú** (古梧) trees stand verdant,
Like the **chán** (蟾) in the moon’s deep forest.
Beneath the tree, the **jiānzǔ** (间祖) Sage from the West arrives,
Silent, he lifts his sleeves, seeking no reply.
Now that we’ve mutually understood,
Within **dìng** (定), we search for the **tí** (提) and **qǔ** (裾襟).
Bodyless, actionless—no leakage,
Whether full or empty, the belly’s not concerned.
Teach you to grasp this truth—
The **bā mài** (八脉) infant wrapped in brocade.
Who can make the **tāixiān** (胎仙) dance?
Only I, with the **sān diē** (三迭) **xīn qín** (心琴).

---
**Five-line Regulated Verse: Early Morning Walk**

**Early Morning Walk**
*(Five-line Regulated Verse)*

---

**True Guest of the True Interval**
A traveler on the straight path ahead,
The road ahead now clear and wide.
No darkness lingers in the long journey’s night,
Swift steps take me east or west at will.
Who knows the moon’s midnight glow?
Only I, the wind’s lone whisper.

For the Assembly of Equal Worth,
I seek no gain nor name’s renown.

---
**Ode to Ninghai Military Garrison**
Ninghai’s garrison—wealth in emptiness,
Where Daoist riches overflow.
Mountain-drinking light, water’s height—
Near water, high the spirit soars.
Fine fare nourishes the taste,
The virtuous meet their fate.

Returning light reflects the dawn,
Together we feast on peach of immortality.

---
**Clarity in Practice**
A wisdom-sword swings through the void,
Its radiance piercing boundless space.
The *Mawǎn* scrolls are slashed away,
The lotus of the watery realm is cut.
The Rabbit’s garden blooms with gold,
The Rooster’s hall unfolds jade.

Yellow brilliance, white radiance shine—
This is **Pílú**’s luminous form.

---
**Visiting the Fragrant Severity Temple**
The bell’s metallic roar resounds,
Fish-sounds heard through wooden tones.
Fire-essence incense guides the way,
Water-dwelling treasures fill the vase.

Who grasps the Four Affairs’ truth?
The Three Vehicles’ teachings shine ever clearer.
To fathom this profound mystery—
Is to attain **Round Perfection**.

---
**The Pure Monk Seeks Practice**
With **Amitābha**’s vow in mind,
Cool breezes stir the heart’s repose.
The Three **Yào** must radiate bright,
The Six **Bōluó** must be known.

**Prajñā** ever reveals itself,
**Bodhi** ever draws near.
True **Suchness** calls for awakening—
Joy erupts from **Sahā**’s world.

---
**Self-Reflection**
A single gate of virtue stands,
Guarded by its own good will.
Gold boys bear jade locks,
Jade maidens hold golden spoons.
Closed, none see within—
Opened, only I know well.

Ever shouldered by **Pì**,
In and out through **Zǐlíngzhī**’s glade.
To see **Bodhi**’s face,
One must know **Mìduō**’s way.

The Three **Zàng**’s treasure bound,
The Six **Bōluó** revealed.
All things lack heads or sense,
Each form has roots unseen.

**Jièrán**’s insight breaks free,
Jade nectar moistens gold’s tide.
Qi surges, spirit clears—
Mind at ease, nature serene.

Palaces distill jade nectar,
Double gates forge gold elixir.
Clarity through the Three Paths,
Roundness in a single sphere.
No lack of crimson flames,
Purple light converges here.
This is the root—
Divine light demands sincerity.

Beyond all worldly scenes,
Extinguish all worldly ties.
The Four Seasons breathe the Middle **Qi**,
The Three Lights shine above.

If **Preverted Law** is mastered,
What fear of **Round Perfection**’s lack?
The Dao lies in nature’s length,
The body frets, yet not the heart.

Yellow shoots spread earth-wide,
White snow blankets the garden’s end.
The **Chāinǚ** delights in joy,
The infant laughs with boundless ease.

The **Dāoguī**’s first method stands—
Beyond this, what more to seek?
To walk the Path of Practice,
First ascend the Treasure Platform.

Gazing upward, beyond all bounds,
Looking down, the Wheel of Rebirth is freed.
Pure essence manifests,
Pearl-like wisdom eyes unfold.
Only through **Preverted Law** can one
Turn back the inverted way.

---
**Five-Character Long Poem**
**To the Governor of Shangzhou**
Along the **Pénglái** path you tread,
Jú’s wife’s joy now spreads.
Your carriage rolls with virtuous rain,
Your fan stirs the wind of grace.
Noble banners lead the way,
Ten thousand steeds charge bold.
Planting **Cháng** as **Zhào Bó** did,
Cultivating virtue like **Wén Wǒng**’s art.
Governance shines with luminous light,
Words and nature merge as one.
Ascending to the **Huái** hall’s seat,
Your heart aligns with mine.

---
**Self-Reflection**
The **Sìfù**’s deeds are done,
The **Sānzǔ**’s harm is third.
A glance back—where I’ve been—
I recognize my former dullness.
The True Dao’s eye now opens wide,
Leaping free from **Sìfēi**’s gate.
Already a guest of the void,
Why linger as earth’s lost soul?

Three sacred peaks stand tall,
Four seasons’ warmth enfolds.
All things are **non-being**,
Non-being—do not debate.
Eyes blind, ears deaf—
No voice, no sound penetrates.

Urge them to cease their **Chàngyù** song,
Ask them why they stir the wind.
If not revering sages’ worth,
Why court the harm of fate’s design?

All things are delusion’s play,
All forms are empty air.
Wife and daughter—iron of a thousand *jīn*,
Sons and grands—copper of ten thousand *dàn*.
How do they know of darkness’ grip,
Yet still chase after crimson glow?
Evil deeds accumulate,
Good roots find no shelter here.
Boasting of the body’s strength,
The heart drifts like a floating reed.
How few know their primal source,
How few recall their ancestors’ way.
Would they fret over earthly graves,
Or speak of heaven’s halls?
Only greed for wealth and desire,
Blindness to all wisdom’s light.
If walking the Path of Equal Worth,
One stumbles into **Wǔhuā**’s snare.

---
**Seven-Character Long Poem (Hidden Head)**
**Continuing to Gift to Master Wáng Zǐróng of the Capital**
[...] This **Huá** lineage, **Zǐróng**’s name,
[...] With elegance, we walk the same.
[...] Silk brocade veils the dust of mundane things,
[...] Horses, pigs, and sheep—worldly beasts’ kin.
[...] Nine **tiáo** escape the door’s hold,
[...] Three **gè** flee the chest’s weight.
[...] Born with a jade tablet bright,
[...] A **dānhuán** bolsters the kidney’s root.
[...] If ancestors knew the craft of transformation,
[...] Spirits would soon grasp **Héyōng**’s truth.
[...] Do not cling to realms beyond three,
[...] Seek not peaks above two’s height.
[...] Kunlun’s summit now appears,
[...] Linwū’s cave-heavens sealed.
[...] Light returns to the primal way,
[...] Below, the **Yùzhōng** may strike.

---
**End of Volume One of the *Zhòngyáng Quánzhēn Jí***
**Volume Two of the *Zhòngyáng Quánzhēn Jí***

**Volume Two of the *Zhòngyáng Quánzhēn Jí***

**Poems by Zhòngyáng Zǐ of Zhōngnán Shān (Wáng Zhé)**

**Seven-Character Poems with Hidden Titles**
*"Separate from the Grave"*
□**The Way’s true nature needs no change,**
□**Smoke and dust dissolve—first to transcend.**
□**Lofty and vast, no laziness to blame,**
□**Empty and still, no wildness to feign.**
□**My heart now rests beyond the grave’s dust,**
□**My nature soars as a transcendent guest.**
□**Above, no trace of my former path remains,**
□**Yet seven ancestors ascend to heaven’s plains.**

**To Monk Zhào Shìfǎshī**
□**Earthly ties dissolved, the soil left far behind,**
□**The heart’s release unlocks true cultivation.**
□**The Dao-eye pierces through the *luóhàn*’s veil,**
□**The spirit-root transcends Zhàozhōu’s pale.**
□**Heaven’s treasures rise in celestial array,**
□**On Jīngshān’s peak, clouds brush my brow’s sway.**
□**Black bark sheds, yellow shoots now gleam,**
□**The green ox roars, the white ox gleams.**

**To Fù Tàichéng**
□**Like Fù Sǎo rising from the mulberry’s shade,**
□**Your eloquence outshines the ancients’ parade.**
□**Blindness cured by *gāo*’s firm touch,**
□**Life’s essence preserved—no servitude’s clutch.**
□**The *guī*’s virtue wields *yīnyáng*’s art,**
□**At noon, *shuǐhuǒ*’s patterns intertwine in part.**
□**Fine deeds lost, yet virtue walks its line,**
□**No star obstructs—just clouds to climb.**

**Reflections**
□**The Three-in-One’s scent perfumes the air,**
□**Leisure’s light reveals the Dao’s bright glare.**
□**Lofty and vast, no gloom can stay,**
□**At the gate, all awaken to cool balm’s sway.**
□**Who can fathom the Three Teachings’ thread?**
□**I alone discern the Three Lights’ spread.**
□**The world chases wealth with greedy hands,**
□**Who then grasps this madness’ strange demands?**

**To Wáng Dàorén**
□**Moon’s wax and wane lighten my frame,**
□**Cloud-carriage rides smooth, without a strain.**
□**How could mortal eyes know such grace?**
□**Daoists gather—*qi* and spirit’s embrace.**
□**The ox’s labor none can gauge,**
□**The tiger’s roar I alone can gauge.**
□**Far from strife, my heart finds Dao’s bliss,**
□**First to savor *shèngdì*’s pure kiss.**

**Echoing Chúnyáng Zhēnrén’s Verse**
□**Here, clear springs play their merry tune,**
□**Washing away the dust of mortal croon.**
□**Not all who seek are swept away,**
□**Yet birth and death in cycles sway.**
□**Years of cultivation dawn at last,**
□**Days of truth now stand so vast.**
□**The white lotus blooms in sight,**
□**The spirit soars to *Dàluó*’s height.**

**Exhortation to Awakening**
□**Lose the human form, and *yànjié*’s doom is sealed,**
□**Unenlightened, a hundred years of woe revealed.**
□**The love-ocean’s tide pulls with endless might,**
□**Mountain-enchantment holds the heart in spite.**
□**Each step toward the Dao must be precise,**
□**Yet all still linger in their vice.**
□**Who treasures these gems in life’s embrace?**
□**Awaiting the wasteland’s silent grace.**

**Joy at Returning to Líquán**
□**Flame’s meeting waters life’s full tide,**
□**Three *yuán* now nourish the *dāntián*’s pride.**
□**Years of virtue shape the *zhōngshì*’s frame,**
□**Days of ease crown the *shàngxiān*’s name.**
□**Though secluded in the valley’s shade,**
□**Great Concealment’s truth is laid bare.**
□**Heaven’s decree now lights my way,**
□**Today’s joy at Líquán’s balm to stay.**

**Ritual Offering by Liú, Jiǎng, and Yáo at Zhōngnán**
□**Heart-talk meets the perfect hour,**
□**Beneath, the grand ritual’s power.**
□**The vulgar rejoice in truth’s embrace,**
□**Yet mercy’s touch now fills the place.**
□**Dao and virtue bring vast blessings near,**
□**Ancestral triumphs shine with cheer.**
□**The sages’ thanks in echoes ring,**
□**Heaven knows the names that spring.**

**Self-Narrative**
□**What proof have I of cultivation’s climb?**
□**Beneath, the pearl must be refined in time.**
□**Barley’s nourishment hides in shade’s embrace,**
□**The sun’s cycle turns—no room for trace.**
□**No stray thought lingers, memory’s tide,**
□**No wild roaming—purity’s pride.**
□**Flame’s meeting waters life’s full tide,**
□**With *yīngzhā*’s joy, the age’s pride.**
□**Your verse’s debt now matches gold’s refined,**
□**Rice must blend with white’s refined.**
□**When teeth taste truth, its flavor’s clear,**
□**The *guī*’s path is worn with care.**
□**The maiden’s words now plainly said,**
□**□ *Yīnggē* returns in joy’s parade.**
□**To know inversion’s law’s design,**
□**Observe this song—no words align.**

**To Xuézhèng Lái Yànzhōng**
□**Between gold’s gaps, who can divine?**
□**High friends awaken the Dao’s shine.**
□**Beyond the Three Lights, none dare gaze,**
□**Within the Four False, the heart’s ablaze.**
□**From the pit’s leap, Penglái’s shore,**
□**At the peak’s repose, none can ignore.**
□**My words now plain, yet still they show,**
□**The adept’s path—*Yànzhōng*’s glow.**

**Wáng Dézhāo Seeks the Dao**
□**Tongues may prattle, yet the heart’s untied,**
□**The true seal’s essence spontaneously arises.**
□**Nature’s roundness, full and bright,**
□**Discernment splits the turbid’s light.**
□**From highest virtue, refinement’s flame,**
□**The inner elixir marks the path’s claim.**
□**Barley’s embrace holds wisdom’s spark,**
□**This truth’s name none can impart.**
□**Wrap all things in unity’s embrace,**
□**Within the mouth, myriad forms trace.**
□**Darkness ignites with spirit’s glow,**
□**Three layers of white *qi* bestow.**
□**No thought on flesh, blood, sinew’s plight,**
□**Liver, kidney, lung—no ailment’s blight.**
□**Who can wield and turn with might?**
□**Ask the master—does he know the sight?**

**Echoing Yáng Qīngsǒu of Hùxiàn’s Glade**
□**Skin reveals the fate of *Yīpō*’s slope,**
□**Above, green leaves in verdant hope.**
□**The *shèyún* pavilion’s purity gleams,**
□**Jade’s dew—no deceit, no dreams.**
□**Straight as bamboo, the *sānmèi*’s thread,**
□**Void’s heart thrives through seasons’ spread.**
□**Below, my verse seems blind and low,**
□**Yet winds alone cross peaks aglow.**

**Reflections**
□**Reciting leaves the worldly stage,**
□**Boldly I seek what green may sage.**
□**Thread unravels—truth’s crude guise,**
□**Entry and exit follow nature’s ties.**
□**The white lotus drips with gold’s dew,**
□**Within, red flames bind the jade’s hue.**
□**The child is gone, the hair’s now white,**
□**Behold the moon’s full, unobstructed light.**
□**Fortunate to play as an infant’s grace,**
□**Later, the sword must carve its place.**
□**Beneath, the pearl’s truth none can see,**
□**Within, the elixir’s mystery.**
□**Dragon-wood stands without alarm,**
□**Tiger-waves crash—no fear, no harm.**
□**Entering the *níwán*’s core so tight,**
□**No obstruction to Penglái’s height.**

**To Zhōngnán’s Chief Clerk, Zhào Wénlín**
□**Gold’s barrier holds no sway,**
□**Mortal and immortal bow in awe.**
□**One region’s tax brings vast shade,**
□**A thousand deeds accumulate *hóngyīn*’s aid.**

「□修仁德皇天眷顾，□下恩泽圣主临临。
□位最高谁可议论，□我先保赵文林。

谢南伯公
□谢前亲慧道粮，□蔬珍馔总馨香。
□高膳罢投新墓，□裹安身是故庄。
□髓益筋颜驻艳，□神定气眼生光。

□谁似得王夫子，□了残余好并尝。
□心乞食谢喉粮，□麦须知胜异香。
□觅三餐滋臭腐，□完四假处冥庄。
□肥身体勤行善，□朴形躯老渐光。
□兀腾腾功行广，□婆嫁我味谁尝。

开德府柬傅公送别以诗赠之
□着余心十里因，□凡送路越红尘。
□牛哮吼精光锐，□马嘶鸣造化匀。
□物含和功行旦，□灵明爽气神真。
□人傅友真惺酒，□出阳关有故人。

赠道友
□此幽居我屡来，□方取正道眸开。
□前琼树风前燎，□裹金莲水裹猜。
□目人人瑶性广，□芽个个玉灵恢。
□中清净长无有，□下交伊上宝台。

道友索如何是修心定性
□灵慧照得真修，□要心头裹面周。
□庆先成归庇应，□阳脱后没淹留。
□中莹宝光频出，□上明珠焰不休。
□马搬驮归净界，□然超过大神舟。

道友作醮篆符简
□抵良辰集众仙，□将玉篆遂同编。
□丝不断依从古，□口相传各取阗。
□字金书谁敢悟，□田丹诀我惟先。
□然水木火金土，□一灵符便奏天。

天长观王师求
□遇华宗理性宽，□公真妙彩光完。
□初面目分明旭，□转灵根自在攒。
□德火生红焰锐，□花水涌紫芒寒。
□般已结今先贺，□脉婴儿饮大丹。

文登韩公索修行
□凡修炼妙中玄，□裹通么道可传。
□把五行无用作，□将四象有新鲜。
□能离水金鳞骋，□解迎风玉腕全。
□喆诗词须谢蒋，□公同处洞中天。

赠马钰名
□询修炼好追寻，□寸飙光寸寸金。
□得果成无漏果，□分音韵有缘音。
□辉月耀三田荫，□魄阳魂九转临。
□位玲珑真性钰，□花台上倚瑶岑。

海
□方大水敢谁猜，□浪银涛类大才。
□正三鳌金体现，□初九曜锦纹开。
□通瑞气明蓬岛，□放祥岑耸玉台。
□此波心无地陌，□川东注傲然来。

赠道友韩茂先
□兀腾腾任自然，□中认取水中莲。
□绵俗冗何时尽，□器尘劳每日牵。
□子拽回无一笼，□儿见处有三田。
□分清净公休挫，□上言谁韩茂先。

七言绝句
**遇师**
四旬八上得遭逢，口诀传来便有功。
一粒丹砂色愈好，玉华山上现殷红。

**奏期**
害风害风旧病发，寿命不过五十八。
两个先生决定来，一灵真性诚搜刷。

**端午**
离上新池逢端午，不知谁会伏龙虎。
白云翠雾得逍遥，劝公好把三光睹。

**兄死作**
人人只会哭家亲，谁肯能哀自己身。
若把己身哀得恸，无生路上作闲人。

**知县邀余拜亡灵余不从**
师僧鼓钹赞亡灵，唯有王喆独自醒。
若是骷髅从拜礼，不从拜礼没骷形。

**和武功赵清明**
三百六十金骨节，段段圆明有分别。
地雷震雨出山头，浣濯黄芽调白雪。

**不饮酒**
醒来不饮尘中酒，达后别传物外杯。
莫衒白云随处有，自然举步到蓬莱。

**金丹**
本来真性唤金丹，四假为炉炼作团。
不染不思除妄想，自然衰出入仙坛。

**警知天命**
得势那堪更得时，得时全不畏阴司。
也宜积行修因果，恶业堤防有满时。

**烧庵**
茅庵烧了事休休，便做惺惺诚猛烈，
怎生学得我风流。

**诫潘十四郎省语**
王喆今逢潘利宾，他能绮语敢相亲。
想君舌窍非皮肉，银裹金楞铁口唇。
一轮明月绝纤埃，一片灵光照玉台。」

「A single grain of gold elixir—none recognize it,
A lifetime’s essence and vitality—who could ever guess it?

**To Master Siwu (Four Mulberry)**

The recluse of Seven Pines abandons worldly dust,
The Five Willows Master sheds all clinging ties.
When the magistrate’s fame shall come to fruition,
He may yet call you, Master of Four Mulberry.

Four mulberry trees stand in astonished wonder,
Two broomrape blossoms laugh as if in anger.
Long seated, the cool breeze summons me—
This night, I’ll dwell beside the moon as neighbor.

**To Dong Defu**

In leisure, I wander, seeking the True—
Cold detachment, pure void, my host.
Your radiant鬓 still boast their former glory,
Yet Defu still treads the crimson dust.

**To Master Du of Jingzhao**

Do not speak of white snow or yellow buds,
Nor of lead, silver, or cinnabar.
Ask Master Du of the Great Dao—
Does Kunlun Mountain belong to whom?

**To Monk Dingyuan of Liu Jiangcun**

Jade-named Pal

The fool who laughs at life’s blind snare,
All claim to nurture family’s care.
Yet family’s but a fire to burn the flesh,
Drying clay—when gone, but dust it is.

Now I would counsel those lost in dust:
Seek the Dao’s fruit, the true cause.
A spark of insight—then you’ll see:
Before the wind, you’re but a heap of dust.

The Yang should not cling to Yin’s embrace,
For Yin will mar your virtue’s base.
Refine pure Yang—seven treasures born,
On the Path of No-Birth, no dust is sworn.

At leisure, I sit, watching common men,
Each digging paths where none are then.
Like fish that cling to water’s flow,
They know not dust—yet sink in dust below.

In this world’s wheel, all turn and turn,
Each soul’s nature, each cause is earned.
A hundred years—from womb to dust,
The Five Aggregates return to dust.

Steady the Azure Ox, as ancient sages did,
The White Ox’s branch—its root is hid.
Confucius, the Physician, three teachings blend,
Till fools awaken lest they sink to dust again.

Born and die—ten thousand souls pass through,
Good fruit and cause between the two.
Jealousy, greed, pride in wealth and rank—
I walk apart, beyond your dusty bank.

Who knows the man within the market’s throng?
Do-nothing, act-nothing—let fate belong.
White clouds guide me, wind and moon my kin,
Free of toil, I leave the world’s dust behind.

Men come and go, each watching each,
Hearts calculating, each with cause to preach.
Three Lights shine clear beyond the dust’s veil,
Revealing form—yet all is dust’s pale tale.

**Reflections on the Water Cloud**

I wandered west to lands afar,
Found true gold—firm, unyielding star.
Sealed in the Vermilion Palace bright,
Its glow illuminates, bathed in crimson light.

The Golden Elixir forms in instant grace,
No need for three years, nine transformations’ chase.
If peers could grasp this truth before the rest,
In Spicy Cloud’s depths, their path is blessed.

Alone before the peak’s true face,
Jade blossoms, fair flowers—scenery’s embrace.
One grain of gold becomes the great elixir’s core,
No further need—no need to boil, no more.

Mysteries profound, yet simple to discern,
Silent stillness holds the truth to learn.
Search out the truth from time’s first spark,
No south, no north—no east, no dark.

Master the true elixir by its name,
Uncover subtle truths—growth will claim.
From then, the tortoise dives into the sea’s blue,
Fire peaks rejoice—Jú Láng’s joy anew.

A true treasure’s light begins to glow,
Four Symbols yield to Yang’s pure flow.
Five-leafed golden lotus blooms in splendor wide,
Ten thousand threads of jade unfold with pride.

Before noon, after child—now clash they meet,
Seizing golden essence, victory’s feat.
A mortal head falls swift beneath the blade,
Lifted high—joy to Ding Gong’s aid.

One golden lotus blooms from birth’s first dawn,
Only the sage’s eye may guess its dawn.
Draw in its scent, take it as your feast,
Merge the Two Qi—conception’s feast.

Ten thousand spirits, sharp and keen,
Defeat a thousand evils—no need for a guest.
Alone, its light shines bright as day’s own glow,
Now known—this place holds pearls of show.

On Jade Peak, I pluck the spirit mushroom fair,
Vital qi and spirit—rooted there.
One point of light, yet radiant bright,
Five hues of mist entwine in pure delight.

In stillness, pierce the Five Phases’ cause,
Thus cast off the Four False forms’ embrace.
Return to origin—true face revealed,
White clouds ride steady—one immortal steeled.

The Four False forms now guests to me,
The True within—my ancient kin.
Alone on Three Peaks, who shares my seat?
Clear wind and moon—my three companions meet.

Who dares wield sword or spear with pride?
Dragon and tiger clash—yet I stand defied.
Seizing the Light-Pearl, one bright gleam,
Dissolves the frost of nine cold winters’ dream.

Beneath White Cloud Hall, the night grows deep,
Fine rain and bells—golden drops weep.
Drink deep from Penglai’s cup, I sing,
Slow, the phoenix flute’s sad, sweet ring.

In practice, first discern what’s true, what’s false,
South, north, east, west—all paths compose.
Water, fire, wood, metal—none need be,
One Light-Pearl gleams from the center’s key.

Inner vision finds its kindred soul,
On Moonlit Peak, I sing at will.
Ten thousand verses—who can fathom?
If understood, the heart grows still.

The Purple Spirit Mushroom’s shell first sprouts,
Plucked, then boiled—its virtue brooks.
Jade nectar, fair wine—now mixed with grace,
Swallowed whole—eternal life’s embrace.

Since I’ve won gold from water’s deep,
I’ve used the knife to sever all that’s steep.
One jade flower blooms toward the sun’s bright face,
Crystalline Yang reflects the Heaven’s place.

The Horse-Ape’s caught—now practice’s done,
All things perish—none are born, none run.
Would you strike the drum on painted towers high?
At dawn, why ring the metal’s chime so nigh?

If you would master the elixir’s art,
Preserve the true spirit—keep it whole and pure.
Look upon Kunlun’s mountain’s grand display,
Spicy Cloud’s glow meets Qin’s vast way.

Surname Wang, given name Zhé, style Ming,
Dao name Chongyang—four flavors sing.
One nature easily harmed by wind’s deceit,
A thousand gold won’t buy a high sleep’s retreat.

Now I’ve torn the net of iron true,
Today I leap from dust’s confining hue.
With bright moon’s light, I play my part,
Scattering clouds—good sport to mar the wind’s art.

Mysteries deep, yet logic’s thread is spun,
Frost of silver’s gone—my heart’s undone.
Ride the Iron Ox to plow the Steward’s land,
In every plot, gold grains take their stand.

Do not covet rebirth’s fleeting shell,
Plant in the Jade Pool—let roots compel.
A white lotus blooms, its scent so clear,
Pierces the Heaven’s heights—no need to fear.

True cultivation’s ease, not hard to know,
Dao’s use in observing Heaven’s flow.
Claim the Two Peaks’ true, boundless realm,
Wang’s flower’s core—its cause is warm.

Within the Jade Pool, yellow buds unfold,
Jade petals, gold branches—flowers of gold.
Each bloom, clear and bright, its qi ascends,
Chimes and bells—our family’s ends.

A lifetime’s purity nourishes the Three Fields,
Now stillness may be rightly heeded.
The bright pearl returns to the mountain’s crest,
Clouds and mists bear it to the Great Dao’s rest.

Though you seek echoes beyond the void,
Or chase the bubbles in the water’s ploy,
A thousand schemes, a hundred turns of fate—
How can you escape this final state?

Do not become a ghost in your hometown’s dust,
Soon I’ll return—a celestial guest.

This natural knows its own retreat—no need to search,
That subtle essence, then, must be studied with care.
Call forth the Primordial Child to examine closely,
Luminous and refined, the Purple-Gold Elixir forms.

Bright and flawless, its marvels none can compare,
Five paths’ radiance gathered as one.
Clothed in white linen, it struggles in water’s embrace,
Or wrapped in green silk, it marches through flames.

Four flavors blend into one, everlasting and sweet,
Endless life is thus attained.
Only those who know how to nurture the Purple-Gold Elixir,
Refine it into a pearl—then will it not be hard.

Its light shines forth, ever more splendid,
All hues of the cosmos gathered at once.
Jade nectar flows, yet none may recognize,
Pearl broth surges, yet who can know its source?

Now I alone irrigate the Golden Flower Tree,
Its fragrant scent fills the Four Quarters.
Only I can eat the flesh of the Azure Crane,
Only I can feast on the White Horse’s liver.

Two stages merge into one, all else falls away,
Onlookers shrink in fear at the sight.
Suddenly seizing this Primordial Essence,
Illusion dissolves—its nature is not mine.

One radiant light, utterly clear,
Five colors vibrant, as I will.
Mercury and lead meet on the long road,
Life and vitality forever secure.

Stirring the water and fire’s vital breath,
Parting the smoke and flames to point to the lake.
Sweet water quells the diagram’s chaos—
Who knows the harm of the **Harmful Wind** in the **Final Southern**?
The **Chang’an** streets hold no sway over West or East.

From time to time, I raise my head to the **Storied Seas**,
Reeling in the **Whale and Giant Turtle**—yet they are not the true heroes.

Again I know: **One Wheel of Moonlight, One Clear Wind**,
Inner and outer harmonize—West returns to East.
A single form emerges from **Kunlun’s** peak,
Shining bright, its breeze crisp—now it stands as the true hero.

**To Master Qiu Chuji**
Fine golden scales play in emerald currents,
Seeking fragrant bait, it swallows the hook.
Gently I reel in its luminous threads,
Dragging it to **Penglai’s** eternal freedom.

**To Master Sang’s Son**
Master Sang’s accumulated virtue is profound and vast,
This child of his understands all matters.
Slightly awakened to inner joy, not external delight,
He seeks the moonlight, playing with the clear wind.

**To Master Tang Gong on Seeking the Dao**
True cultivation must not follow worldly desires,
For following them, the Dao cannot be realized.
Serving the same current as others, yet none awaken—
Only when the heart truly understands is the path revealed.

Seeking the Dao and refining the True Nature is no hasty affair,
Ever sweeping the heart-field clear.
Awakening to transcendence lies in severing dusty attachments,
If Heaven had sentiment, Heaven too would age.

**To the Scholars**
All you gentlemen here possess noble talent,
Both sharp and bright, your Dao-eyes open wide.
Do not be ensnared by fame and gain,
Instead, follow me to **Penglai’s** gate.

**To Ninghai Begging for Paper and Banners**
The **Harmful Wind**’s man asks what proof he has,
All techniques and methods are useless—he cannot.
Daily deeds are but this alone:
Eat above, ascend below.

**To Master Ma Yu of Dengzhou**
Speak of the Moon’s brilliance, its light radiant,
Fragrance from the **Cassia Tree** spreads nineteen branches.
At the **Midnight Hour**, when the **True North** aligns,
Unleash its spirit-luster to illuminate the **Jade Pool**.

**To Master Ma Yu**
Master, you once wrote this poem in **Shaanxi**,
When you reached **Ninghai’s** military encampment,
We met for the first time—now I inscribe your name again as a gift.
One farewell at **Final Southern’s** **Water Bamboo Village**,
Your home lacks sons, daughters, or grandchildren.
A thousand leagues away, I seek my true friend,
Guiding you to the **Gate of Immortality**.

**Self-Portrait as a Skull**
This was the **Harmful Wind** of my past life,
Why does he now wander West and East?
Let him roam as a skull in the wilderness,
Free in the moonlit void, his true nature revealed.

**To Master Huang Ge**
Gather wisdom-grass and add broad oil,
A single bright lamp atop his head.
Illuminating the **Five Gates**, all paths are clear,
Teaching him to clap hands in endless joy.

**To Master Sun Ergong**
(No direct translation, as the name appears to be a title rather than a personal one.)

**To Master Sun Ergong**
Your Second Aunt is kin to my **Harmful Wind** household—
Once, the Master twice split a pear to share,
Feeding it to husband and wife, intending both to transform.
A year after my **taking the Way (出家奉道)**, Sun’s family also embraced the Dao.
The pear was split ten times for transformation last year—
The heavens granted a fine hour, the Master’s natural virtue.

Why did you not then **leave the home**?
Ah, you waited only for the **Golden Lotus (金莲)** to be bound.
At home, they called you merely "Second Aunt (二婆)",
But once outside, the **fire of home (家火)** was extinguished.
Leaping into white clouds, you transcended the **Sea of Suffering (苦海)**,
Now I call you **Xianma (仙姑)** in endless joy.

---

**The Impermanence Bell (无常钟)**
The bell rings not by time—yet those who hear it grieve.
They know the world must now **rest (休)**.
Its few chimes follow the setting sun,
Silent guests nod in wordless farewell.

---

**To Master Feng (冯先生)**
A hundred years of light and shadow pass without return—
Turn back, and you’ll see the **mist of illusion (迷蒙)**.
I teach you to recognize the **upside-down (颠倒)** in the scene,
To crush the dust of **mundane particles (微尘)** and trample **void (空)**.

---

**The Perfect Form (圆相)**
One perfect round form, I know it well—
At this hour, **Master Wang Zhe (王哲)** is right.
He emerges from the peak of **Kunlun Mountain (昆仑山)**,
Inviting **wind and moon (风月)** to the **Heavenly Pool (天池)**.

---

**The Weaver (织造人)**
The weaver who spins—what fate has he?
Before the street, he still plies his shuttle and loom.
If he were like me, a **free Daoist wanderer (逍遥客)**,
Would he still weave a thousand threads and endless strands?

---

**Snow (雪)**
The **Six Flowers (六花)** fall against my nature—
Drifting down, they crush **worldly affairs (是非)**.
The **Blue Cavern (碧洞)** warms in four seasons’ absence—
How could they dare to soil my **six-inch robe (六铢衣)**?

---

**Inscribed on Bamboo (题竹)**
They say you’re **elegant in the moonlight (潇洒)**,
But I know your **pure and clear nature (清虚本意)** is profound.
Had **Harmful Wind (害风)** not come here,
How could you be moved to **recite these verses (引动君吟)**?

---

**Inscribed on the Moon Bay Tree at Pure Business Temple (题净业寺月桂)**
Who would plant this **moon bay tree (月桂)** in the earth?
How could it bear to open its blossoms to the **mundane and vulgar (尘凡)**?
I pluck a single branch in my hand,
Then take the **celestial seed (仙种)** to **Penglai (蓬莱)**.

---

**Seven-Character Absolute Poems with Hidden Lines (七言绝句诗藏头)**

**To Master Xu Shoudao, Leader of Pingdeng Hall in Laizhou (赠莱州平等会首徐守道)**
□ **comes** to beg and seek—how shall I reply?
□ **opens** his mouth to praise your **good deeds (善事)**, spreading ease.
□ **holds** treasures, ever guarding them,
□ **knows** his ancestral name—**Xu (徐)**.

---

**To Master Ren, Lecturing on Repentance (赠仁法师讲忏)**
□ **can** dissolve repentance for those who first seek it,
□ **benefits** the heavens, spreading freely.
□ **benefits** the Buddha’s presence, incense rising,
□ **knows** the Master’s **true nature (真如)**.

---

**To Master Feng Wulang of Jingzhao (赠京兆冯五郎)**
□ **abandons** worldly deeds—do not part from your wife,
□ **lovely** children will naturally come in time.
□ **holds** incense, burning it fervently,
□ **reaches** your name to the **Yao Pool (瑶池)**.
□ **words** may be spoken, but none can **polish (磨)** them,
□ **holds** deep within his **jade-like essence (玉润)**.
□ **accepts** sweet nectar—do not blame,
□ **family** will also be called **Pingge (凭哥)**.

---

**Jingzhao Seeks the Master for Calligraphy (京兆来学正觅墨)**
□ **holds** the **Pine Treasure (松宝)** title—**Master Chen Xuan (陈玄)**,
□ **dwells** in secluded depths, far beyond mortal mists.
□ **wraps** the ink to form **three characters (三个字)**,
□ **comes**—this is the **Great Luo Heaven (大罗天)**.

---

**To Master Zhang Qutong (赠张曲通)**
□ **already**—the **benevolent man (仁人)** bears the name **Qutong (曲通)**,
□ **truly**—he has **wondrous abilities (奇功)**.
□ **fields** do not understand the **cool realm (清凉境)**,
□ **holds** the Master’s **fixed poverty (守固穷)**.

---

**Lishan (骊山)**
□ **ever** visits, drinks, and finds true leisure,
□ **between** golden blossoms, distant peaks are tamed.
□ **knows** the gods and immortals come here,
□ **knows** his body now dwells in **white clouds (白云间)**.

---

**The Official’s Flowers (文官花)**
□ **in** spring, the scene is fine—often observed,
□ **views** the flowers, not all the same.
□ **shores** may rise above the **Sea of Suffering (苦海)**,
□ **officials’ gardens (文官园)** hold **Lotus Blossoms (金花)**.

---

**To Master Du of Jingzhao (赠京兆杜先生)**
□ **demands** straightness—**walk straight (直兮行)**, keep your path clear,
□ **sources** pure, **bright and lucid (澄澈)** as **knowing wisdom (知明)**.
□ **sees** the **black jade hare (银蟾)** spitting moon,
□ **bitter** heart reveals a **sweet resolve (甜显志诚)**.
□ **blows** the **jade flute (玉笛)**, dancing with **baby immortals (婴哥)**,
□ **faces** golden blossoms, never fading.
□ **women** sing—do not **recognize (占认)** them,
□ **hears** the laughter, clapping hands **hohoho (呵呵)**.

---

**At the Tea Stall, Exchanging Tea with Master Jia Silar (因茶坊贾四郎换茶)**
□ **divine** wood bears **virtue (德)**, new shoots in spring,
□ **tongue** tastes sweet nectar—**unique refinement (别有华)**.
□ **obtains** the **wind’s essence (风生)**, surpassing even the **staff of the sage (杖柱)**,
□ **old** man rejoices, exchanging **fresh tea (新茶)**.

---

**The Lamp-Stirring Staff (剔灯杖)**
□ **wondrous** body generates **a hundred grasses (百草丛)**,
□ **comes** to pluck and dip in oil.
□ **ends**—he stirs the **dim lamp (昏灯)**,
□ **emerges**, bright light revealing his **merits (功)**.

---

**Inviting Guests to Admire the Qingming Festival (邀客赏清明)**
□ **person** **King Wang Zhe (王喆)** seizes the **festive feast (华筵)**,
□ **longevity**—all guests drink from the **spring of life (醴泉)**.
□ **washes** the **Qingming Festival (清明)**, truly lovely,
□ **meets** this scene—**immortals gather (神仙)**.

---

**To Brother Ji, the Historian (警史四哥)**
□ **Dao** is **not** common Dao—**unharmonious (不和)**,
□ **sweet** heart is **bitter**, grinding mortals.
□ **seeks** the flames within—who can find them?
□ **has** the **evil historian (邪史)** as his **brother (四哥)**.

---

**Guarding the Time Hall (守时堂)**
□ **ever** comes here—**no thought (并无思)**,
□ **loves** the **forefathers (前亲)**, always composing verse.
□ **says** the streets hold **six false cases (虚六案)**,
□ **Time Hall (守时堂)** reveals **peace (安时)**.

---

**In Harmony with Master Chi’s Rhymes (和迟法师韵)**
□ **straight** bow, **bent** arrow—**created (有为)**,
□ **midst** the surging waters, **two forms (两相)** suit.
□ **passes** through **Daoist teachings (道德)**, following the Master’s **commentary (注)**,
□ **intends** **non-action (无为)**, knowing only **self (自知)**.

---

**Daoist Friends Request Cakes (道友请食饼)**
□ **above**—**sweet nectar (津生)**—**bed cakes (床饼)** stick,
□ **within**—**refined essence (秀气)**—my **new cakes (新尖)**.
□ **compete** with three meals—**truly distinct (真个别)**,
□ **round** cakes taste **naturally sweet (自然甜)**.

---

**Requesting Brother Ji to Sing While Sipping Tea (请史四歌啜茶)**
□ **golden** intervals **separate (间隔)**—**no evil (并无邪)**,
□ **rectifies** his heart, riding the **rainbow (彩霞)**.
□ **segments**—**cloud-born things (云外物)**—are joined,
□ **child** turns back, **new tea (新茶)** obtained.

---

**Master Xu Strikes the Bell (学公击钟)**
□ **heavy** words and speech—**well-suited (好相容)**,
□ **opens** his mouth to teach, **do not be lazy (莫放慵)**.
□ **wraps** the **monkey (猿儿)**, first capturing him,
□ **person** rejoices, striking the **golden bell (金钟)**.
□ **wind, fire, water** are now **forgotten (已相忘)**,
□ **within**—**spiritual roots (灵根)**—descend **auspicious (吉祥)**.
□ **you** speak—**truly marvelous (真个妙)**,
□ **this** year will share the **White Cloud Hall (白云堂)**.

□ **wind** **fire** **water**—**already forgotten (已相忘)**,
□ **within**—**spiritual roots (灵根)**—descend **auspicious (吉祥)**.
□ **you** speak—**truly marvelous (真个妙)**,
□ **this** year will share the **White Cloud Hall (白云堂)**.

---

**Inscribed on the Cloud Tablet at Pure Business Temple (题净业寺云版)**
□ **words** strike—**all monks hear (众僧闻)**,
□ **within**—**new sounds (新声)**—**lawful rain (法雨)** divides.
□ **benefits** the heavens, **teaching’s resonance (振教响)**,
□ **sound**—who **awakens (悟)** to the **iron-born clouds (铁生云)**?

---

**Exhorting Master Cui Yanheng (劝崔彦横)**
□ **leaves** **no wind (无风)**—autumn’s **qi (气)** is clear,
□ **heavens** **do not speak (不语)**—how **distinct (分明)**.
□ **crow** **moon** **hare** **fly and run (飞走)**,
□ **I** **rest (休争)**—**no need to exhort (劝彦横)**.

「Inscribed on Master Cui’s Pharmacy (题韩茂先药铺)
□ **At times**, **his nature** **does not resemble** this **child** (斯孩),
□ **At noon**, **his body** **is but** **dead ashes** (死灰).
□ **Extinguish** **smoke**, **dispel** **delusion**—**truly clumsy** (悟真拙),
□ **Encase** **him**—**then** **he sees** **Penglai** (蓬莱).

**Inscribed on the Wooden Fish (题木鱼)**
□ **Its root (根)** is **pure and clear**, **its tail (尾)** **especially** **vermilion** (尤赪),
□ **Its body** **is pristine**—**another** **name** **it has** (别有名).
□ **Within**, **it holds** **pearls** **and can** **meet** **the** **requirements** (能会食),
□ **At the hour of the tiger (辰)**, **it must** **resound** **with** **the** **sound** **from** **its belly** (腹中声).

**Inscribed on the Warm-and-Cool Fan (题温凉扇)**
□ **Bamboo** **for** **handle**, **silk** **for** **face** (腮),
□ **You** **toil** **toil** **to relieve** **the** **heat** **disaster** (热灾).
□ **The hall** **has already** **left** **you**—**do not blame** (莫怪),
□ **I** **have** **another** **favorite** **breeze** **coming** (好风来).
□ **Its form** **is used** **to awaken** **the** **mind** **and broaden** **it** (觉心宽),
□ **Heat** **invites** **wind**, **coldness** **gathers** **again** (复攒).
□ **The bamboo handle** **is worthy** **to hold** **and present** (堪执捧),
□ **You** **have** **neither** **warmth** **nor** **cold** (无暖亦无寒).

**Gift to the Bath Hall (赠浴堂)**
□ **Seeing** **Master Cui’s** **bathing** **hall** (澡浴堂),
□ **His body** **is perfected** **with** **cool** **tranquility** (得清冻).
