□ **His mind** **is** **the** **cool** **realm** (清凉境),
□ **Why** **not** **carve** **his body** **to make** **a** **chamber** (作洞房)?

**Seeing Magistrate Dong Host a Guest and Sighing at Falling Flowers (见董知县会客坐上叹落花)**
□ **The Daoist King** (道王) **Three** **has already** **abandoned** **his** **household** (弃家),
□ **The taste of mutton** (羊滋味) **has long** **been** **forgotten** (久相趖).
□ **Within** **the** **noble** **and** **clad** **all** **sleep** **in** **spring** (皆春寐),
□ **Who** **would** **awaken** **his** **mind** **to** **the** **falling** **flowers** (悟落花)?

**Gift to a Daoist Friend (赠道友)**
□ **Once recognized**, **then** **no need** **to** **seek** (便休寻),
□ **Each step** **brings** **good** **sounds** (好音).
□ **He is** **in** **Master Cui’s** **hall**—**as if** **seen** (如可见),
□ **The man** **handles** **gold** **in** **water** (水中金).

**Master Ren Explains the Three Sixes to the Sixteen Disciples, King Zhe’s Childhood Name is the Eighteenth Boy (十八郎), Thus Awakening to the Eighteen Precepts (戒).**
□ **The Three** **and** **Six** **do not** **concern** **the** **Sixteen** (不相干),
□ **The Eighteenth Boy** **comes**—**examine** **closely** (子细看).
□ **Below**, **Master Ren** **transmits** **wonderful** **words** (传妙语),
□ **Now** **he has** **obtained** **the** **delights** **of** **the** **hare** **and** **suffered** **hunger and cold** (兔饥寒).

**Five-Character Quatrain (五言绝句) [Gift to Master Ma Pin] (赠马钰)**」

---

**Transforming Master Ma Pin, he still refuses to follow.**
**Desiring to lock the hermitage gate and sit for a hundred days,**
**To show the family’s Dao/Way and transform him.**
**Ma Pin asks if the Master is cold in the winter,**
**Thus, he gives this poem to him as an answer.**

**No need to worry about the cold of the King’s Dao/Way,**
**For the King’s Dao/Way is never cold.**
**A hundred days of fierce winds sweep past—**
**When you step outside, you’ll see for yourself.**

**Reflections on My Life**
□ **A treasure** **is** **bound** **by** **the** **Three Fields** (田), **gathered** **in** **abundance** (聚).
□ **The lotus** **blooms** **with** **five full leaves** (叶).
□ **Within** **the** **Jade Pearl Palace** (蕊珠宫), **one gazes** (裹看),
□ **And sees** **a** **single** **radiant** **white orb** (白光圆).
□ **If** **you have** **money**, **you must** **use it wisely** (使),
□ **Or else**, **you’ll be** **too** **naïve** (憨痴).
□ **Do not** **wait** **until** **the** **wild outskirts** (荒郊裹),
□ **Standing** **before** **the wind**, **gritting** **your teeth** (咬齿儿).

**Accumulating Three, Breaking Characters, and Seven-Character Prelude (拆字并七言引子)**
□ **If** **you wish** **to read**, **do not** **ponder** (思),
□ **Three words** **turned** **into** **seven-character poetry** (七言诗).
□ **When** **the sun** **rises** **in** **the** **Jin (金) hour**, **the golden rooster crows** (鸡叫),
□ **You must** **nurture** **the** **jade hare** **within** **the** **moon’s** **palace** (蟾中).
□ **Five-Character Quatrain** **[Gift to Master Ma Pin]**
□ **□□** **Horse** **and** **Master** **meet** (相见),
□ **□□** **Zhe** **and** **Ren** **are bound by affection** (相恋).
□ **□□** **Reside** **in** **the hermitage** (庵中),
□ **□** **Practice** **the** **skillful means** (做方便).

**Five-Character Regulated Verse (五言律诗) [On Master Ma Pin]**
□ **□□** **Ma Pin**, **son** **of** **the** **King’s Dao/Way** (王风子),
□ **□□** **Never** **seeks** **anything** (总不求).
□ **□□** **Divides** **the** **hours** **of** **Zi (子) and** **Wu (午)** (分子午),
□ **□□** **Watches** **the** **sunrise** **of** **Chun** **and** **Qiu** (旭春秋).
□ **□□** **The** **fire** **and** **li (离) phases** **merge** **with** **kan (坎)** (炎离坎),
□ **□□** **The** **tiger** **and** **ox** **emerge** (出虎牛).
□ **□□** **Lead** **and** **mercury** (铅与汞),
□ **□□** **Are** **bound** **in** **harmony** (结成休).
□ **□□** **The** **Master of** **Chongyang** (重阳子),
□ **□□** **Could** **ever** **seek** **immortality** (仙岂求)?
□ **□□** **The** **favor** **of** **the** **Great Cavern** (大洞恩),
□ **□□** **Is** **asked** **in** **the** **midnight hour** (问中秋).
□ **□□** **The** **tiger** **strikes** **gold** (槌金虎),
□ **□□** **The** **ox saws** **wood** (锯木牛).
□ **□□** **At** **the** **beginning** **of** **Wu** (初午得),
□ **□□** **At** **the** **hour** **of** **Zi** (子时休).
□ **□□** **The** **Master of** **Chongyang** (重阳子),
□ **□□** **Composes** **fine verses** (咏好吟).
□ **□□** **From** **the** **moment** **of** **acceptance** (从有口),
□ **□□** **Zhe** **has** **no** **desires** (喆无心).
□ **□□** **A thousand** **works** **are** **completed** (千篇就),
□ **□□** **Ten thousand** **poems** **are** **written** (万首临).
□ **□□** **Exiting** **the** **path** (出去也),
□ **□□** **He** **rests** **on** **high peaks** (卧高岑).
□ **□□** **The** **Master of** **Chongyang** (重阳子),
□ **□□** **Is** **truly** **a** **transcendent sage** (分正仙),
□ **□□** **Lead** **is** **settled** **by** **the** **elixir** (铅得镇),
□ **□□** **Mercury** **relies** **on** **the** **spring** (汞凭泉).
□ **□□** **The** **sun’s warmth** **opens** **the** **trigram** (煦开卦),
□ **□□** **And** **reveals** **the** **penetrating green** (见彻绿).
□ **□□** **The** **spirit** **and** **qi** **emerge** (神气出),
□ **□□** **The** **light** **ascends** **to** **heaven** (光升天).

**Hidden-Head Poem (藏头诗)**
**Book** **and** **paper** **flags** **lead** **to** **Ma Pin**, **Tan Chuandan** **teaches** **transformation** (教化).
□ **□** **Summons** **one** **to** **know** **—** **it** **is** **thus** (呼知已亦如然),
□ **□** **Extinguishes** **the** **smoke** **and** **consumes** **the** **search** **for** **money** (灭烟消去觅钱).
□ **□** **Plants** **on** **the** **land** **to** **yield** **golden** **vessels** (黄器壁),
□ **□** **Grows** **on** **the** **peak** **into** **white-lotus** **flowers** (白花莲).
□ **□** **Directly** **visits** **a** **friend** **by** **the** **sea** (直访海边友),
□ **□** **Seeks** **the** **sage** **beneath** **Mount Zhongnan** (终南山下贤).
□ **□** **The** **pulse** **of** **a** **baby** **in** **the** **wheat field** (麦田整),
□ **□** **Invites** **the** **wind** **and** **moon** **for** **a** **gathering** **of** **five** (邀风月五人圆).

**End of Chongyang’s Complete Perfection Collection, Volume Two (重阳全真集卷之二竟)**
**Start of Chongyang’s Complete Perfection Collection, Volume Three (重阳全真集卷之三)**

**For the Chongyang’s Complete Perfection Collection, Volume Three (重阳全真集卷之三)**

「终南山重阳子王哲撰 词 黄莺儿」
*Composed by Chongyangzi Wang Zhe of Zhongnan Mountain*
*Lyrics to the tune of "Huang Ying Er"*

How lamentable is the floating world’s way of passing through!
Wine and lust entangle like vines,
Wealth and **qi** sink deep like buried treasure—
All mortals follow these paths,
Four evils binding them tightly.

From high to higher rises their splendor,
Each step breeds deeper confusion.
All boast of cleverness and cunning,
Each strives to outwit the other—
All entangled in greed and jealousy.

From ancient times to modern,
How few turn back in time,
Willing to take **Dao** as their master.

Even if one follows the **monkeys and horses**,
Their schemes are ever in disarray—
No way to grasp the lineage of the ancestors.

Only by turning into the barren cliffs,
By plunging into the depths of the earth,
Does one await the final hour’s approach—
Yet still cannot escape the Three **Avīci**’s torments.

The heart’s true nature is the master of cultivation.
Refine the **golden elixir** (金丹),
Let the **essence and fluids** (津液) flow and merge,
Pouring over the rootless—
Nurturing the **jewel-tree** (琼树) with sprouts.

Ever watering the **jade-branches** (瑶枝),
Whispering through the dense leaves—
The **Huang Ying**’s melodious voice.

The **resplendent and refined** (莹灵) sounds and tones,
The bright eyes gazing—
Now the **baby** rides the **Tiger** (骑虎),
The **Fu** phase (兑方) has arrived.

How wondrous—
The **maiden** astride the **Azure Dragon** (青龙),
Four souls united in departure.

From the **original essence** (元初),
First attained—**stillness** (静) wraps **radiance** (辉),
The **returning light** (回光) makes the **embryonic immortal** (胎仙) dance.

It should emerge, manifesting on **Kunlun**,
Restoring the **Penglai** abode.

I do not presume to fancy clouds and mist,
For the **luan and he** birds (鸾鹤) come naturally.

The **flower-heart stirs**—
Lock tight the **heart-monkey** (心猿),
Awaken to the **light** (光) of time—
The dusty, mortal span is left behind.

Begin cultivation with decisive action,
Return to the **original essence** (元本),
This day to discard the **corporeal prison** (骸屋).

First leap from the **domestic pit and trench** (坑堑),
Then abandon the body—
Alone, one finds the **host** (孤宿).

In **stillness** without disturbance,
**Qi**, wealth, lust, and wine—
All swept away, utterly expelled.

The **mundane sights** (俗景) vanish one by one,
Desire extinguished.

One must forsake even **parents, spouse, and kin** (爷娘共妻骨肉),
To attain **freedom** (自在) and **ease** (逍遥),
Falling into **detachment** (落魄) and **leisure** (清闲),
Recognizing the **jewel within the wrapped head** (裹头金玉).

The **jewel-petals** (琼英) and **jade-buds** (瑶蕊),
The **flower-heart stirs**—
Releasing fragrance to fill the air,
A scent of **auspicious radiance** (祥辉) clustering in the **Nine Curves** (九曲).

**Yutang Chun** (玉堂春)
Cultivation attained—
Swift paths open before one.

Both **child and parent phases** (子午) are transcended,
Why cling to **Zao and You** (卯酉)?

Only the **two treasures** (两珍) suffice—
The rest may be left to guard each other.

Let **lead and mercury** (铅汞) be guided to form the **sphere** (球).
Then the **elixir** (丹) is perfected—
All phases revealed, utterly transparent.

Align the **true wind** (真风),
Name spreads, undying.

Search out the **original essence** (元初),
Who else would be the true companion?
Only now does one know the **piercing truth** (彻头).

Again—
**Lock the door.** (锁门)

「Jade’s nature is true gold’s essence,
All may transform—**this is the Way**.

Jade nectar, gold **elixir**—
Ever welcoming, again and again.

Jade hare, gold crow—
Their luminous **qi** ranks second only to the sun.
Shining upon jade railings, sprouting jade shoots.

**Jade-buds**, gold stalks—
Ever flourishing, never withering.
Jade maidens, gold boys—
Ever seen, yet never lingering.

Jade locks, gold keys—
Every door opens beneath.
Praise **Yutang Chun** and **Jade Flower** together.

There is a **Kingly Wind**—
Often sleeping, often resting.
No dreams, no wakefulness,
No calamities, no misfortunes.

White tiger, green dragon—
Naturally mating in harmony.
Water and fire meet—
Above and below, in perfect balance.
This **cause and effect**—
Truly the **original meditation** (打坐).
Let me ask all **adepts**—
Do you still recognize it?

Like me in **cultivation**,
Gain your **merit** through ** Daoic exchange**.
No need for toil, no need for suffering.

**The ancient saying of taming the monkey and the horse—**
**Softness overcomes rigidity.**
**In all matters,**
**Prioritize others, then yourself—**
**Diligently recognize the shifts of fortune.**

**With the Six Relatives in harmony,**
**Friends gathered in perfect circles.**

**Ancestral Hall and Filial Piety**
Sacrifice at the sacred ancestral shrine—
Frequent acts of filial devotion,
Ordered by ancestral rites.

At festive seasons,
Joyful gatherings, toasting and song,
All singing *Manting Hua* in harmony.

**Desiring to Leave the Household**
If one seeks to practice,
Ultimate stillness must be attained—
Free from dust and worldly clamor.

Do not rely on external seats,
Morning and evening, stir the heart’s incense.
Must one diminish wife and abandon affairs,
Leave kin and homeland,
Only then does one return to the One.

When the people are at ease, the nation prospers,
Victory in war and strength in arms.
Enduringly, with ease,
Seek the profound mysteries,
Recognize the coolness of detachment.

Yet the Dao is boundless and formless—
Only in the radiant light of self-illumination
Does clarity arise for measurement.

On *Chongyang*’s day,
Golden chrysanthemums greet the frost,
Alone, one drinks to *Manting Hua*’s fullness.

**On Practice**
When yin is exhausted and yang is pure,
Life halts, nature abides—
First, recognize cinnabar’s wisdom, lead’s knowledge.

White firm, black steadfast,
Earth-Horse follows Wood-Ox.
From *Mao* and *You*, follow *Zi* and *Wu*,
*Jia* and *Geng* converge—
Use *Kan* to welcome *Li*.

When the *Daoqi* arrives,
Shock-Dragon and *Dui*-Tiger,
Crimson Phoenix battles the Tortoise.

Fitting—true water and fire,
*Gui*-Ding’s furnace and kiln,
When the elixir forms, no doubt remains.

Sipping nectar and jade dew,
Divine waters in the flowered pool.
Nourishing the sacred sprout with blessed snow,
The rooster crows at dawn,
The rabbit shifts with the moon.

The Golden Elder rejoices,
The Yellow Nurse stands ready,
Nurturing the fair maiden and the infant.

**The Jade Flower Society of Wen Deng’s Zhang and Shao**
Master Wang’s legacy remains,
The Jade Flower Society convened—
This was for Zhang the Lord.

Then came the Shao clan,
Their halls unbuilt, neglected.
All now regret, awakening fiercely—
The hare rises, casting aside the clay ball.
Do they not know?
A broken string cannot be mended,
Spilled water cannot be retrieved.

Cease, cease—
Each to their own path,
Though I linger with affection,
I shall not turn back.

May all noble hearts remember,
In shared currents of the Dao.
Parting thoughts already stir—
Golden lotus seeds,
Their light fills the Western State.

I must return to Wen Deng’s triumphant scene,
No longer to revisit.

**West River Moon**
Nurturing the *Jia* cannot compare to cultivating nature,
Refining the body cannot match refining the heart.
From beginning to now, all this striving—
Each day’s labor, what does it truly gain?

Seek the subtle mysteries,
Then ponder the profound principles.
A friend who glimpses gold in water
Would not wander in barren fields in vain.

**Recalling the Wandering Prince**
They say the mouth is the gate of calamity,
I say the tongue is its root.
Silence is better than idle speech.
Measure dawn and dusk—
Then one preserves life in tranquil ease.

**Su Mu Zha**
Few bother me, seldom do they gather.
I have no favors to bestow—
Do not blame others for their indifference.
With virtue and frugality, my heart is at ease.

□[Do not] seek their company,
For rabbits often linger in debt’s embrace.
When wealth is plentiful,
All flock to show their affection.
But when money is gone,
Even kin grow cold and distant.
See how the world’s emotions shift so swiftly—
I have fathomed human hearts,
Yet find no remedy beyond this.

**Golden Rooster’s Call**
A warning to Master Liu:
I seize the empty void—
Graceful and refined, peerless in elegance.
Profound within profound,
Wondrous beyond all wondrous.
Naturally, five hues radiate with spirit’s glow.
A single luminous pearl,
Envelops in a thousand threads of dawn’s blush.
Pure and clear, cool and bright,
Dim and silent, shadowy and elusive.
All things in the cosmos gleam with splendor.
Moon wraps the hare’s cry,
Sun wraps the golden rooster’s call.

**Recalling Old Friends in Peach Springs**
On the tortoiseshell branch, jade blossoms gleam,
And coral buds form in secret.
The dark jade leaves are my delight—
Which of the four can truly compare?
In stillness, I recognize the true treasure,
Its brilliance no mere trifle.
Only one knows it for what it is,
Together we return to the **Penglai Isle**.*[^1]

---
*[^1]: **Penglai Isle** (蓬莱岛) – One of the Three Isles of Immortality in Daoist mythology.

**Song: *Nanxiangzi***

**On the Nature of All Things**
All things must cease, cease.
Shatter every form—pierce through to the end.
Recognize the original true face—
Cultivate, cultivate,
A single luminous sprout, steady and sought.

Fire wraps the swift boat.
Flame wraps the pale lotus’ hidden face.
Fragrant and dense before the wind, stretching far—
Drifting, drifting,
Piercing through the azure void to true freedom.

**Admonishing Those Who Pay Homage**
How pitiful these stubborn men!
Wasting strength in crude, futile toil.
Five limbs prostrate to the earth—
Foolishly, still laboring over this borrowed flesh.
The Dao is fundamentally empty and boundless.
Mysterious within, concealing mysteries beyond measure.
Within lies the primal light—yet none perceive it.
Only I, day by day, observe and breathe it in.

No longer chasing after all things.
Waving away, I walk—all matters cease.
Turning back to behold my true form,
Carefree, unbound—where is there sorrow?
Boarding this great divine vessel,
Jade oars and pearl buckets crossing the current.
Surging past the raging waves, all obstacles vanish—
Strategy now—soaring above the Ten Isles and Three Isles.

**To Master Yu on Illusory Transformation**
Illusory forms swirl about.
Lightning’s afterglow ripples on the water’s surface.
Sudden presence, sudden absence—swift as the wind,
Like a storm—
A white steed fleeting past the blink of an eye.

Why not awaken from this empty delusion?
Turn early to nurture the jade sprout.
On it, the golden elixir shines radiant—
Manifest, piercing through the cloudy paths into the emerald sky.

**To Master Shao on Beginning Practice**
My fate is not dictated by Heaven;
Plow the Three Fields with skill, guarding the wondrous mystery.
Sweet rain deepens first—planting the seeds,
Gold coins scattered—
Everywhere, the yellow sprouts bloom most vividly.
Cultivate the jade lotus—
Each leaf distinct, forever firm.
Pearl medicine stirred by the wind,
Fragrance spreading—a single luminous thread, natural and free.

**On the Wind Chime**
The master’s hand delights in new creation.

**The Sixteen-String Zither**

Sixteen strings—each with its own name,
Hanging in the Palace of the Clouds beyond mortal paths,
The wind greets them—
Then they willingly summon their own resonance.
Not bound by the common, but heard in the profound.
Seizing the celestial melody to expound the **Dao** scriptures,
Only beside me do all listen with perfect clarity—
Chiding, I lead you to **Penglai** within the Jade Court.

*Master Xiao* laments the calf that fails to call its mother.
Its nature is like rushing waters—
Swift, the emerald waves flow.
It knows only sweet milk to make balm and oil,
Ever following its mother, wagging its tail, shaking its head.
Into the stream it plunges, then the ravine—
Gradually, it runs wild with no restraint.
Galloping through valleys, untamed by bridle, it follows its own will.
Chasing fragrant grasses, how could it know the woes of tigers and wolves?
Worthy of lament—this calf of the world!

The **Dragon Gate** ox stands firm,
Galloping with the wind’s flow.
Its body smooth as ink, supple as oil,
Charging boldly—dragged back, it turns no head.
When will this suffering cease?
Its sinews strained to exhaustion, it lies in the ditch.
Without cause, it is reviled by men.
Like idle water grass, it cannot escape a single blade’s woe.

**The Wind Chime (Sguazo Society)**
The Sguazo Society’s wind chime—
This wind chime is the music of the **Dao** Immortals.
Seeing a spirit child, within it so bright and graceful,
Naturally it can play in harmony.
Long strings gleam with jade pendants,
A golden flower blooms upon its head, radiant—
Then it sets the Five Directions leaping in rhythm.
At dawn, it lifts its cloud-treading feet,
At dawn, it lifts its cloud-treading feet.
In its ecstatic dance, the true joy is perfect.
Revealing its delicate intricacies—
Clear, resonant, adorned with tinkling ornaments—
It draws down the **Luan** cranes and **He** herons,
Welcoming and sending them in endless flight, together they swirl,
And together they dance, radiating the Nine **Danyao** lights.
On the **Penglai** path, there are vows to be kept,
On the **Penglai** path, there are vows to be kept.

「Lament for Delays in Joy#1
**Zhiqing** (喆) **Sai** (排三), surnamed **Wang** (王),
Courtesy name **Zhīmíng** (知明), posthumous title **Chóngyáng** (重阳).
Like the chrysanthemum, as if to exhale its fragrance slowly,
Waiting for the frost to deepen.

In years of studying the *Yì* (易, *I Ching*), he grew old,
His **Dao** attire (道装) met—
Encountering **Yuánmíng** (渊明, *Mister of the Abyss*), speaking of me in **Jiāxiáng** (嘉祥, *Auspicious Luck*).
Pointing to **Penglai** (蓬莱),
Measuring the **Mǎilù** (买路, *Path of Purchase*) as if returning home slowly,
The land need not hurry.

**Mountain Pavilion Willow** (山亭柳)
Swiftly turns its head—
Clear reasons, clear causes.
Seeking no more in things and matters.
Seeing clearly, each grasp distinct—
All things shattered, free in leisure.

Pure naturally, luminous and transparent,
Clear, reaching the true **xiū** (修, *cultivation*).
Wondrously, within it flows passage and return,
Mysteriously, its surface is searched with fine care.

Brightly, it penetrates the **míngyōu** (冥幽, *darkest obscurity*).
Steadily, it holds the **yínzhào** (银棹, *silver oar*),
Awake, it steers the **Dàfǎ shénzhōu** (大法神舟, *Divine Vessel of the Great Law*).

Swiftly, it departs to cross the **bì'àn** (彼岸, *Further Shore*),
Soulfully, it manifests in **Yíngzhōu** (瀛洲, *Isle of the Sea*).

**Spring in Wǔlíng** (武陵春)
Heaven and Earth honor only the **Zhēnrén** (尊人, *Venerable One*), and he is noble,
The sun, moon, and stars attend him.

The **Dao** (道), **Shì** (释, *Buddha*), and **Rú** (儒, *Confucianism*) teachings are most profound,
**Jīngqì** (精气, *Essential Qi*) aids the spirit in tranquility.

The four **sānbān** (三般, *Three Categories*—*Dao*, *Buddha*, *Confucianism*) are all understood,
**Dānjié** (丹结, *Cinnabar Essence*) transforms into gold.

On the **gǔnshàng** (衮上, *Imperial Robes*), the **Míngtáng** (明堂, *Hall of Light*) reveals its jade peaks,
Beyond the void, it finds its resonant companion.

**Sweetgrass Son** (甘草子)
Dust-bound, unwilling to cultivate,
Each clings to fleeting joy.
Turning again, enamored with glory and splendor,
How could they ever awaken to enlightenment?

Waiting only for **Yīngōng** (阴公, *The Lord of Darkness*) to guide them,
Then they hurry to follow.
Already sent back to earth by their children and grandchildren,
Who now will be their master?
**Welcoming the Dao Guest** (迎仙客)

The Master said:

*"Why, if one practices the Way, do teeth fall out and hair turn white?"*
I reply: *"At fifty-five, I still toil to gather the harvest.
Fifty-five—past half a century—all you noble ones search for me relentlessly.
Eyes dim as if veiled, ears still hear, yet teeth crumble in my mouth,
My beard and mustache now white as frost.
Externally, my form is withered and gray,
Internally, my essence remains black as ink.
Golden flowers bloom upon the earth—true millet and wheat.
Stalks are painted, ears are arched,
Three carts carry them away—then comes the **Welcoming of the Dao Guest**."*

**Lamenting the Fleeting Bloom**
All you noble ones study—do not stray from the path.
Do not let your hearts wander like wild monkeys or inferior steeds.
In stillness, recognize the profound mechanisms at work.
Silent, yet naturally joyous—
Pure and clear, you pull the void itself taut.
When asked, *"Do you not arise nor perish?"*
I answer: *"Merit and practice must be fully realized.
With a true teacher, the path becomes clear, and they come to guide you.
The Tortoise of the First Heaven enters fire—seen with certainty.
The Tiger of the Sixth Heaven plays in water.
Going and returning, they escort you as companions.
Naturally, they are the two households that bind you."*

「Well able to nurture and refine into fragments,
Wrapping the outer and transforming it into exchange.
In the void, a youth of **Dao** is summoned—
At that moment, a single surge pierces the celestial realms.

**Pointing the Vermilion Lip**
The Master first locks the door for a decade,
Then opens it again—
With a single pearl, he cuts it into ten,
And shares it with the **Ma** and **Yue** couple.

Once the door is opened,
Only **Yue**’s household lineage becomes his disciple.
At this point, he bestows upon them a verse.

*"Tenfold Pearls from the Pear"*—
In the year before, I birthed a **sangha** institution.
The two elders and their mother—
Await my teaching to become **cloud-hand** adepts.

I shattered their hearts with my own,
And laughed their doubts away.
From this day onward,
Let them return to their original ways,
And follow the **Kingly Dao** as companions.

**The Graceful Moth**
Admonishing the **Dao** officials:
Seeing one another’s **true nature** (*xīngxīng*)—
A genuine, unrestrained encounter,
Worthy of comparison to the **Great Sage** (*dàzhàng’r*).

Do not begrudge the **graceful moth** beneath the lamp,
For it ruins one’s **fate** (*mìng’r*).
Turn back early and seek the **hidden marvels** (*mìmiào*),
Nourishing the **Dao**’s blossoming youth (*zhīnǚ yīng’r*).

The **Dao robe** exchanged for a **plain hemp garment** (*zàoshān’r*),
Now serving the **Highest Sovereign** (*Tàishàng*) as a son.

**The Southern Branch**
A white egret stands in the **heart of the Jiang**,
A tortoise dives beneath the water’s depths.

---

**The Vermilion Chicken**

A crimson rooster gathers among jade-green bamboo,
Four phases refined in the pot to elixir’s gold.
The five flavors blend in harmony’s feast,
The *Chónglóu* plant trusted as sustenance.

Filling the six *fǔ* organs brings peace and health,
Nurturing the *Zhēnshén*—vital essence leaps into the *xiān tán*’s hall.

They sigh at the wind’s flickering candle,
They lament the water’s drowned corpse.
Birth and death in endless cycle—when will it cease?
Like the wheel’s turning, boundless in *liú*’s endless flow.

Know the donkey and the horse,
Yet not ignore the mule and the ox.
How does one escape this fate?
Fortunate in human form, now hasten to perfect *Zhēnxiū*.

**Night Palace Tour**

My body rests in deep mountains, drifting with ease,
Ascending green peaks, free as I please.
Cold, I wear coarse grass robes; weary, I sleep.
Feasting on pine, when thirst comes, I drink clear streams.

Nurturing *shén* and *qì* in balance, I know no want—
No chill, no hunger, no restlessness.
I’ve claimed the land of *xiāoyáo*, pure and free.

In joyful ease, I enter crimson clouds,
Enveloped in emerald mist.
I revel in the *Jiāngshén*’s grace.

**Empty Within, Void Without**

I see the fullness in the hollow, boundless *yíngyíng*.
Delight in the path ahead, clear as day.
I’ve found the *Zhēnshén*—firm and true,
With *huì*’s light guiding my newfound way.

Five gates open, passage free and wide,
Come and go as I will, roaming at my leisure.
On towering peaks, I move with ease,
Weaving cloud canopies, my might is fierce.

One form shines with *língguāng*—mystic radiance,
A single point like crimson cherry’s essence.
Colors swathe me in endless, tranquil embrace,
In cool serenity, my life eternal.

**Praise for the Sacred Reign**

To cultivate the *Dao*, one must wear simple cloth,
And take the meal of *jìngliáo*—silent, pure.
The *Dao* heart differs from the common mind,
Severing cares, free from all thought’s bind.

Within, I recognize the *Jīnwū*’s gathering gold,
And the *Yùtù*’s moonlit, luminous fold.
The *Chìluán* clutches the *Hēiguī*’s essence bright—
Who among you grasps this truth’s pure light?

**Longing for the Dao**

Zhōugōng’s question: *"How to know the heart, to see the nature?"*
Do not recite, do not chase—
This *Xuánjī* is deepest, most profound.
How can one discern the *Běnxīn*’s ground?

Seize it with skill, or scale its heights.
A lone moon wheel gleams on jade peaks,
Only then does one know—water enfolds gold.

**The Curtain Rises**

Téngqí releases the tortoise—
This *shén guī*, deep thanks I owe.
Your *Dù* vast, your grace profound,
In endless *míngmíng*—radiant, boundless glow.

Like *Máo Bǎo*’s return to shore,
You honor me with your praise.
I bow in jest, with *Jīnlian*’s grace,
And *yì*’s humble embrace.

A thousand years of *xiálíng*—longevity’s span,
Now my life’s joy grows ever grand.
My spirit brightens, clear and strong,
In one breath, I lift you to the clouds’ throng.

---

**#2**
*Again, the monk of Qin渡 Funeral Grounds seeks instruction*
Look well upon the scriptures, know how to offer repentance.
With gold-faced rouge, dip again and again—
The swirling hue grows deep, never fading thin.
Its color wraps the Perfect Truth,
And Perfect Truth becomes clear and luminous.

Hold the lead pen, brandish the mercury tool—
Carve through darkness, through the murky night,
To reveal the dazzling silver clouds.
Ten thousand rays of radiance converge in one point.

*Prajñāpāramitā*’s waves—
Gained and gained, yet never more or less.
Do not cling to the body,
Nor sit in vain meditation.
Agitate the marrow, shake the sinews,
Suckle thick, viscous saliva—
External practices bring no resonance.
You weary your spirit, waste your efforts in vain.

Act as you will, like one asleep.
Just pierce the heart’s single thread—
The reflected light reveals itself:
Five-colored radiance enfolds the luminous pearls,
The Five-Peak Mountains, their threefold brilliance.
All Eight Consciousnesses illuminated,
The Four Symbols’ spirit light encircling.
The *Arhats* turn to see the *Bodhisattvas*—
The fruit of Buddhahood is complete,
Here, no words can answer.

Attain the *Void* (*śūnyatā*)—then you are free.
Pure and serene, all supported,
Clear and bright, their harmony complete.
Do not divide the spirit pearls by rank—
Their hues transmit their splendor.
The Golden Pagoda manifests anew.

---

*Again, to Brother Tán and Brother Táng*
Teach all people:
Do not toil ceaselessly.
Search for hidden mysteries,
Cultivate *merit* and *wisdom* (*huì*).
Light the lamp to scrutinize the nature.

Carefully nurture your form—
Eat and drink to secure your fate.
Bow to the wind as uncle,
Two by two.
Nephew, do not cling—
I press you with urgent words.
Follow the new precepts, clear and refined,
*Tánglín*’s truth, *Dàdá*’s essence.

---

*Again, to the Apothecary Master Zhào of Jīngzhào*
Master Zhào, invited to feast,
Eats water-rice.
Pearl by pearl, grain by grain—
*Lingzhi* mushrooms, their roots entwined.
Consumed, they birth the luminous garden.
Open the *Lotus Sutra*’s radiant blossoms,
No longer bound to mortal flesh.

Merge the Three Lights,
Divide the Four Symbols.
Strengthen your spirit—
The child of the treasure cauldron thrives.
Five-colored radiance fills one foundation,
This is the fullness of a lifetime’s wish.

---

*Again, exhorting the people of Líqúan*
People of Líqúan, all do good.
Time flees swift—like water, like an arrow.
Do not boast of empty honors.
Your mortal forms are fleeting,
Like silkworms knowing their fate.
Each is bound and tangled,
Praising their cocoons.
Wrapped in true essence,
They wait for the pot’s searing.
This is King Sān’s expedient means—
Before belief, no harm in windy faces.

---

Break apart the finest dust,
Leap forth from the Three Peaks’ gate.
Moon rises in the east,
Sun sets in the *yǒu* direction.

Shining stars, three in step,
Their radiant light follows.
Pass the *qi* pure,
Move the spirit refined.
When the two meridians harmonize,
True practice and true power are achieved.

Piercing the clear sky’s brilliance,
Only then does *wuwei* reveal itself—
At last, the path to *wú lòu* is seen.

---

**Again, presenting to the Duke of Jingzhao, Wang Xiaoliu**

This virtuous man,
Skilled in martial arts and agility.
When asked of my practice,
He speaks of extraordinary intent.
Yet how can he escape
The burden of time and family affairs?
And there’s another matter—
Wives and children are hard to abandon.

I advise Master Ming:
Do not seek *chūlí*—
Burn incense daily,
Cherish the Three Lights’ nobility.
With a mind full of expedient means,
Year by year, step by step,
You’ll reach the clouds and mists wrapped in radiance.

---

**Again, exhorting those in cultivation**

Do not practice *gōng*,
Cease not sitting in meditation.
If you wish to cultivate,
First tame the heart-monkey.
Draw in the black *qi*—
Break through to *wú lòu*.
Slowly ascend and nurture,
Preserve your spirit-essence.

The dark maiden plays,
The infant sleeps.
Lifted to the Central Field,
Passing through the Bright Hall.
A single white *lotus* folded,
Carried into the void,
Pearls released, one by one.

The tears flow thick and the saliva pools—
Consumed, they drain the vital essence.
The dregs of the Five Grains linger, hard to transmute.
Just fodder for the hungry ghost—
What need for idle vexation?

He who knows cultivation understands inversion.
Another taste exists—
Naturally divine.
The Spirit-Waters and Flower-Pools align with the True Dao,
Irrigating the Elixir Field,
Soon returning to Penglai Isle.

---

**To the Cart-Driver**
Wood has no sentiment, yet it acts.
Skilled hands shape its form—
A hollow shell.
The black ox strains, the yellow ox pulls taut,
Drawn into the red dust—
How can it escape the wheel of rebirth?
Busy in stillness, active in leisure—
How to attain true ease, unbounded joy?
Only when the white ox leaps,
A single lotus blooms,
A myriad rays of radiance flare.

---

**Exhorting the World**
The human body—like dew on grass—
Morning light dries it back to dust.
A hundred years’ span is fleeting.
Yet cling to the dusty world,
Willingly enduring hardship’s sting.
Hear me, all who listen:
Break free from the mundane cage,
Seek the path of eternal life.
Turn back soon, yet still you linger—
On the Seven Treasures Peak,
Become a companion of the clouds and mists.

To Penglai Isle #3—
The hermitage burned, yet fruit remains.
Two disciples from Ninghai return to rebuild.
Master Zhongyang—
Nothing is pursued.
Clouds and waters drift in carefree play—
The thatched hut burned, yet all is at rest.
Another fine return awaits.
Preserve the foundation—
Future generations will restore it.
Even as a refined Daoist precept,
How can one emulate my elegance?
I have already gone to Yingzhou.

---

**Seeking Money at the Liquor Spring**
The Liquor Spring is fine,
Yet it favors the poor child.
To shatter the empty illusions of desire,
I seize the foolish monkey’s hand.
No sons, no daughters—
On both sides of the street,
I beg for small coins.
Together, let us buy golden barley-rice,
Feeding the iron ox three times daily.
Tending the aged infant.
The True Dao can unite *kàn* and *lí*—
Recognize where the Five Phases do not reach—
Before parents gave you birth.
This truth is not hard to know.
Reflect swiftly—
Begin cultivation now.
Above, the Three Lights shine eternally,
Within, the Two *Qi* must not be divided.
Pluck the Jade Spirit-Mushroom.
The cultivator must seek the path ahead.
Dark and obscure, stripping away self,
Dull and silent, severing human ties.
In the True embrace lies purity.
Only then does one awaken—
Leisurely, reaching clarity within emptiness.
All things shattered, clear as day.
Cultivation’s work—
Carefully laid out.
Externally, the Four Limbs’ comforts,
Internally, the Five Viscera’s inversion—
This is True Wholeness.
Firmly guard the foundation,
Nurture the shell with diligence.
The Two *Qi* harmonize, opening innate nature,
The Three Fields are moved, aiding spirit and essence.
Only this summons the Immortal.
The True Great Medicine—
Its brilliance is evident.
The Two *Qi* enfold the Threefold Refined,
Double-sealed, locking the Ninefold Mysteries.
Who understands this need not be taught.
Ancient hymns of the Immortals—
Two lines hold the deepest study.

「To cross the river, ordinary bones indeed need a raft,
Yet sages reach the shore without need of a boat.
Ascending beyond the harm of the *prevalent winds*,
Where monkeys and horses dwell—
Life and *Dao* naturally known.

A single grain of *Dao-qi* opens the Four *Xiàng* (phenomena),
Two methods of *sword-fist* slay the Three *Shī* (corpse-spirits).
Divine water irrigates the *Huá Chí* (flowering pool).
Observe well—
This is the *Kàn* (water) and *Lí* (fire) hexagrams.

Earth-horses drive back the Golden Tiger,
Iron oxen plow forth the Jade Dragon.
Only then does one meet a True Teacher.

True *forging* and *cultivation*—
Driving away illusions, dispelling confusion.
Crushing the moonlit path to reveal the straight way,
Splitting the wind-scape to enter the *Mystic Gate*.
Only then does the *Dao* family’s honor shine.

No grasp needed—
A single point reveals *Kūnlún* (the sacred peak).
Returning to dwell in the void, transcending *造化* (*Zào Huà*, the Creative Transformation),
Obtaining return beyond the world, surpassing *乾坤* (*Qián Kūn*, Heaven and Earth).
If one fails to grasp this, it will perish.

*Zhòng Yáng* (Master of the Double Yang) drank water and gained the True cause—
Washing away dusty toil, clarifying purity to its utmost,
Irrigating the root, extending the *jiǎ yá* (first sprouts of life).
Here, *qi* and spirit are nourished.

Serene and tranquil, sweet dew tastes the True.
Drip by drip, it opens the Three Teachings’ principles,
Stream by stream, it transmits the Four Seasons’ spring.
Flowing in pure renewal.

If one can act—
Then one knows this *yuán yuán* (primordial origin).
Why does one grasp the Three-in-One Law?
All because of insight into the Five Thousand Words.
Raising the True root’s source.

With firm steps,
Leaping into the *water-crystal basin*.
Summoning forth that which all fail to recognize,
Yet today still stir themselves to seek.
Ascending beyond the harm of the *prevalent winds*,
With reverent return—
Only then does one know *Xī Yí* (the Hidden and Obscure).

*Forging* and *cultivation* must extinguish all emotions,
*Cultivation* must strictly oppose worldly forms.
Piercing through this is the True return.
The *Moon Rabbit’s Jade* moves—
Recognize the *Golden Phoenix*’s flight.

East and West exchange positions, penetrating earth’s marrow,
Above and below harmonize, merging with Heaven’s mechanism.
Only then does one attain the subtle wonders.

The cultivator—
Discusses the Four *Shì* (affairs) in inverted order.
Earth, Water, Fire, and Wind must be transformed and let go,
Colors, sounds, scents, and tastes—how can they endure?
Only then does the True cause reveal itself.

All attainments—
Obscure and silent, with dimness and confusion.
Wisdom’s nature returns to the path of clarity,
True spirit enters and exits the Mystic Gate.
Beyond the void, the Nine Radiant Lights are complete.

The True Great *Dao*—
Its nourishment and taste cannot be exhausted.»

The moon’s light shimmers bright within its glow,
The clear wind whistles soft with *mòmò* grace.
From here, the *zhī* sprouts are revealed—
No narrow or broad, nor distant or near.
Round and whole, effortless and free,
One attains the boundless, drifting with ease.
Only then does clarity fully shine.

The oriole’s song—
At the time of its call, it circles the red.
The trees must answer as master.
With *yīngyīng* voices, bright and clear,
It plays with the sun’s tongue and feathered scales.
Hidden within the lush crimson woods,
Its speech shifts endlessly in myriad forms.

Joy in fresh lead, fresh mercury aligned,
Calling back to the ancestral root.
Awakening the drowsy, suddenly knowing
The original source—natural rule and measure.
Fixed are the divisions—*jiǎyǐ gēngxīn*,
The Nine Palaces, Eight Trigrams’ gates.
Drive the Four Symbols, push through the Seven Returns,
Use the thousand days to forge *wénwǔ*—
This *jīndān*—
In two years’ time, gradually made visible.

An infant straddles the tiger,
A fair maiden rides the dragon,
White clouds summon emerald mist.
Each wields—
Steel blades, wisdom-swords,
Clashing edges, hidden mechanisms—
No fear between the two.

The tortoise and crimson phoenix
Come to submit and surrender,
Warfare ceases, arms laid down—
The spirit-child constructs harmony.
From this point onward,
Searching slowly for treasures complete,
To see is to know their count.

Ten thousand pearls—
Spouting divine light, inverted and encompassing.
A silver mist unfurls,
Piercing the clear sky,
Dazzling the bright expanse,
Opening the jade path.
Within, alone stands
The True Marvel, the True Mystery—
Star-crowned, moon-cloaked in solemn array,
Lifting its twin eyes to gaze again and again.

Gazing clearly, pure and bright,
Deep and limpid—
The *hài* wind finds its match.

**Observing the Floating World—**
To be human is noble.
Abandon glory and wealth,
Preserve *qi* and spirit whole.

「Nurture the *dāntián*, abandon all taste.
Then bring forth—
The hare makes no concealment.
Self-aware, self-restraining,
Cultivate the means to eternal life.
Self-vowed, self-vowed—
Today, I speak in detail.

Open the boundaries to awaken wisdom,
Subdue wine, lust, wealth, and *qi* in equal measure.
Rooted and preserved,
The belt is eternally steadfast.
How to achieve the union of Tiger and Dragon,
How to command the *zāyīng* to sleep in harmony.
Cast aside all dusty labors,
Merge the Two Paths, return to the original kind.

Contemplate the *Xuán-xuán*,
Seek the *mì-mì*.
Self-moving, self-moving—
Realize nature without command.
Self-alert, self-alert—
First seize the black tempest.

Let the inverted encompass only what can be sung,
Both pulses flowing back and forth bring auspiciousness.
Distinguish the clear and the still—
The tortoise now takes warning,
Opening its gaze to radiant brilliance.

Frolic in waves, revel in tides,
Behold the radiant scene atop *Hèxī* Mountain.
The waves settle, the billows still—
Self-dwelling, self-dwelling,
Retreat to the *Kǎn* door of the *Lí* palace.
Self-enlightened, self-enlightened,
Build the lead chamber within the mercury.

Often glance, often regard each other,
The upward and downward surges harmonize—
Their paths known.
Gradually entering,
The path of clouds and mists.
The crimson phoenix flies, its feathers vibrant,
Drinking deep from the *Wū* River, beholding the Water Palace.

With the spirit as master and ancestor,
Only the *dāo* and *guī* can soothe *Cháng’ān*.
Then shall you teach—
The child to accompany noon.
Self-seated, self-seated,
True fire seen upon the wood.
Self-joyous, self-joyous—
No calamity from before.
The eastern rain is settled, trustworthy and sincere,
Moistening leaves, nourishing branches into blossoms.
Clustered, clustered—
Jade pearls.
Emerald mist ascends, locking all beneath,
White dew congeals, bearing the void above.
Exchange structures, sleep together in ease,
Only then does life know no binding.

Not by Heaven, but by Self.
Self-reclining, self-reclining,
Rest in the Western Quarter.
Self-assisting, self-assisting,
Gather true fire upon the Spirit Platform.
The *Gēng-Xīn* lessons resonate in harmony,
All things plucked—all shattered.
Originally revealed—
This one alone.
Leaping beyond, neither small nor great,
Striking after—neither rigid nor weak.
Resounding like this sound—
Echoing through the *Míngtáng*, clear and resonant.
Encountering the *línglóng*,
Together in celebration.
Self-knowing, self-knowing—
Only this is clear.
From this, henceforth—
Obtaining One, no longer Four.
Within the void, scatter golden threads,
Ten thousand rays of *xiá* light permeate the embrace.
Restore the Original,
Behold the Beginning.
To refine the true and authentic essence,
No need for Wood, Metal, Fire, or Water.
Build the foundation of good cause from the heart,
The inch-square realm—cool, without joy or sorrow.
Attest to eternal life,
And prolonged vision.

*Chóngyáng* Child,
The *hài* wind’s master.
*Wáng Zhé* by name,
*Zhīmíng* as character.
Speaking of cultivation’s intent—no deceit,
Within the *Zhuómù* words, true principles unfold.
To all gentlemen,
Take heed and commit.
*—From the Complete Works of Zhōngyáng Quánzhēn, Volume Four*
#1 This *cì* title may be incorrect.
#2 This *cì* title should be *“Chángxiāngsī”*.
#3 This *cì* title should be *“Wàng Jiāngnán”*.
*—Volume Five, Zhōngnánshān Zhōngyáng Zǐ Wáng Zhé’s Composition*
*Word: Tànchūn Lìng*
*Locking the Gate—Hua Mǎ Yǔ*

---

To grasp the true principle,
Silently ponder, subtly reflect—
Rely on cause and effect.

Now, joy and delight arise,
Devotion to the Mysterious Dao,
And the gate is sealed.

Incandescent and lucid—truly worthy,
With natural incense and fire;
In stillness, profound tranquility—
Distinctly, one sees:
The Master comes to behold me.

Exquisite wine and delicacies,
Trustingly consumed at will—
Feasts are best of all.

Sated with virtue and power,
Only singing and dancing in revelry,
[□] rejoicing in Dao’s discourse.

Frequently plucking the *língzhī* spirit-plant,
Summoning its fragrant essence.

Clouds and mists envelop the world,
Cranes and mandarin ducks lead the way—
Yet I depart for the *Pénglái* Isles.

*Moon-in-the-Heaven*:
A self-composed ode.
I ask you, Wang San,
What is your *yīnyuán* cause and fate?
The *hài* wind’s harm—
Where does it dwell in your heart?

Alone, with a serene smile,
For life and death, death and life—
Most clearly discerned.

Turn to awaken your true nature,
No longer envious of
Mortal praise and the Five *Dà* Robes.

The realm of pure coolness,
Flesh and fur are of no use—
Why recall silk and cotton?

When the body fully manifests,
This robe of green and white,
All of coarse hemp.

A *húlú* gourd stores medicine,
And in my armpit, the *jīngwén* sutras—
Saving humanity from suffering.

A bamboo staff to lean upon,
Attending to the *zìzài* boundless,
The *xiāoyáo* free and easy *zhōnglǚ* bell.

The Dao’s path homeward,
With mist and cloud as companions.

*Obstacles of the Spring Wind*—
Suddenly encountering *Ruǎn Láng* Lord,
Without warning, my eyes redden.

My vision obscured by misty veils,
How can I see the precious pupils?

The wondrous medicine,
Now cultivated and revered—
The skilled physician’s virtue shines.

A single stroke of the golden comb,
And the thread of fate is severed—
The Three *Guāng* [Sun, Moon, and Stars] are inherently pure.

---

*Ode to the Paper Robe*—
A gift to *Cài Lún* for aiding in its creation,
Revealing the paper robe on my person.

Fresh and spotless—rare in the world,
Shielding against dust and toil.

Jade-like sheen,
Luminous as jade—
The cold wind’s force grows faint.

The chill’s might retreats,
Unveiling the Dao’s essence—
White clouds drift freely.

---

*Spring’s Joyful Migration*—
A gift to a Daoist friend.

You seek the good—
This Great Dao is wordless,
How then does one return?

Abandon the superficial,
Search for the Mysterious Dao,
Casually wrapped in cultivation’s art.

Seize the original true nature,
Grasp the root’s expedient means—
Its primordial face,
How does it appear?
Must it be revealed.

Behold it directly,
Worthy of deep affection—
Please come to the *Gōngjiāo* [Palace of the Red Bird],
Where a jade feast awaits.

In the gathering’s radiance,
A thousand rays of cloud-light,
Piercing the pearly *yáo* snowflakes.

A single gem of precious clarity,
Bursting forth like lightning’s brilliance.

Ascending to the *Zhōngyāng* Central,
Returning to the *Dàluó* Great Netherworld—
Forever free from transmigration.

---

*Joy of the Return to Court*—
Where did I dwell when *Heaven* and *Earth* first divided?
What name did my parents bestow when unborn?
Must this be made clear,
And the principle explored—
No need to debate its truth.

Refining the *bù'èr* non-dual,
One essence remains, tracing back to its origin.

Frequent comings and goings,
Lost in confusion—
When shall I receive the gift of speech?

Suddenly, the true spirit appears before me.

Recognizing its original form,
I rejoice—
Incandescent and lucid,
Gazing upon its solemn essence,
Its radiant return,
Illuminating all with ease.

When seen, it is kept in secret,
In the profound subtlety of the Mysterious Dao.

Emerging from the perfect light,
The Five *Bān* hues,
Returning to their original auspiciousness.

---

*Subtracted-Character Plum Blossom*—
A farewell poem.

This mortal frame of Four *Jiǎ* [Illusions],
Though long-lived, will not escape decay.
Water burial for the fish,
Teach you—
Humanity’s *yè* [business] and bones are mere dice.

This return,
A single pearl of clarity—
Priceless.

True cultivation,
Steadying the *xiāoyáo* boundless boat,
Reaching the shore.

---

Self-composed ode:
My small name—eighteen,
Studying the *Xiào Jīng* [Classic of Filial Piety] through its chapters.

To celebrate the *Qīngcháo* [Pure Dynasty],
I dance the *Liù Wǔ* [Six Measures] before the wine.

The *Hú Lú* [Gathering] is always met,
Six dice—three lost in the game.
Foolishly, I am the first
To strike the drum in the *chóng* [clustered] crowd.

Seven years of the *hài* wind’s harm,
Awakening to the *Xīn Jīng* [Heart Sutra]—
No obstruction remains.

Trusting in the West and East,
South and North—
No division above or below.

The *Lónghuá* [Dragon Flower] Three *Huì* [Assemblies],
Silently recognizing the *xiáoyáo* [boundless] *guānzài* [observing] *Wúzàifú* [Self-So]ness.

To see true emptiness,
The *Yuánshǐ* [Original Beginning] *xūwú* [void] is my ancestor.

At the time of *Wǔjiǔ* [Five Nines],
The Dao’s use—
*Duéxiān* [Exiled Immortal]’s three cups of wine.

Gay banners and breezy elegance,
Demonstrating the *Nónggēng* [Agricultural Plough]’s *jìtǔniú* [striking the soil ox].

*Dōngjūn* [Eastern Sovereign]’s virtue is profound,
Freeing the mountain plum and riverside willow.

Cultivating the true essence,
A single pearl of clarity emerges from the Jade Tower.

Green mountains and verdant waters,
With the Daoist—
Long is the present intoxication.

Green waters and blue mountains,
Are the Daoist’s true leisure.

Bright moon and clear wind,
Seizing the boundless freedom—
Unspeakable.

Clear wind and bright moon,
Together are the Three—
I am one with them.

The heart, low or high,
Searching for the Mysterious Dao’s essence.

High or low, the heart descends—
At *yǒushàng* [10 PM], the East becomes the West.

The heart ascends, fire surges—
Lost in the *Sāntián* [Three Fields]’s *táng* [sugar] and honey.

Fire surges, the heart ascends—
The wheel of transmigration turns again.

The spirit is clear, the *qi* is refreshed,
Revelry in the tranquil—
Worthy of a single song.

The *qi* refreshed, the spirit clear—
Drumming out the voice from my origins.

Spirit clear, *qi* refreshed,
Nurturing the *huángyá* [yellow sprout]’s fate—
Aiding its growth.

*Qi* refreshed, spirit clear—
Recognizing the path ahead,
Its true essence.

---

*A Gift to Wang’s Drinking House*—
Cool broth must be prepared,
With skilled hands rolling it like snow in one’s grasp.

The broth prepared and cool,
Jade petals swirl into the precious pot.

Sliced finely with the knife,
In the bowl—silver threads and jade shavings.

Finely sliced with the knife,
Further divided—
The *bìtáo* [plum]’s green hues.

---

*Transforming Ragged Silk*—
Long dwelling by the sea,
A robe of silk is not needed for warmth.

By the sea, long dwelling,
The mortal frame’s nature is naturally temperate.

I pray for your care,
Turning many into one for praise.

Praise for your care,
Nurturing the *xiān tāi* [immortal embryo],
Granting ease and expansion.

---

*Wandering Waves*—
A poem for the *Táng Xiùcái* [Tang Scholar] seeking *Chūn* [Spring]’s chill and *Qiū* [Autumn]’s heat.

**《气色》**
Qi’s hues clash in ceaseless interplay—
Four seasons blend without distinction.
Above congeals, below emits—
Two forces grind in mutual friction.

Warmth deceives cold, cold presses warmth,
Their shifts resist all firm decree.
Like fleeting splendor, men pursue their fate—
Gaining warmth, they court the baneful chill.

Wealth and poverty, heat and cold—
All shift like waves in sand’s embrace.
Harmonious qi seeks to ascend,
Yet cold’s dark weight drags it down.
Cool clarity within may yet surge,
But outer flames suppress its flight—
Spring’s chill, autumn’s stifling steam.

Yin ascends, yang surges bright,
Yang delights, yin swells in turn.
Men boast their strength at life’s decline—
Heaven darkens just before the dawn,
Fate and fortune intertwine.

---
**《叹虚》**
*Oh, the Void’s ethereal drift!*
Stone-fire spares no fleeting spark,
Lightning wraps in flame’s fierce burn.
A hundred years—like bubbles burst
In water’s grasp. Life’s flash and fade,
Like wind-torches, burns too fast.

You dwell in vain, in worldly dust—
Awaken! Seize the hollow bloom.
With wisdom’s lamp, dispel the oil of fate.
Its radiance burns eternal, bright and clear,
Reflecting back the sacred sprouts.

Men must grasp the golden seed—
Yet cling to fleeting, gaudy bloom.
The mundane, once transcended, becomes the Dao.
All things, once touched, dissolve—
What need for infantile delight?

Penglai’s glow shines through mist and haze,
Emerald vapors, crimson clouds.
In the Ever-Spring Garden, sacred blossoms bloom.
Though veiled in dimness, light remains—
Cease your boasts, and rest in stillness.
*Mùshān’s* stream winds on.

---

**玉堂三老**
The Three Elders of Jade Hall,
Only Master Wáng Sān cāo knows.

**复许辨三台**
He can discern the Three Platforms,
And further, nourish the Three Fields with ease.

**更能润、三田倚靠**
Moistening them, leaning on their support,
**自然三耀**—the Three Radiances arise.

**攒聚气神精，运三车**
Gathering *qi*, spirit, and essence,
He drives the Three Vehicles.

**依三教，永没沈三道**
Following the Three Teachings,
He sinks forever into the Three Ways.

**须通三宝，方见三清好**
Only when he masters the Three Treasures
Does he behold the Three Pure Ones’ splendor.

**真性照三峰**
His true nature shines upon the Three Peaks,
**陡兔了、三焦做造**—
Swiftly, he dispels the Three Burners’ afflictions.

**休论三世**
Do not speak of the Three Worlds,
For all Buddhas appear before him now.

**诸佛现前来，得三乘**
He attains the Three Vehicles,
**游三昧，莹莹归三岛**
Wanders in the Three Meditations,
And returns to the Three Isles in luminous grace.

**修行学道，切莫凭婴姹**
In Dao cultivation, do not cling to youthful charm,
For these are but fleeting illusions.

**只是这些儿，把尘俗、般般不惹**
He avoids all worldly dust—
Every trifle, he shuns.

**自然萧索，寂寞与他依**
Thus, he dwells in serene desolation,
In quietude, aligned with emptiness.

**餐残饭，着粗衣**
Feasting on leftovers,
Wearing coarse robes—
**饱暖休相舍**
Yet never forsaking fullness or warmth.

**常从坦荡，守养身躯假**
He abides in boundless openness,
Nurturing his mortal form with steadfast care.

**闲裹得真闲，觉清凉**
In idle ease, he finds true leisure,
Feeling the cool, refreshing breeze—
**惺惺洒洒**
Vigorous and bright.

**暗中功行，直待两盈盈**
In hidden toil, his practice ripens,
Till both *qi* and spirit brim full.

**灵明显，做逍遥**
The spirit becomes clear and luminous,
And he achieves boundless freedom—
**师父看来也**
As the Master sees.

**水中沤起，来往相随走**
Like gold dredged from water’s depths,
He moves with the ebb and flow.

**旋旋被风吹，便生灭**
Swiftly, winds scatter him—
Life and death arise in turn.

**暂无还有**
For a moment, he lingers—
**忽亡忽聚，遄速没人知**
Then vanishes or gathers, unseen by any.

**如浮世，不坚牢**
Like this transient world,
He is not steadfast.

**名利难长久**
Gains and glory fade too soon.

**诸公早悟，休要迷花酒**
All noble ones, awaken early!
Do not be ensnared by beauty’s fleeting allure.

**养聚气和神，更认取、三光灵秀**
Nourish *qi* and spirit in harmony,
And know the Three Lights’ refined essence—
**朝昏调摄**
Balancing them at dawn and dusk,
**保护结金丹**
Guard them to forge the Golden Elixir.

**添真莹，放明光**
Augmenting true clarity,
He emits bright radiance—
**永得逍遥寿**
And attains eternal, carefree life.

---

**赠刘哥会剃头面**
*To Brother Liú, Master of Hair-Trimming*

**公能力镊**
Your skill with the tweezers is unmatched—
**将彼姿颜接**
You pluck those features with precision.

**刮削与提得**
Shaving and lifting—
**甚停当、心洽意惬**
How perfectly refined!
Your heart and mind are at ease.

**如描似画**
Like ink on silk, or strokes of brush,
**眉秀鬓须齐**
Brows are fine, temples and beard aligned—
**添嫩貌，减衰容**
You enhance youthful grace,
And diminish signs of age.

**又更增言捷**
With swift words, you further polish—
**内灵和协**
Inner harmony prevails,
**无质无腮颊**
No flaws remain on cheek or jaw.

**妙手有何述**
What could be said of such skill?
**敢把此、分明拈捻**
Yet you dare to pluck with such clarity—
**若还会得**
If you truly master it,
**慧剑便磨聋**
Your wisdom-sword grows dull from overuse,
**呈白刃，显青钢**
Revealing its steel—
**剃出圆成晔**
You trim to perfect, radiant form.

---

**燕归梁**
*Yàn Guī Liáng*
This path of cultivation is profound—
**这个修行理最深**
Like gold washed in river currents.

**水裹淘金见**
In purity, search for its truth—
**清净处细搜寻**
Only wind and moon
**唯风月，是知音**
Are true companions.

**绵绵永永，无令歇如**
Endless, unceasing—
**捞得称嘉吟**
You gather praise in verse.

**一从携去上高岑**
When you take it to the heights,
**方能显、道人心**
Only then does the Daoist’s heart reveal itself.

---

**挂金灯**
*Guà Jīn Dēng*
*To Liú Jiāng’s Hermitage*

**好池亭，华丽於中莹**
Fine pavilions by the pond,
Luxurious yet luminously clear.

**善修外景，装成内景**
You cultivate outward beauty,
And adorn inner refinement.

**这两事，谁能省**
These two arts—
Who could neglect them?

**谨按黄庭缉整，表裹通贤圣**
Following the *Huángtíng* Classic’s meticulous instructions,
You emulate the sages’ perfect form.

**水心炎炎，火焰猛劲**
The pond’s heart burns fiercely,
Its flames are vigorous.

**溉炼出、真清净**
Through refining, you reveal
**真清净**—true purity.

---

**金蕉叶**
*Jīn Jiāo Yè*

**扑入尘凡世俗，这思牢、更兼爱狱**
Plunged into the dusty, mundane world,
You cling to worldly thoughts—
**被玉杻金枷紧束**
Bound by jade chains and golden shackles,
**受无穷不足**
Enduring endless, unfulfilled longing.

**百岁光阴迅速，更朝磨、夜磨催促**
A hundred years pass swiftly—
**朝磨** at dawn, **夜磨** at night,
Time presses relentlessly.

**早离了家缘孤宿，结神仙眷属**
Detach early from worldly ties,
And bind to the Daoist’s true kin.

---

**武陵春#2**
*Wǔlíng Qīngchūn #2*
**咏骷髅**
*Ode to the Skull*

**无事闲行郊野过**
In idle strolls through countryside,
**见棺函板破**
I find a coffin, splintered open.

**裹头白白一骷髅，独潇洒愁愁**
A skull, stark and white,
Alone in carefree, melancholy grace.

**为甚因缘当路卧，往来人诽谤**
Why does it lie here, blocking the way?
Passersby mock it—
**在生昧昧了真修**
In life, they were blind to true practice,
**这回却休休**
Now they rest in vain.

---

**定风波**
*Dìng Fēng Bō*
**赠马钰**
*To Mǎ Yù*

**万万人中这个人，忽然自悟说良因**
Among ten thousand souls,
This one suddenly awakens—
**恰似白莲花一朵**
Like a single white lotus,
**尖新，泥沙脱了出迷津**
Fresh and pure,
He escapes the muddy path of illusion.

**邀住清明开嫩脸，朗窍明月作毗邻**
He dwells in clarity,
His face blooms with youthful grace—
**住向空中腾馥郁**
Afloat in the void,
**灵真，此回占得四时春**
His spirit is refined,
And he claims the eternal spring.

---

**〔浣溪沙〕**
*Huàn Xī Shā*

**空裹追声枉了贤**
Chasing echoes in emptiness—
A scholar’s futile labor.

**水中捉月事同然**
Grasping the moon from water—
**隔靴抓痒越孜煎**
Like scratching an itch through a shoe—
**劝人认取裹头人**
How fervent the pursuit!

**本来面目好相亲**
Yet the true form is ever near—
**浮世都怜假合身**
Worldlings adore the false.

**休要迷花酒**
Do not be lost in beauty’s fleeting dance.

**返照回光知去处**
When radiance returns,
You know its source—
**逍遥自在乐天真**
Boundless freedom,
Joy in heaven’s true nature.

**锐然颖脱出嚣尘**
Swiftly, you transcend the dusty world.

---

**江梅引**
*Jiāng Méi Yǐn*

**宁海范明叔邀饭览月桂花**
Brother Fàn Míngshū of Nínghǎi invites me to a meal,
Beneath the moonlit *guìhuā* tree.

**凌晨静至乐倍**
At dawn’s approach, the stillness doubles my delight,
**倚栏隈，观奇材**
Leaning on the railing,
I behold its marvelous form.

**正是蟾宫余影世间来**
The moon’s last light descends—
**遂得睛空甘露力**
I gain the void’s nectar,
**润根荄，发修条，伟又瑰**
Moistening its roots,
Unfurling its branches—
How grand and rare!

**能绽粉苞加红艳**
It bursts with pink petals,
**按周天，四序开**
Following the cosmic cycle,
Blooming through all seasons—
**蕊撒黄金，腾馥郁、道眼堪猜**
Its stamens scatter gold,
Its fragrance ascends—
A sight for Daoist eyes alone.

**岂许姿陆地、混尘埃**
Who would allow such grace
To be buried in earthly dust?
**呼取好风同引去**
I summon the finest breeze,
**上瑶台，复灵根，月裹栽**
To lift it to the Celestial Terrace,
Where its spirit thrives—
Planted in moonlight.

「When one recognizes the wondrous Dao of the rare and distant *Xīyí* realm,
It is naturally—
A state of **no vexation, no sorrow**.

Wife, son, grandson, granddaughter,
All entangled in endless affection.

Yet bound by *yù* (prison) and *yīn* (mountain of debt),
I clutch my body tightly—
Seized and held fast.

If one seeks to refine oneself into such **playful perfection**,
One must **wield the wisdom-blade**—
Sharpen it often,
And strike it repeatedly.

Even a **ten-thousand-catín iron chain** will shatter.

I pay tribute to Master Liú,
And awaken to my own **golden rooster’s call**.

**Grateful for the Sovereign’s Grace**—
In the tenth month of *Dīnghài* (1747), the Master wished to transform *Mǎ Yuè* (Horse Moon),
So for a hundred days he sealed the gate,
Desiring that *Yuè* witness the family’s **Daoist discipline** and thus comply.

A hundred days the gate of the *ān* (hermitage) was sealed,
*Mǎ Yuè* was taken and bound—
In the tranquil stillness,
Both true and false *qi* were cultivated.

I alone sigh and ponder,
**How such ease could be attained.**

My kin know well,
**How pure and refined** it is.

There is another kind—
**Distinct and clear like fine art**,
Again and again I lift it forth,
Temporarily to hang.

To behold it fully,
One must pay a **price of ten-thousand *hú* (斛) of pearls**.

At that time, I would pass it down—
A few words.

**The *Ruì* (auspicious) *Zhì* (crane)**—
In *Chángchūn* (Eternal Spring), the scenery lasts forever,
In the **land of eternal night**,
It never sleeps.

**At ease and unhurried**, except for my own thoughts,
**Roaming freely**, who could restrain it?

Only knowing **beyond the world is the world itself**,
**Gazing within the heavens reveals another heaven**.

**Five-colored clouds** forever as its companion,
**Golden flowers** encircle the *Dàluótiān* (Great Lotus Heaven).

**Do not refine the outward form**—
Only **kindle the crimson heart within**.

From this point, one may **generate fire from wood**,
Naturally **nurturing gold from water**.

**The *Yáo* (jewel) *Fāng* (fragrance) tree** and its kindred guard,
**Jade leaves and gem branches** intertwine.

**Do not seek companions elsewhere**,
For **this alone is the true resonant voice**.

Which **Daoist cultivation** is refining the **gold elixir**?
Only when refined does one **know the two affairs are complete**.

**Seven returns** must not open the **four gates**,
**Nine rounds** should turn the **three fields**.

**Qi and spirit** intertwined form the treasure,
**Luminous nature** clearly reveals the **Great Sage**.

Today, it returns to its **origin’s path**,
Naturally **pure and tranquil** forevermore.

**Lamenting the Yellow Flower**—
Yesterday, drunk with wine,
I was bound at the elbow.

On the bridge,
I fell into a **sudden downpour**—
**Mocking laughter**.

No one to help me,
Wife and children **none would save**.

I awaken suddenly—
**My kin have cursed themselves.**

**The Unattached Youth**
The willow droops in vain for me,
The blossoms bloom for none but her.
My wife—oh, my wife—
A painted dog of false pretence.
I guard the dike with care,
Lest it breach and spill my breath.
That wretch, Wang San,
Should never walk this path again.

When the bean leaves turn yellow,
I’ll repay the worthy and brave—
Let them leave this world soon.

The **Lingjing** landscape is pure,
Cool and serene, a perfect dwelling.
It opens the **Gate of Eternal Life**.
Then take up practice with true **virtue/power** and true **Daoist cultivation**,
And the **Luminous Nature** will shine forth.

The maiden rides the dragon,
The babe straddles the tiger.
They trade **pearls and jade**,
Tossing them aside for fleeting gain.
Yet here is the realm of **free and easy ease**—
A single **gold elixir** (*mingming jindan*), radiant as gold mirror and gold glow, gathered tight.

The **Sacred Gourd**—
This gourd holds **spirit/qi** divine.
Awake and clear, **incandescent and lucid**,
I grasp the **free and easy ease** true.
With **head and mouth** wrapped in its grace,
I chant the **Daoist scriptures** without cease.

I take the **good karmic causes**,
And fill my belly with them.
Pure and clear, they turn to **purity’s flow**.
With **jade staff** in hand, where shall I go?
I follow my **Master**—
**Clouds and waters** mark my path.

**The Foolish Guolang**
Someone asks: *"How can one escape the heart of hatred and love?"*
The deeper the hatred, the more it grows,
The more one loves, the greater the folly.
Both weigh on the mind—
How does one resolve them?
When others rejoice, I take it as my own delight,
When others suffer, I feel it as my own affliction.
The heart becomes a single mass—
Each erodes the other.

Guolang’s **sloth** (*màn*)
Dissolves the silver mist,
Sweet rain forming pearls of dew.
He summons the **Clear Wind**,
**Qi and spirit** aiding him.
Then he **invites the Order**—
To guard and follow close,
To treasure the **Three Fields** (*sān tián*),
And gather the **Nine-turn elixir** (*jiǔ zhuàn língdān*).

Before the **Azure Void**,
Jade mushrooms and golden trees sprout in abundance.
The **Lingming Flowers** (*yáohuā*) bloom,
Filling the sky with countless fragrance.
The **Luminous Blossoms** (*qióng yì*) unfold,
Their jade petals exhaling sweet perfume—
Right in the midst of this scent,
A single point of light resides.

**Free and easy ease**—
Serene and unrestrained, he walks.
With **spirit staff** in hand,
His wide sleeves sway at leisure.
The **colored clouds** swirl around,
And distant fragrant breezes,
With emerald mists, coax him near.
He lifts his head—
And suddenly beholds a **radiant vision**, ever more refined.
Sees the **Green Robes** half in the air,
Waving him forward.
He calls to me: *"Do not part—follow me!"*
And points to the **white clouds’ depths**,
Where **Daoist immortals** dwell.

**The Deep Gratitude**
My **Master** once said:
I once carried a **gourd of wine** from the **Sweet River**,
Heading back to my **hermitage**,
When I met a **Master** who asked:
*"Would you share your wine with one struck by the wind?"*
I gave it to him.
The **Master** drank it all,
Then ordered me to fill the gourd with river water.
I did so and gave it back.
He returned it to me,
Saying I should drink.
I drank—and it was **nectar of the Dao**.

How much wind-water was drunk?
From this, the **mysteries of the Dao** were revealed.
A **white linen robe** and **blue silk headband**,
Fitting him perfectly—truly **spirited**!
No need for a mirror to behold his face,
For all things are clear in his mind.

In dreams, he sees the **true self** beyond dreams,
And thus is he **free and easy**, crossing to the **other shore**.

---

**Again—The Master’s Practice**
He stokes the furnace,
Burning out the **cool and serene vision**,
Seizing the **gale’s shadow**.
Lightly, he fills it with **free and easy ease**—
The **heart-moon** shines clear beyond the void.

From the start, he **vows with clarity**,
Heeding the **Celestial Decree**.
A **Daoist chant** calls him—
Now he may return to the **elixir’s celestial heights**.

**Free and Easy Ease #3**
If one would **Daoist cultivation** seek,
One must **search with utmost care**.
Lock tight the **Golden Pass** and **Jade Gate**,
Let **upper** and **lower** merge in harmony,
Their **positions** exchanged, **irrigating** and **nourishing**.
Then comes the **afterbirth**—
Awake and **lucid**, yet still they **guess and debate**.

They enter the **Azure Void**,
And cast aside the **root and stalk**.
**Radiance** gleams in the **silver mist’s realm**,
Fresh as **jade’s hue**,
The **true spirit** luminous and smooth.
Clear and pure, they **pierce the void**—
Fine as the **filaments of silk**.

They cast off the **muddy wine**,
And drink the **transmitted clear water**.
This **taste**—
**Fragrant, sweet, and truly divine**.

---

**Over the Towered Hall**
No trace of dross remains—
The **Five Gates** open, **irrigating** with **sharp clarity**.
The **Seven Treasures** flourish, the **Three Fields** nourished.
With **tenfold mastery**, **knife and pill** blend in secret.
A **true crystal** forms—**radiant and resplendent**.
On **mountain peaks**, **wind and moon** invite transcendence.

**Temporary Respite by the River**
Each day’s practice is but fleeting—
Today, **sudden ease** unfolds.
**Yin and Yang** merge in **harmonious clusters**.
Like **baby to maiden**, **tiger coiled with dragon entwined**,
The **Four Symbols** copulate, **spinning jade threads**,
Piercing through the **Golden Elixir** in one stroke.
**Natural brilliance** emerges from the **muddy sphere**.
Words fail to capture—
Silence speaks no fault.

---
**The Old Gourd Master’s Song**
*(A gourd he carried, ever filled with wine)*
Through streets he wandered, day by day,
Who knew this gourd’s **true worth**?
**Fine wine** needs no purchase—
Drunk daily, never empty.
**Body’s work** now fully done,
**Spirit** stays—**never parting**.
With staff in hand, he sails the **rivers and lakes**,
A **boat of wind and moon**, **eternal clouds unfurled**.

**Tying the Cloud-Waist #4**
*(Self-Composed)*
At **Zhongnan’s peak**, **Zhongyang** stands—
**True freedom**, most **free and easy**.
With **clear wind and bright moon** as constant companions,
**Echoing spirits** call—
Beyond the void, **refined**, **rich in resonance**.
The **Penglai path** is often trod,
Only to **visit ancient sages**—**Qing and Hao**.
**Crimson clouds and emerald mists** gather thick,
Riding the **light breeze**, **cloud-waist tied high**,
Ascending to the **Azure Heights**.

**The Guest of Immortals**
To **cultivate** is to **search**—
For **true clarity**, **true stillness**, **true heart’s gain**.
This side **verdant**, that **snow-white**,
A **blackened crown**, **crimson above**.
Together they dwell in **lapislazuli halls**,
**Jade-petal flowers** folded in **celestial bloom**.
**Jade Boys sing**, **Golden Boys clap**—
**Heaven’s chosen**, **mountains their home**.
This **breakthrough**—
First the **breakthrough**, then the **Guest of Immortals** revealed.
To **see through** is to **know through**—
Look again, and **my belly splits open**.
How to **do**? Just **as it is**—
Why **nap at noon** like a fool?
What’s said? What’s done?
**Hidden in self**, **alone in practice**.
This **harmful wind**—
**Heart already broken**, **no ordinary discipline**.
No **calamity**, no **misfortune**—
**Seeking nothing**, **no ink-stained scholar’s toil**.
**Great Immortals chant**, **True Ones respond**,
In the **Full Perfection Hall**, **no smoke nor flame**.
**Worry-Free Child**, with **three companions**,
**Sudden coolness**—**free, at ease, seated**.

---
**The Complete Works of Zhongyang, Volume Five Ends**
#1 This tune should be *"Midmonth Moon Osmanthus."*
#2 Original tune mistakenly labeled *"Zhu Yingtai."*
#3 This tune should be *"Pining for the Lovely."*
#4 This tune should be *"Tying the Skirt-Waist."*

**Volume Six of the Complete Works of Zhongyang**
Composed by **Master Wang Zhe of Zhongnan Mountain**

**Volume Six of the Complete Works of Zhongyang**

**On the Tune *Satisfying the Heart’s Desire* (满庭芳)**
□ *What’s the inquiry on the Dao/Way?*
□ *Alone in practice, dwelling in stillness,*
□ *Gold, wood, water, earth—all in perfect balance.*

□ *Flame arises in the core,*
□ *Five matters* [1] *all unfold with skill.*
**Granted to the Immortals, the *qi* fully refreshed—**
□ *All is pure, all is absolute,*
□ *Beyond the lofty peaks of Songshan.*

□ *The source is true,*
□ *The transmission of its marvelous use.*
□ *Two elixirs* [2] *taste divine.*
□ *The broth is brewed, often refined,*
□ *The *Dao/Way*’s path of jade revealed,*
□ *Manifesting auspicious brilliance.*

□ *The Golden Elixir shines in truth,*
□ *Its luminous hues radiant and bright.*
□ *Soaring, vast, and boundless,*
□ *In carefree wandering,*
□ *Its tones resound like crystal.*

□ *At dawn’s first light,*
□ *The True Ones* [3] *are joyful,*
□ *Emerging from the tune *Satisfying the Heart’s Desire*.*

**Again—Discussing the Dao/Way with Master Wang Zhe of Zhongnan Mountain**
□ *On the Dao/Way’s inquiry,*
□ *The elder calls me to attend,*
□ *The True Ones* [3] *must open wide.*

□ *The profound mysteries are laid bare,*
□ *In the subtle, all is clearly explained.*
□ *The silent virtue* [4] *is everlasting,*
□ *Pure and profound,*
□ *Worthily practiced.*

□ *Within the core, the treasure gleams,*
□ *Its blossoms fragrant and dense,*
□ *Like silver frost above and below.*
□ *Gazing ahead,*
□ *I see the golden light.*
□ *Who understands white and black,*
□ *Green, red, and yellow combined?*

□ *All pulses flow through the Nine Transformations,*
□ *The refining and transporting* [5] *are done,*
□ *Piercing through Kunlun’s peaks.*
□ *Looking forward,*
□ *The jade dew* [6] *before me,*
□ *Fits this tune *Satisfying the Heart’s Desire*.*

**Again—Addressing Master Sin Jifu of Jingzhao While Watching Him Play Chess**
□ *Playing chess on the board,*
□ *My mind turns ten thousand times,*
□ *My emotions focused, complete in stillness.*
□ *The spirit seeks and reflects,*
□ *Each move cleverly deceives.*
□ *The Dao/Way spreads its intricate schemes,*
□ *Like a contest where both sides vie,*
□ *Each holds their own hidden stratagem.*

□ *Retaining the move,*
□ *The True Ones* [3] *make their play,*
□ *Silently breaking through dull confusion.*
□ *The face—how fair!*
□ *The posture, how refined!*
□ *Before me, the rhythmic strikes,*
□ *In this calm, the sounds resound.*

□ *From the *Geng* Tiger year,*
□ *Roaring winds in high mountains.*
□ *The Dao/Way is clear yet unrecognized,*
□ *White and black—*
□ *One knows how to guard and respond.*

□ *Ahead, the victory,*
□ *The golden osmanthus* [7] *in the hall,*
□ *Who will ascend with me?*

**Again—Words for Master Shao and Master Yang on Family Matters**
□ *Discussing hunger and cold,*
□ *The elders come to ask,*
□ *How can I endure father and mother?*
□ *Dragging sons, tripping daughters,*
□ *Wives and children vex my heart.*

□ *The hexagram’s meaning is clear,*
□ *The *Field of Earth* [8] *is pure,*
□ *Shocking the land with coolness.*
□ *Looking south,*
□ *A single point before me—*
□ *Why not act now and explain?*

□ *The tones resound,*
□ *The sequence arrives,*
□ *Wood, fire, water, metal—*
□ *Each releases its radiant light.*
□ *Thus the true scene is revealed,*
□ *Naturally expansive.*

□ *Witnessing the crimson clouds rise and fall,*
□ *After opening, the wisdom’s blade swings steel.*
□ *The blossoms unfold,*
□ *The *Dao/Way*’s threads weave and draw,*
□ *Forever fitting this tune *Satisfying the Heart’s Desire*.*

**Again—Gift to Mother Xi Yang**
□ *Speaking of emptiness and nothingness,*
□ *From the core, the lotus emerges,*
□ *The True Ones* [3] *encounter Xi Yang.*

□ *Her virtue surpasses mine,*
□ *In all matters, she shines bright.*
□ *Soaring, vast, and boundless,*
□ *The wind moves,*
□ *In harmony with the Dao/Way.*

□ *The treasure is hidden,*
□ *The blossoms open—*
□ *In the void, the true fragrance is scattered.*
□ *Beside her,*
□ *The silver waves* [9] *flow,*
□ *Meeting the mist and flames,*
□ *Summer’s heat turned to frost.*

□ *Green sprouts, golden leaves,*
□ *Each cool and refreshing.*
□ *Standing on the southern ridge of Jingzhao,*
□ *Her name—*
□ *Beyond the heavens, it spreads wide.*
□ *In life, I remember,*
□ *In my heart, the words and tunes,*
□ *Must be sung to *Satisfying the Heart’s Desire*.*

**Again—Parting Words for Jingzhao**
□ *Urging Master Han,*
□ *To return eastward,*
□ *The True Ones* [3] *must refine with care.*
□ *Teaching me,*
□ *I must compose words and verses.*

□ *The land’s compassion is vast,*
□ *The wheel displays*
□ *Its round, luminous light.*
□ *Who can attain*
□ *A mind without obstruction,*
□ *Good fortune naturally unfolds?*

□ *Long-lasting,*
□ *The virtue is truly benevolent,*
□ *A single point of the heart,*
□ *Ever making the bells chime.*
□ *Their resonant sounds,*
□ *Echoing clear and bright,*
□ *The tones resound like crystal.*

□ *Friends and old companions,*
□ *Dancing sleeves arrive to converse,*
□ *Within the core,*
□ *They know only my boundless mercy.*
□ *The master,*
□ *The wind does as it pleases,*
□ *In the hall, it cannot stay,*
□ *Heavy footsteps depart.*

□ *Already cool and clear,*
□ *The round light returns,*
□ *Emerging from the garden’s embrace.*
□ *Auspicious blessings, joyful celebrations,*
□ *Now where do they lodge?*
□ *The truth is revealed,*
□ *Not distant nor faint—*
□ *Gazing at the *Chao Yuan Guan* [10].*

**Again—Master Yu of Huang County Seeks Instruction on the Dao/Way**
□ *On the inquiry of the Dao/Way,*
□ *The elder is most pleased,*
□ *The *qi*’s crossing* [11] *worthy of jade broth.*

□ *The fire is pure, the heat reversed,*
□ *All is auspicious, all prospers.*
□ *The golden crow is bright,*
□ *Within the core,*
□ *The jade hare is refined.*

□ *□□□,*
□ *□□□, the proper place,*
□ *Summer’s heat turned to frost.*

□ *Now it is clear,*
□ *Within the core, the treasure gleams,*
□ *Pearls and jade,*
□ *Each stored away.*
□ *How excellent, how virtuous!*
□ *The nature’s flame shines bright.*

□ *The luminous clarity grows ever more radiant,*
□ *Within the land,*
□ *Its straight light is ever present.*
□ *The hidden point,*
□ *The mist disperses—*
□ *Worthy of celebration in *Satisfying the Heart’s Desire*.*

**Tune *Sudden Mountain Stream* (蓦山溪)**
□ *The monkeys gather in clusters,*
□ *This is the pattern of True Practice.*
□ *Each attains their own gate,*
□ *Long in leisure,*
□ *Then returns to the path of Yang.*

□ *The years pass like scenes,*
□ *Awakening brings this coolness,*
□ *The signs are clear,*
□ *The hall’s Immortals,*
□ *Below, the poor recall.*

□ *I was favored with your teachings,*
□ *Each day I search with care.*
□ *The intent rises,*
□ *Hearing the sounds,*
□ *How can I block them out?*

□ *Before me, the misty affairs,*
□ *A different family’s wind,*
□ *The corpse is gone,*
□ *The pine’s harmony,*
□ *Dare I call this mountain stream sudden?*

**Tune *Joy in the Relocation of the Swift Orchid* (喜迁莺)**
□ *The gate opens with enlightenment.*
□ *This parting is hard,*
□ *My eyes turn back in farewell.*

□ *I gain the cloud-chariot,*
□ *Content and steady in its driving,*
□ *Beyond the gusts, the music’s joy is seen.*
□ *Old friends and companions,*
□ *Dancing sleeves arrive to converse.*
□ *Within the core,*
□ *They know only my boundless mercy,*
□ *The master of compassion.*

□ *The master,*
□ *The wind does as it pleases,*
□ *In the hall, it cannot stay,*
□ *Heavy footsteps depart.*

□ *Already cool and clear,*
□ *The round light returns,*
□ *Emerging from the garden’s embrace.*
□ *Auspicious blessings, joyful celebrations,*
□ *Now where do they lodge?*
□ *The truth is revealed,*
□ *Not distant nor faint—*
□ *Gazing at the *Chao Yuan Guan* [10].*

**Tune *Golden Pheasant in the Marsh* (瑞鹧鸪)**
□ *The yellow wheat flourishes,*
□ *Changing with the autumn.*
□ *Within the core,*
□ *The body burns day by day,*
□ *In constant worry.*

□ *The sons and grandsons are long-lived,*
□ *The daughters and wives add to my cares.*
□ *Within the core,*
□ *The sorrow is deep,*
□ *The toil never ceases.*
□ *Abandoning the golden flower* [12] *as if awakened,*
□ *I now urge you to turn back soon.*

**Tune *Beside the River, the Golden Phoenix* (临江仙)**
□ *This earnest plea seeks one method,*
□ *The transmission of pure stillness,*
□ *Its wonders rare and grand.*

---
---
[1] *五事* (wu shi): Five matters (in Daoist alchemy, typically referring to the Five Agents—wood, fire, earth, metal, water).
[2] *两液* (liang ye): Two elixirs (often the *Upper Elixir* and *Lower Elixir* in Daoist internal alchemy).
[3] *真人* (zhen ren): True Ones (a title for advanced Daoist practitioners).
[4] *默* (mo): Silent (here referring to silent cultivation or the silent virtue).
[5] *搬运* (ban yun): Refining and transporting (a Daoist alchemical process).
[6] *琼路* (qiong lu): Jade path (metaphor for the refined Dao/Way or elixir).
[7] *仙桂* (xian gui): Immortal osmanthus (auspicious symbol of Daoist immortality).
[8] *田* (tian): Field of Earth (hexagram reference, often linked to stability and nourishment).
[9] *银浪* (yin lang): Silver waves (likely referring to the moon’s reflection or refined *qi*).
[10] *朝元观* (chao yuan guan): Hall of Reverence to the Primordial (a Daoist temple or sacred space).
[11] *津* (jin): Crossing (here, the convergence or refinement of *qi*).
[12] *金花* (jin hua): Golden flower (a term in Daoist meditation, often symbolizing enlightenment or the refined essence).

「Surprising the gods and startling the spirits, self-destruction comes to pass.
□ The Master enters the *Yào* mirror, □ opening the Daoist eyes.
□ Outer demons and mischief are all exterminated, □ able to cure illnesses and ward off calamities.
□ The red water and green thunder with one voice—
□ within the *Tian* field, the precious seal arrives at *Pénglái*.
□ Again, issuing a solemn oath—
