□ in the outer courtyard, the jade scroll is displayed,
□ robes lined up in orderly ranks.
□ The *Gui* has already been permitted to present new scriptures.
□ The words are the same, □ but the *Zhēn* scrolls are burned.
□ When the flames rise, clouds and rain appear,
□ the spirits convey without confusion.
□ The system connects to the Celestial Lord.
□ The transmission returns—□ the Daoist Saint knows and hears.
□ Again, the white tablet records the golden *jué* and *luò*.
□ Other names and surnames of lost souls.
□ The spirits are startled, each pondering their own fate,
□ receiving posthumous commendation, □ you love the Gate of Life.
□ The household doors are opened to reveal the mysteries of the Dao,
□ all people unite in harmony with the Celestial Venerable.
□ A single light endures without darkness,
□ its radiance like the moon, □ water flowing from *Kūnlún*.
□ *Dìngfēngbō* #1
□ Wrapped in leisure, the idle wander outside,
□ only then to roam among the white clouds.
□ Shooting the sun, they gaze upon the radiant scenery,
□ □, □ before the *Kūnshān* peaks are clearly seen.
□ They attain joyful ease, all matters neglected,
□ within the *Gui*’s treasure, ascending to the heights.
□ Wrapped in the golden flower’s fragrant bloom,
□ its scent permeates beyond the Jade Gate Pass.
□ *Rú Mèng Lìng* – Gift to Monk Zǐzhé
□ The mouth recites the sacred leaves of the ancestors,
□ the *dé* of tea is kindled with fragrant embers.
□ Extinction and smoke vanish,
□ like the *Gui*’s secret teachings.
□ Truly, □ truly—
□ the words benefit the Celestial Sage, Zǐzhé.

□ *Yǒngyùlè* – Two Poems for the Retired Official of Dēngzhōu
□ The *Zhuàng* (ornament) transforms, □ the homeland takes the auspicious,
□ the nature is clear and bright.
□ The heart is filled,
□ the governance is upright and refined,
□ the administration is particularly clear and refreshing.
□ The five horses are ordinary, □ yet they assist in governance,
□ their nature feels gratitude and ease.
□ The body resides in tranquil retirement,
□ searching for Daoist treasures.
□ Because of this, they seek the radiant,
□ the light shines forth,
□ the elixir is wrapped in truth.
□ How much more so—
□ the household is long-lasting,
□ the Gate is burned frequently,
□ the irrigation is ample, worthy of reliance.
□ Life must be preserved;
□ the sons and grandsons gather, □ their appearance and bearing are refined.
□ In due time,
□ the aspects and perspectives are clear—
□ awaiting the post of prime minister.
□ You come to observe,
□ the people are joyful and delighted,
□ the words are composed with a brush.
□ Friends are resounding, □ companions are close,
□ each gazing afar.
□ The void is revealed,
□ the Jade Tower’s scenery,
□ the omens of the mysteries are the same.
□ The Gate opens—
□ winds and moons are clear and bright,
□ the four seasons endure eternal spring.
□ It is fitting to indulge in wine,
□ at the hour of the *Mǎo*,
□ to drink until intoxication, then awaken with enlightenment.
□ The leisurely heart is content,
□ emotions are diminished,
□ joy comes from singing and reciting.
□ Truly, they offer prayers,
□ extending the life of *Péngzǔ*,
□ assisting the Primordial *Yuán* in its firmness.
□ Now there are—
□ the true *Lè* spirits, Daoist immortals,
□ arriving here to meet eternal joy.

□ Again, *Zōu Gōng* seeks
□ the steel essence,
□ the flower exhales auspiciousness,
□ the medicine’s fragrance glows,
□ refining the clear spring,
□ quenching the red flames,
□ all wealth is spent and exhausted.
□ A single *Gui* grain,
□ its essence like wheat and rice,
□ transforms into a common form, all traces gone.
□ On the mountain peak,
□ they wander and play in all four seasons,
□ often pouring the spring wine.
□ Together with the *Mǎo* hour,
□ the realm becomes serene and tranquil,
□ they see the infant become the *Chī* (beautiful).
□ They rejoice in harmony,
□ transmit the *Jīn* (elixir),
□ the night’s radiance is flawless.
□ Fortunate in years,
□ they share the morning dew,
□ refining it into a spirit elixir.
□ Long life and eternal vision at *Péngdǎo*,
□ they meet and encounter eternal bliss.

□ Again, *Guō Fǎshī* seeks
□ the green smoke and red,
□ the threads unbroken,
□ the axe cleaves the sacred.
□ The method first depends on this.
□ Not without control,
□ the Daoist resolve is firmly established in the heart.
□ Practicing the true *luò*,
□ the names and surnames of the land,
□ death is taught and its fate determined.
□ The wealth is presented—
□ gold and treasures at the body,
□ none of which need to be received.
□ The Master’s essence is luminous,
□ the flower opens to reveal the profound,
□ the armor is pure and refined through cultivation.
□ The celestial seal descends,
□ arriving with purpose,
□ the sword is sharp within the *Xīng* (heart-mind).
□ At the hour of the *Chén* and *Yuè*,
□ the head is adorned with the *Dài*,
□ the transformations shift toward the Immortal Path.
□ In their wanderings—
□ natural joy and delight,
□ they meet and encounter eternal bliss.

□ *Bǔ Suànzǐ* – Obtaining the *Huángtíng Jīng*
□ The Master knows the luminous essence,
□ roaming within the market stalls.
□ The mind is like a monkey, unwilling to settle,
□ discussing glory and fate.
□ The teeth retain their true nature,
□ the body dwells in stillness and clarity.
□ Seeking the boundless void,
□ they tread upon the *Pénglái* landscape.
□ *Bǔ Suànzǐ* – Before and after, each accompanied by the *Shèmǎ* (sound)
□ The words of divination are spoken,
□ the sweet *Jīn* (elixir) is sprinkled above.
□ Nurturing the soul’s smoke and fire, cultivating the lotus,
□ the wandering thoughts,
□ the *Shèmǎ* and *Yúmǎ* (both distractions) are all abandoned.
□ The inner elixir is priceless,
□ hanging at the mountain’s edge.
□ There are the *Tún* and *Méng* (obstacles) sewn with jade threads,
□ the wild thoughts,
□ the moon’s descent brings peace below.

□ *Sū Mùzhē* – For the *Fǎshī* (Master)
□ The pit is at rest, □ the appearance is revealed.
□ The pulse is like that of an infant,
□ fed and nourished to satiety.
□ The true *Yuán* (Primordial Essence) is steadfast and refined.
□ Like the clear wind, the bright moon in the profound mysteries.
□ As the *lù* (roe deer), □ like the *bào* (leopard).
□ The *Sháo* (ladle) returns to its appointed time,
□ who can comprehend its profound teachings?
□ The peach blossom’s fragrance drifts faintly.
□ Within the *Gui*, the pearls are fully obtained,
□ illuminated by the three luminaries.
□ Again, *Jiāo Gū* seeks
□ to listen and hear,
□ to reveal the mysteries of the Gate.»

---

The insects perish, the furnace and stove stand firm and secure.
□ The essence is ever pure beyond the void’s gaze.
□ Piercing clarity, serene and thought-free.
□ Often forgotten, □ pressed down.
□ The Golden Elixir is forged, penetrating the Hall of Light.
□ The axe’s length sharpens the steel’s edge.
□ Offering the Primordial Essence, rushing toward the Penglai Path.

Again, two verses—Master Li seeks:
□ Human discourse, □ flames aiding.
□ Like springs and sources, intertwined and steadfast.
□ The Wooden Essence locked tight.
□ Palm upheld, vital qi ever firm.
□ Sweet within, □ pure above.
□ Like a babe, the maiden often gazes.
□ Beyond the void’s edge, true elegance resides.
□ Entering auspicious clouds, one becomes an immortal.
□ Jade-green still, □ yellow candles glow.
□ Smoke vanishes, white, black, and red lights radiant.
□ The Soul’s Elixir turns for bathing.
□ [囗] eternal life, five colors clustered before.
□ The lineage’s evaluation, talismanic rites.
□ Writing the Golden Scripture, saving from calamity, returning blessings.
□ The merit of devotion is complete.
□ The Golden Elixir manifests, jade from Kunlun emerges.

*Wu Ling Chun*—Remembering the Dao Companion:
□ The clouds of the world’s edge hold another scene,
□ The *Wu Ling* spring’s curve.
□ Days of leisure, no toil,
□ Years of attaining the True One.
□ Neither people nor things are heeded,
□ Who would deign to be close?
□ Brother Shi’s words bring fresh insight,
□ The axe cuts through the River of Delusion.
□ Days of nectar pour endlessly,
□ The *Bing* returns in kinship.
□ With ambrosial wine and jade dew, the spirit is nourished.
The earth awakens at the Hour of the Tiger, nine presses in three circuits at the Golden Child—
the flavor is savored, the *Wu Ling* spring is relished.

Again—Master Zhao of Jingzhao urges drinking, yet I refuse:
□ In the groves and springs, another wine exists,
□ The *Mao* hour’s verses.
□ On the second tier, drinking jade nectar,
□ Wrapped in flames, light is born.
□ Drunkenness and sobriety blur,
□ The night is most worth savoring.
□ The taste returns, turning ever prosperous,
□ Emerging toward the Penglai estate.

*Zi Xiaoyao*—At Ease:
□ Qi complete, the spirit sits like a swallow.
□ Gathered from the four quarters, lessons taught.
□ Speaking of the Soul’s Root, □ the Kun opposes.
□ *Hu xiang mo, mo miao*—self and none beyond mortal ken.
□ Spearheads clash, □ level ground for celebration.
□ The treasure within, forged into one pearl.
□ Awakened minds, □ clarity untainted.
The dew is borne—this vessel, that tube must be used.

Again—Conveying to Master Du of Jingzhao:
□ Recognizing the piled heights,
□ The body frail and weary.
□ How to resolve, how to distance the self?
□ The Essence steadfast, □ nurturing the breath.
The marrow of grain, the dice roll—joy follows its course.
□ Chanting scriptures, □ abandoning fame and gain.
□ The *Gui* method—pause from arranging.
□ The Golden Lock sealed, □ the nest tightly shut,
The key to wash—must discern the subtle and noble in division.

*Yu Jia Yao*—In Praise of Master [Iron] □, Who Carries This When Traveling:
□ Dwelling on the Pure Platform’s quiet observance,
□ The Master’s four limbs must be kept warm.
□ Daily, teach to carry □.
□ Near the kiln, □ mixing rice and flour with jade nectar.
□ The stove as furnace, often smelting and refining,
□ Lead and mercury boiled, long □.
□ Hunger stirs—white vapors fill.
□ Within it glows, □ before, a single true gem is admired.

Again—To Master Du of Jingzhao:
□ From Shaanxi’s high renown, your surname Du,
□ The Golden Interval has long been your domain.
□ At seventy-five, your years are blessed.
□ Able to dwell, □ surpassing mortal concerns.
□ Purity returns to clarity, again donning,
□ Often recognizing the number of plum blossoms.
□ Your conduct knows the hidden halls.
□ The immortal ledger, □ merit enters the Penglai Path.

Again, two verses—Master Li seeks:
□ The Sage Laozi, originally surnamed Li,
□ Today his legacy stirs anew.
□ Seeking liberation beyond the world.
□ The enlightened station, □ from the dark *Kan*’s cool depths.
□ Then practicing benevolence and wealth in righteousness,
□ Still recounting leisure’s subtle intent.
□ Within, no heart—true activity.
□ The allotted share, □ water and fire must harmonize.
□ With virtue cultivated, seventy years true,
□ From crane-feathers to childlike visage.
□ Above, the spirit spring flows swift.
□ Like the *Mi* method, □ the corpse dissolves, the intestines fill.
□ The Dao penetrates the void as entering a chamber,
□ Commanding lead and mercury into elixir grains.
□ Then drifting free, a million quiet stillnesses.
□ No need to visit, □ often gathers with immortals.

*He Chuan Ling*—To Master Zhao of Jingzhao:
□ Heart aligned, eyes closed, ears keen and intent still,
Tongue articulate, nose attuned.
□ Speaking of mountain peaks, a clear stream descends the ravine.
□ Within it simmers, □ brother of flames, neither hasty nor slow.
□ The Western Gold dissolves the Eastern Diagram,
□ A single piece—then the Tiger and Dragon await.
□ Obtaining the pearl of light, no trade in all its forms.
□ Spring arrives, □ gold is born, flowers bloom anew.

Again—To Master [Name] of Jingzhao, with *Shi* rhyme:
□ The robe is worn thin, yet in the world’s affairs, it suits well,
Knowing white, guarding black.
□ The courtyard detached, cherish the pearl of light.
□ In years past, □ because of green, how was it accumulated?
□ The heart’s resolve is its own rule,
□ A single *Gui* grain—careful thought finds no difficulty.
□ True nature recognized, then the immortal’s essence is attained.
□ O noble one, □ devoted above,
All rhymes press under *Shi*.

*Ta Sha Xing*—Reflecting on the Dao’s Cultivation:
□ The Dao refined, □ men sigh,
□ Within it, words speak of endless continuity.
□ The knife sharpens wisdom’s edge,
□ The head alone earns the immortals’ praise.
□ Movement radiant, □ ever full,
□ The clear spring’s glow is worth observing.
□ Before it are but these few things,
□ The heart discerns the mountain’s play.
□ Speaking of cultivation, □ elegant phrases,
□ Life’s jade disc shines resplendent.
□ Within, mercury and lead are fused,
□ The *Jia* wood’s transmission is incandescent.
□ The Fire Mother, □ the son unrecorded,
□ Master, point to the cool truths.

「□根甘液是真因，□都得此丹无价。
□ Guard the elixir-field (*Dantian*), □ discern its essence thus—
□ O noble one, □ recognize the true Dao, lest it falter.

□包四象立虚名，□言千日成功课。
□ The Four Emblems (*Sì Xiàng*) contained, □ fame in vain bestowed—
□ A thousand days of practice, □ words but empty boast.

□作良缘，□丝缠锁，□花开处琼英妥。
□ Cultivate auspicious bonds, □ silk threads entwined like fetters—
□ Where the flower blooms, □ jade essence (*Qióngyīng*) is secured.

□人返得丈夫身，□身风了千千个。
□ The mortal returns, □ attaining the body of a worthy man—
□ The Dao’s breath (*Fēng*) dispels myriad illusions.

---
*Another Stanza: A Farewell to Daoist Friends at Bai Lu Guan*

□要吹灯，□中有作，□离暂别休疑却。
□ The lamp must be extinguished, □ yet work remains within—
□ Though parting is brief, □ no need for doubt or hesitation.

□游白鹿观头看，□前便是成行脚。
□ At Bai Lu Guan’s peak, □ the wanderer’s path is clear—
□ Before you lies the Dao’s fulfillment.

□要归来，□宵为约。
□ When you return, □ the night shall be our pact—
□ The silk of truth (*Zhēn*) shall never sever.

□诚语朴决重欢，□间紧把猿儿缚。
□ Sincere words, □ plain and decisive, bring joy—
□ In close moments, □ bind the *Yuan* (monkey, metaphor for unruly mind).

---
*Drunken at Penglai* (*Zuì Pēnglái*)

□时间有吏，拱手前来，谨传台旨。
□ At the appointed hour, □ the officials arrive, bowing—
□ Carefully conveying Your Highness’s decree.

□晚难参，□俟辰先起。
□ Evening makes it hard to attend, □ await the morning’s dawn instead—
□ Let us rise before the hour.

□至庭阶，□争通报，□上人心喜。
□ Upon reaching the hall’s steps, □ they vie to announce—
□ The Master’s heart is pleased.

□出尊谈，□推学道，须留妙理。
□ The Master steps forth to converse, □ urging study of the Dao—
□ Retain the subtle principles (*Miàolǐ*).

□液琼浆，□生三宝，□脉光门，□华丽美。
□ The essence yields nectar (*Qióngjiāng*), □ birthing the Three Treasures (*Sānbǎo*)—
□ The vein’s luminous Dao-gate (*Guāngmén*), □ its radiance ever splendid.

□抵神清，□俾气无睡。
□ It reaches the clarity of spirit (*Shénqīng*), □ letting *qi* know no slumber—
□ The mind is ever wakeful.

□下知州，□圭休禀，□自然仙瑞。
□ Descend to the prefecture, □ the *Gui* grain’s virtue (*Dé*) is naturally received—
□ The immortal’s blessings (*Xiānrúi*) arise effortlessly.

□现灵芝，□游宝洞，蓬莱一醉。
□ The *Língzhī* (spirit mushroom) appears, □ the treasure-cave explored—
□ A single drunken spell at Penglai.

---
*Another Stanza: Ode to Snow*

□然间云雾，密布长天，徧空呈瑞。
□ Suddenly, clouds and mists gather, □ densely veiling the vast sky—
□ Across the heavens, □ auspicious signs (*Ruì*) unfold.

□屑飘飘，舞风前轻坠。
□ Snowflakes drift and sway, □ before the wind, softly descending—
□ Delicate as whispers.

□面凝酥，山头铺粉，又爽兼鲜媚。
□ The earth’s surface hardens like butter, □ mountain peaks dusted with powder—
□ Both crisp and fresh, □ a sight of pure delight.

□姹婴儿，相将拥手，同来游觑。
□ The snowflakes, □ like playful infants, press close—
□ Hand in hand, we come to gaze upon them.

□裹全真，□实中迎，□宝满插，琼花荣贵。
□ Wrapped in the True Reality (*Quánzhēn*), □ we meet within its substance—
□ Treasures brimming, □ jade blossoms (*Qiónghuā*) adorned with splendor.

□脉和明，更三光分锐。
□ The veins harmonize with clarity, □ the Three Lights (*Sānguāng*) sharpened further—
□ Illumination refined.

□地生辉，震方通耀，放烂银霞起。
□ The earth emits its own radiance, □ shaking the quarters, light spreads—
□ A rotten silver cloud (*Yínxiá*) ascends in splendor.

□见师呼，仙童邀我，蓬莱一醉。
□ The Master summons, □ the immortal child invites me—
□ A single drunken spell at Penglai.

---
*End of Volume Six of the Complete Works of Chongyang Zhenren (Zhuangzi)*
#1 The original word card was mistakenly written as 『*Dìngfēngbō* (Stabilizing the Wind Waves).』
#2 This word card should be 『*Tiàorénjiāo* (Teasing the Heart of Man).』

*Volume Seven of the Complete Works of Chongyang Zhenren (Zhuangzi)*
*Composed by Master Zhongnan Shan Chongyangzi (Wang Zhe)*

「Word: *Jiěpèi-lìng* (解佩令)
□ Dwelling in my hermitage, seated in stillness—
□ the more I flee worldly toil, □ the greater the dust of labor grows.
□ Greedy for rice and flour, □ I watch the passing of travelers.
□ With staff in hand and dagger at my side, □ I have a magnetic bowl (*cíwǎn*) and five-earthenware pot—
□ a spoon of sinew, □ a ladle of bone, □ a steamer piled high.
□ Sweeping fields and scrubbing pots, □ extinguishing lamps to dampen fire.
□ At the gate, I bolt the door; □ stepping out, I lock it tight.
□ Originally, I sought tranquility—
□ yet many things plague me daily;
□ hard to bear is the chariot of □ five-colored clouds (*wǔsè yún*).

□ Turned to *Zhuǎndiào Chǒusnú’ér* (转调丑奴儿)
□ I bitterly urge the foolish man—
□ wealth and desire (*cáisè*) drain his spirit.
□ Do not cling to profit’s bridle or fame’s lock,
□ for youth’s bloom flees swift as an arrow’s flight—
□ do not linger!
□ Cross the Delusion’s Ford (*Míjīn*) early,
□ delight in purity, □ cultivate the True Self (*Tiānzhēn*).
□ When the nature is perfected and the elixir (*Dānjié*) forms,
□ only then will you know □ the strange vistas of Penglai.
□ Here, truly, lies another Long Life (*Chángchūn*).

**解佩令#1** (Jiěpèi-lìng) □ *Presented to Mǎ Yuè*
□ Exhort me, Master Yifu of Exhortation (*Fúfēng Yìfǔ*),
□ to hear my Daoist teachings.
□ You have yet to truly enter the Way (*Rùdào*).
□ Yet there will come a Great Blessing (*Hóngxǐ*),
□ when old friends reunite—
□ like the mountains of Lu, returning once more;
□ listen carefully to their profound mysteries (*Xuánlǐ*).
□ Do not leave these peaks,
□ for here is where you must dwell.»

「兼乞觅、庵粮便利。
When seeking alms for the hermit’s rice,
□ wait until the moon is full and round—
□ then together we shall honor the Master’s rites,
□ dwelling in the Ten Isles, all rejoicing as one.

As for the nature of life and death,
□ search day and night without cease.
□ Illumination shines—what matter fat or lean?
□ As the sun and moon drift westward,
□ the North Star stands firm at the cosmic pivot;
□ celestial flowers bloom, their fragrant essence unconfined.
□ All is empty yet fully manifest,
□ all is void yet utterly transparent.
□ In the chill purity, we frolic in boundless ease.
□ At ease in the True, beyond the gusts of wind,
□ we ride the essence of clouds and crimson mists.
□ Gathered as cloud-companions, mingling with crimson friends.

**On Tea Without Absolute Grade**
□ Tea without absolute grade—
□ the truest virtue is supreme.
□ Invite the honored guests to come and go.
□ When the cup steams and the pot boils,
□ clouds surge like snow-waves;
□ sip lightly—qi refined, spirit refreshed.
□ Seven bowls like Lu Quan’s—
□ drink them, and clarity unfolds.
□ Know its taste, as did Master Zhao of Zhongzhou.

**New *Jiěpèi* Verse**
□ Sung anew by Wang Haifeng,
□ composed together in harmony.
□ Beneath the moon’s light,
□ four voices share their brilliance.

**Composed After Admiring Liu’s Poetry**
□ A lifetime of wild folly,
□ the heart-monkey’s careless flight.
□ The *Yezhang Collection*—
□ read it endlessly without rest.
□ Freeing the nature, seizing the numinous,
□ recognizing past transgressions,
□ surpassing cultivation in one stroke.
□ Four decades have passed—
□ wisdom’s light now lofty and vast.
□ The flavor in verse meets the Dao face-to-face.
□ A single phrase, clear as day—
□ then Master Qiqing’s words dawn:
*"Willow-shore, dawn wind, fading moon."*

**Chrysanthemum Sky**
□ This elixir’s divine power brings singular joy,
□ healing life and death to perfect wholeness.
□ Named *Zǐjīn Dān* (Purple-Gold Elixir).
□ One dose ensures eternal peace and safety.
□ The Three Fields’ treasures refined,
□ a pearl emerges from the muddy cauldron.
□ Five hues, nine radiant mists converge,
□ gathered to present at the Daoist altar.

**On Wind**
□ This elixir’s divine power brings singular splendor,
□ curing the body’s stubborn numbness.
□ Its effects are threefold.
□ No need for warm wine—
□ choose salted tea instead.
□ Taken, it renews sinews and bones,
□ even forging cinnabar elixir.
□ Instantly, spirit clears, qi brightens—
□ most praiseworthy, most praiseworthy,
□ each step wreathed in cloud and mist.

**On the Eyes**
□ This elixir’s divine power bears a renowned name,
□ curing the eyes’ restless affections.
□ One drop renders clarity pure.
□ Naturally, one gazes upward,
□ recognizing the path ahead.
□ Further, with a golden comb’s light strokes,
□ it banishes dust from the pupils.
□ The mundane world now shines empty and bright,
□ most refined, most refined—
□ the Three Luminaries blaze anew.

**On Coughing**
□ This elixir’s divine power bears singular sentiment,
□ curing the lungs’ trapped melodies.
□ It rectifies the water’s gold.
□ It frees the public from their plight,
□ granting voices beyond measure.
□ No longer plagued by cold winds or scorching heat,
□ the Five Evils lose their grip.
□ Seasonal colors fade, wealth is conserved—
□ age-old, age-old,
□ life and death now sought in harmony.

**On Food**
□ This elixir’s divine power bears a singular method,
□ curing the five viscera’s deepest afflictions.
□ One dose, taken with broth,
□ instantly permeates—
□ peace and safety restored.
□ Further, the True and Mysterious reveal their secrets—
□ let the sages ponder carefully.
□ Nurture qi, preserve spirit intact,
□ longevity, longevity—
□ eternal abode in serene coolness.

**Coincidence with the *Bǔsuànzǐ* (Diviner’s Verse)**
**For the Monk Who Sought at Miàojué Temple**
□ Miàojué’s compassionate proof
□ leads directly to the Bodhi path.
□ Daily, he opens the Gate of Expedients,
□ his wisdom illuminating all sentient beings.
□ Seated in snow, like Śākyamuni’s honor,
□ facing the wall, as Dàmó’s enlightenment dawned.
□ Observing this, the karmic fruit of conditional practice,
□ he dwells now in Tuóshuà Heaven’s realm.

**Coincidence with the *Bǔsuànzǐ* (Diviner’s Verse)**
**Each Stanza Begins and Ends with the Sound of a Horse’s Neigh**
□ Trusting the water, the wild monkey roams free,
□ unbound by the wind’s mischief.
□ To go where the clouds drift, to ride the wind’s whim,
□ mount the fine steed, sit steady on the fragrant silk saddle.
□ South and north, east and west—
□ choose the highest or lowest.
□ Everywhere, coming and going at will,
□ the bow drawn, the pearl shot with precision.
□ One fine stallion, its brilliance like a painting.
□ Yet saddled with silver, its body bound—
□ how can it gallop wild and free?
□ Better to run mad, untethered, unshackled.
□ Shaking its mane, defying the stable’s chains,
□ as a wild horse, it frolics in boundless ease.
□ Truly true, luminously clear—
□ moving through the void’s ethereal mist,
□ riding the wind-horse, trusting the drift.
□ Occupying the incandescent, the radiant—
□ traversing the clear sky’s boundless expanse,
□ mounted on the cloud-steed, at ease, unbound.
□ Chasing away the midday crow,
□ snatching the moon’s hare.
□ Then, clad in crystalline light,
□ the Golden Horse rests—
□ only then is Double Ninth celebrated.
□ The cosmic pivots reveal their True Function,
□ transforming substance into True Delight.
□ Here, one still knows the boundless roam—
□ the Jade Steed departs, entering the cloud-path.

**Coincidence with the *Bǔsuànzǐ* (Diviner’s Verse) #3**
**Seeking a Friend**
□ There’s a wind-loving one,
□ searching the sea for a worthy companion.
□ Only because his heart is too tightly bound,
□ the mind-horse confined—
□ his whole body erupts in scabs.
□ Slowly, he seeks with care,
□ year by year, month by month,
□ until he finds the Central Four Treasures Pearl.
□ The swift steed carries him into the Western Pass.

**Coincidence with the *Bǔsuànzǐ* (Diviner’s Verse)**
**Opening the Gate and Transforming into Mǎ Yuè**
□ You must resolve to walk with steadfast heart,
□ I must resolve to guard with steadfast heart.
□ A hundred days of sealed gates—
□ then I shall speak.
□ Open the four seasons’ flowers,
□ unfurl the three springs’ willows.
□ Recognize this original person,
□ and together drink the Elixir of Longevity.

**Coincidence with the *Bǔsuànzǐ* (Diviner’s Verse)**
**Composed in the Snow**
□ Who knows this wind’s wildness?
□ Who recognizes these three sages?
□ Just as the heat’s oppressiveness yields to cool relief,
□ the cold now feels like warmth.
□ Uplifting the words of the Perfect Ones,
□ I gained the True Immortal’s secret.
□ In the ninety-nineth frost, flowers bloom anew,
□ yet in the Dog Days, snow still falls.

**Lament for the World’s Delusion**
□ Worthy of lament are the world’s people—
□ who would dare to gaze heavenward, to seek the Dao?»

---

**On the Wandering of the Northern Dipper and Southern Pole**
The Northern Dipper and Southern Pole shift day and night,
A flying hare and rabbit flee their bounds.

Yet still you are tormented by this world,
Still grasping at greed and jealousy.
Soon will the **Yingzhou** (Underworld) summon you,
What words shall you plead?

No need to rush your cultivation,
There will be those who come to meet you.
Already bound with white clouds as companions,
Ever composing verses and rhyme.

Wrap yourself in stillness, turn to serene ease,
Joy returns as you gaze upon the light.

A youth in green stands before you,
Presenting the **Ledger of Longevity** (长生簿).

**Fisherman’s Defiance**
Leaping free from the cage of the mundane to seek true life,
The human heart ever craves the tranquil and the pure.
This is the swiftest path to true cultivation.
Through **Chan** (禅) and **dhyana** (定), observe the void’s vast expanse.
Awaken to the **original nature** (祖宗), ever more alert—
Flame-red, blazing like the **golden essence** (金定).
Gradually, the radiant light becomes clear and bright.
The **Perfect Ones** (通贤) and **Sages** (圣) tread the path of **non-birth** (无生) with steadfast virtue.

---

**To My Nephew Yuan Bi and Yuan Zuo After My Brother’s Departure**
My brother Yuan Bi came before, aiding you both,
Honoring our elders—do you still remember this?
Yesterday, I laughed as your heart turned to clarity.
Do not despair, for in time I shall surely arrange your fate.
This **transmission** (这个) comes only from this **transmission**—
How can one escape the cycle of birth and death?
Leave graves, abandon ancestral mounds, break free from bonds.
Avert calamities, for on the path of **non-birth** (无生) all becomes cause and effect.

Who knows if **King Wang** (王三) can trade in the Dao?
Where the **Dao-heart** (道心) stands firm, retreat is impossible.
Ever wear the **Three Lights** (三光) with reverence.
With reverence worn, you rend the world’s net and dwell beyond dust.
The wind brings harm as it takes its course—
Today, seek no blame in those who come for coin.
You have gained the **freedom of the carefree** (逍遥),
True **liberation** (自在)—
Carry the clouds and return to **Penglai** (蓬莱) to meet.

---

**To My Dao-Friend**
This **King Wang** (王风) bows in deep respect,
Pearls and water-rice feasts indeed worthy of envy.
Filled to the brim, his **pure qi** (白气) shines forth.
His **pure qi** shines—
Today, I ask only of the **lotus petals** (梨花片).
When the time is ripe, they open fully;
After my words, their fragrance grows ever sweet.
High upon the tree, true **jade-like purity** (真玉) gleams,
True **jade-like purity** gleams—
Under the bright moon, it illuminates the **Pure Cool Pavilion** (清凉院).

---

**To Ning Sheng**
Calling forth **Third Brother’s wife, Ninth Sister** (三郎妻九姐),
Two **mulberry trees** (橡) merge into one dwelling.
Their bones become beams, their skin the tiles.
Do not boast—
Our parents have already guided them to their home.
I wish as a son to serve my family,
She wishes as a daughter to wed—
Uncle and aunt tend to their duties—when shall they cease?
Daily, the **offerings of merit** (功钱) are hard to repay.
Hear my words—
Long practice **filial piety** (孝顺) shall repay this debt.

---

**To the Dao-Friend from Jingzhao**
Seeking **obtainment** (得得) within **obtainment** (中间),
**King Wang’s silent verse** (默诀) is only for **King Liu** (王六).
If you seek purity like white jade,
Stay alone in retreat—
I alone must rid myself of **emotional desires** (情欲).
This **spiritual youth** (灵童) is bright as a candle,
Ever awake, able to sing the **Hymn of Non-Birth** (无生曲).
The **public** (公家) does not recognize him.
Do not seek him—
A **clear heart** (心澄) is the true message.

---

**At the Stone Gate Hermitage on Kunlun Mountain**
Entering **Stone Gate Mountain** (石门山) to dwell above,
Brothers’ hands and feet find no rest.
Three times a day, we meet in long embrace.
To the kitchen gone,
Chopping firewood, fetching water, stoking the pot—

---

**To the Dao-Friend from Jingzhao**
If you urge me to join the **rushing currents** (同流疾作) of worldly affairs,
Do not let even a spark of **delusion** (一点) cloud my heart.

I shall speak clearly one sentence:
Since **awakening** (开悟),
I dare not lightly reveal the **heavenly secrets** (天机).

At the **fifth watch** (五更), I leave the **hermitage** (舍),
Only to meet another **hermitage-leaving one** (出舍郎) in return—
Then the **wind** (便) rages wild.
**Success** (成功) is achieved,
Arriving at **Penglai** (蓬庄).
I repay that person with **clarity** (如惺悟),
Engaging in **profound discussion** (好商量).

At the **fifth watch** (五更), I depart—
Detailed and refined (细消详).
At the **first watch** (一更), *lo!* I meet a **hermitage-leaving one** (出会郎),
Far from my native home.
On the journey ahead,
I move with steady resolve.
First, I grasp the **dark tempest** (黑飙),
Sealing it within my **skin-bag** (皮囊).
Bound and secured,
It drifts no more.
At the **second watch** (二更), *lo!* I meet a **hermitage-leaving one** (出舍郎),
Transformed into **silver frost** (银霜).
Boiling water, burning fire—
A husband and wife bow in unison,
Entering the **Elixir Chamber** (丹房).
Sleeping together in retreat,
Lying on the **tooth-rack couch** (牙床).
At the **third watch** (三更), *lo!* I meet a **hermitage-leaving one** (出舍郎),
The most fitting time.
The **divine elixir** (神丹) is ready,
Nurturing the **child-mother** (养儿娘).
A perfect union of **yin and yang** (阴阳),
They ride in the **carriage** (车厢).
The **Golden Ox Boy** (金牛子),
Busy with his **elixir-carrying** (载搬忙).
At the **fourth watch** (四更), *lo!* I meet a **hermitage-leaving one** (出舍郎),
And find **cool refreshment** (清凉).
On the **multi-tiered pavilion** (重楼),
I drink the **Nectar of Heaven** (琼浆).
I dance and sing, awake or drunk,
Yet the more I taste, the sweeter it becomes.
The **true essence** (真滋味),
A thousandfold **fragrant heart** (万般香心).

At the **fifth watch** (五更), *lo!* I meet a **hermitage-leaving one** (出舍郎),
With **no defense** (没堤防).
**Unobstructed**, I pass through the **Bright Hall** (明堂).
A **radiant pearl** (明珠) rolls in the **imperial robes** (颠倒衮),
A **auspicious sign** (瑞中祥).
On Kunlun’s heights,
I release the **glow of clouds** (放霞光).
Recognizing the **Five Varieties of Hermitage-Leaving Ones** (五般出舍郎),
Their **black and white** (黑白) are revealed.
Among them, the **crimson** (赤) shines brightest,
With **emerald and golden** (青黄) hues interspersed.
*Lo!* *Lo!* *Lo!* *Lo!* *Lo!* (哩啰啰□哩啰哩),
The **wondrous Dao** (妙玄) is supreme.
When **perfectly refined** (玲珑了),
It **resonates like bells** (便玎珰).

---
**Ode to Chess** (丑奴儿#4)
Two players vie in skill, each boasting mastery,
Yet their paths **cross and conflict** (路路相违).
Move by move, they **deliberate** (子细挨依),
Only when the **end of the age** (劫尽) do they **break free** (解了围).
The **foolish and lost** (愚迷) fail to grasp the **double meaning** (双关意),
Each concealing their **hidden strategies** (藏机).
Who is right, who is wrong?
The **spectators** (傍观) smirk in cold amusement.

---
**On Confusion and Longing** (迷怀)
In the **marketplace** (廛中), there dwells a **practitioner** (修行子),
Yet he cannot leave the **fire-hearth** (火院).
Only when **pushed away** (推辞),
Does he **reluctantly turn back** (恁不回头), awaiting some day.

Today’s fate is not guaranteed for tomorrow’s,
And **the Great Termination** (大限) knows no one.
How **pitiful** (可) is this **foolishness** (愚痴),
Waiting in the **wild outskirts** (荒郊) to gnash his teeth!

Last night, I lay alone on the **ice-ridge path** (冰棱道),
Observing the **Three Radiances** (三耀).
With a **free and tranquil heart** (自在心安),
I feel the **cool refreshment** (清凉) yet not the cold.
The **tail-end of the river** (尾闾) flows past my **spine** (夹脊上),
Its **rolling waves** (辘辘) carry me along.
It **penetrates the mud pellet** (透入泥丸),
Returning **youth** (返老) and granting **longevity** (长生)—
A joy beyond compare.
The **people of Caoxi** (曹溪一路) struggle to **awaken** (难悟),
How could they abandon their **beautiful wives** (妍妻)?
Unable to bear **solitude** (孤俩),
At night, they sink deeper into **confusion** (越越迷).
Though the **path of longevity** (长生路) is clear,
Who among them can **ascend** (跻)?
What **eastern or western** (东西) methods?
Who dares **extract themselves** (抽身) from the **filthy mud** (污泥)?

If **common folk** (凡人) understand the **Three Radiances** (三耀),
They shall **form noble bonds** (结良缘).
When they **discover the true Dao** (真玄),
Only then do they **trust the Great Sage of Emptiness** (虚空出大仙).
A **single grain of gold elixir** (金丹一粒) must not be **wasted** (无为漏),
For it holds the **refined essence of anger** (怒精妍).
Its **luminous roundness** (明莹光圆),
A thousand **rays of cloud-glow** (万道霞光) ascend to heaven.
Like a **dream** (如梦), fleeting yet profound.

「Ninghai folk all wake to insight,
When shall we meet again like this?

Only may I **replenish the Golden Lotus** (重金莲),
And **nurture noble causes** (作做良因) with care.

**The way home, the way home** (归路),
Where **endless white clouds and emerald mists** (白云翠雾) fill the gaze.

---

**To the County Magistrate** (赠县令)
Daily here we feast and revel,
**Feasting on flesh** (食肉) while **virtuous officials gather** (诸公总善).
Only **Lord of the Harmonic Wind** (害风王) need not blame
My **frequent visits** (频来) to your presence.

**Magistrate, Magistrate** (知县),
Now is the time to **act with beneficence** (与人方便).

---

**In Response to a Friend’s Kind Words** (蒙友惠词)
The **Bright Moon** (明月) endures through ancient and modern times,
Yet how can **Huazong’s reckless tongue** (华宗海口) bear it?
Wrapped in **dark caves** (黑窟), my head abides,
**Gloom** (黯暗) knows no **night or day** (不分夜昼).

**My friend, my friend** (吾友),
How shall you **grasp the method** (如何下手)?

**Yangliu Branch** (杨柳枝)
**In a dream, I awaken to the lofty celestial moon** (梦悟青霄月正高),
**Plucking the coiled peach** (射蟠桃).
A **single white brushstroke** (一枝白笔) meets its fate,
**Yet also the blade** (更兼刀).

**Words flow like ink as they are penned** (应手诗词随写染),
**Guided by the wind of the *Cao*** (运风骚).
Upon **jade slips** (玉笺), **cloud-waves rise** (起云涛),
**Leisurely and unbound** (任陶陶).
A **breath’s duration** (一息) brings the **waning vital sphere** (衰气球),
**Unleashing the wind of elegance** (骋风流).
Do not come—**a breath’s absence shatters the sphere** (破胞抽),
**This time, rest** (这回休).

If you **still follow the old paths of Chang Jian’s trade** (常建贩),
**Begin anew** (复从头).
**Gather the vital sphere** (气重收), **wrap it close** (胞儿裹面),
**Again, refine and bend** (再罗偻).
Who **recognizes the golden well beyond the sky** (天边一井金)?
**Purple light invades** (紫光侵).
**Day after day, it confronts the eyes** (朝日朝日),
Yet **no one seeks it** (没人寻).
Only **I, in stillness, know its whereabouts** (静中知去处),
**Worthy of trust** (自堪任).
**Measure and weigh to enter the Pearl Forest** (尽斤尽两入珠林),
**Ascend the lofty peaks** (出高岑).

---

**Refining the Vital Essence** (捣练子)
**Monkeys ride horses** (猿骑马), **displaying wild chaos** (呈颠傻),
How can they be **seized and subdued** (难擒难捉)?
**Oh-ho!** (哩啰□), **Oh-ho!** (哩啰□).
**The wisdom-blade opens** (慧刀开), **all cut down** (齐下杀),
**Teach you to recognize the root and source** (认得根源也).
**Oh-ho!** (哩啰□), **Oh-ho!** (哩啰□).
**Water and fire combined** (水兼火), **Kan and Li** (坎和离),
How can you **know their interplay** (消息怎生知)?
**Oh-ho!** (哩啰□), **Oh-ho!** (哩啰□).
**Cease refining, cease cultivation** (休烧炼，莫修持),
**For it is all these very things** (元来只是这些儿).
**Oh-ho!** (哩啰□), **Oh-ho!** (哩啰□).
**Refining the Vital Essence** (捣练子), **Harmonic Wind Brother** (害风哥),
**A single body leaps beyond death and life’s waves** (一身跃出死生波).
**Oh-ho!** (哩啰□), **Oh-ho!** (哩啰□).
**This is the true freedom of effortless ease** (便是逍遥真自在),
**No one restrains—trust the humming and sighing** (没人拘管信吟哦).
**Oh-ho!** (哩啰□), **Oh-ho!** (哩啰□).

With **blade and compass** (用刀圭),
**Severing the confusion** (剖昏迷),
How can you **harmonize it all** (合和一处怎生携)?
**Oh-ho!** (哩啰□), **Oh-ho!** (哩啰□).
**Heads fall** (人头落), **rainbows appear** (现虹霓),
**White lotus blooms from green mud** (白莲花朵出青泥).
**Oh-ho!** (哩啰□), **Oh-ho!** (哩啰□).
**The sea of fame, the river of strife** (名利海，是非河),
**Beyond the Harmonic Wind’s lofty slope** (王风出了上高坡).
**Oh-ho!** (哩啰□), **Oh-ho!** (哩啰□).
**Ten years of merit, and the task is done** (十年功行满),
**Laughing beneath the deep white clouds** (白云深处笑呵呵).
**Oh-ho!** (哩啰□), **Oh-ho!** (哩啰□).
**The Three Elixirs’ treasure** (三丹宝),
**Hard to divide and refine** (难分剖),
**In dimness, how can it be preserved** (默默怎生保)?
**Oh-ho!** (哩啰□), **Oh-ho!** (哩啰□).
**In the void, held in embrace** (在虚空，长怀抱),
**A crimson robe wraps the child, a new black hat** (绯衫裹子新乌帽).
**Oh-ho!** (哩啰□), **Oh-ho!** (哩啰□).

---
**Treading the Grass** (踏莎行)

**Treading the Grass** (踏莎行)

Do not boast of sons, nor praise your daughters,
For with the master, they bring harm to your fate.
Scraping fat and grease from others’ bones,
Only repaying debts from past lives’ sins.

Gilded halls delight the eye, yet pity stirs the heart—
Even iron fortresses crumble in time.
Many sins you’ve indulged in, now your own to bear,
When the eyes close, how will you wear the crown?

---
**Another Spring for Another House**
Wives and daughters, do not sigh,
Sons and grandsons, hold no grudge—
I have other friends in the clouds.

Free of shackles, my heart knows it well,
Cool realms revealed, only I see them.

Step by step, clouds deepen,
Bay by bay, waters shallow—
Fragrant winds spray my face wherever I go.

On Kunlun’s heights, I wander free,
Wrapped in mist and clouds, refining my essence.

---
**Self-Composed**
Gold misleads the mind, the mind controls gold—
Give and take, when does it end?
Even stubborn bronze wears away,
What use has mortal flesh to flee life and death?

Turn back early, seek the wondrous truth,
Carefully examine—do not speak without guidance.
Two paths open within the belly,
One bright point shines clear in the heart.

Mercury wraps the clear spring,
Lead holds fiery brilliance—
Pouring upside-down, spreading sweet dew.

Tiger’s roar shakes the Green Pole’s blue,
Dragon’s chant summons the White Tiger’s white.

Claim the true field, divide the paths,
Plant and pluck the golden peach yourself.
Jade boys bear it aloft in their palms,
At the jade feast, it may be shared.

The Dao without name, the harm of winds,
Wrapped in *Treading the Grass*, joy unfolds.
Step by step, refining brings it to birth,
Lotus steps follow, never parting.

Emerging from clear springs,
Surging to the Azure Void—
Forming clouds, gathering canopies, vast and grand.
Outer fragrance draws the radiant light,
Inner luminosity illuminates the true elixir.

Unrecognized, ashamed—
Seek guidance, let compassion arise.
After meals, do not waste your thoughts.
How dare doctors examine,
Or others weigh in—
The talisman’s water is the true seed.

*Lī□ līlū lī□ lī□,*
Forever walking toward Penglai’s jade halls.

---
**In Gratitude for a Gift**
Felt slippers left behind,
Wooden helmets shared—
With humble sincerity, I repay your kindness.

Endless feasts may be prepared,
A thousand flavors savored—
The tranquil sage, the pure bodhisattva,
All owe this to such gifts.

Wrap mercury and lead in your head,
Fill them fully—do not scatter.

---
**To a Friend**
Last year’s hemp, this year’s wheat—
One hemp, one wheat, passing the message.
Left, a golden cake—yang’s birth,
Right, a silver vessel—yin concealed.

No partiality, no inversion—
The heart-lamp shines, discerning fate.
Not strolling through Zhongnan’s streets,
But knowing the truth on Jingdong’s road.

---
**On Burning Incense**
The body is the censer,
The heart, the incense—
One essence, clearly divided.
Burning at the proper hour,
Piercing Kunlun’s peaks,
Incense curls into auspicious omens.

Rising to the cloudy heights,
Distinct and wondrous—
Forming clouds, gathering canopies, enfolding the mystery.
In the Golden Flower Hall, I wander free,
Beside the Jade Emperor’s seat, I attend.

---
**To a Friend**
One point of luminous clarity,
Two straight paths—
How to begin, how to act?
Teach me to bow toward Heaven’s hall,
Lest I stumble into the Underworld’s grasp.

The sun turns the Golden Rooster,
The moon births the Jade Rabbit—
All things in the cosmic net move in measure.
Do not cling to prolonged life,
But firmly grasp the golden essence.

---
**Kunlun’s Circular Hermitage**
The model is made,
Yet do not raise the beams—
How would the masters know my convenience?
Water talismans do not pass here,
But fate has led me to Wen’deng County.

Each must hold fast to cultivation,
Swiftly return to refining—
Its essence reveals itself to you.

Now gradually it aligns with the Mysterious,
Then often we meet face to face.

---
**Burning the Hermitage**
Years of toil, dwelling in Liu and Jiang,
Daily dust in the hermitage’s halls.
Suddenly, the true fire blazes open,
Burning it all to the supreme.

I urge all masters—
Do not grow disheartened,
For we have deeper truths to share.
Only the ashes remain, unvisited,
Penglai’s cloud paths open for passage.

Searching in sleep, acting in dreams,
Eyes closed, recognizing the true—ever joyful.
Imagine the Three Treasures as divine,
Forging the Nine-Turn elixir.
Gathering auspicious clouds,
Coming and going between Azure Void and earth,
Following and leading, only cranes and phoenixes remain.
White light in ten thousand rays springs from the garden,
Red light, one point, burns at the center.

---
*End of Volume Seven of the Complete Authentic Words of Chongyang*
#1 The original word card was mistakenly written as *"Again"* (又).
#2 It was said: The original mistakenly wrote *"Field"* (田) instead of *"True"* (正).
#3 This word card should be *"Coining Divination"* (卜算子) with a *"Ho!"* (喝马) before and after, each once. The three words *"Seeking a Friend"* (寻知友) are the word’s title.
#4 The original word card was mistakenly written as *"Coining Divination"* (卜算子).

---
*Volume Eight of the Complete Authentic Words of Chongyang*
Composed by Master Chongyang of Zhongnan, Wang Zhi.

**Volume Eight of the Complete Authentic Words of Chongyang**

**Coining Divination (卜算子) – Seeking a Friend (寻知友)**

Nine-nine’s mysteries now revealed in speech,
The bright moon clearly shines upon the jade pool.
True insight into the double meaning’s essence,
The first three threes and the last three threes.

Nine-nine’s words must be corrected,
Refining the original nature to its primal source.
Only return to yang from yin,
And resolve to pure, elegant chanting.

O Virtuous Ones, O Virtuous Ones,
Grant me leave to compose *As If in a Dream (如梦令)*.

Nine-one’s chill begins with inherent cause,
The winter *qi* freely unfurls and expands.
There, the fierce cold of the southern lands congeals,
Just as the mid-winter node arrives.

Hidden wonders, hidden wonders,
Within lies the new yang’s subtle emergence.

Nine-two’s austere yin is piercing,
White snow spread far along its edges.
Yet still it nourishes the numinous root,
Guiding the yellow sprouts to thorough examination.

As such, as such,
The Northern Sea’s divine tortoise drinks freely.

Nine-three’s cornered *qi* accumulates,
The water’s face entirely frozen.
This nature’s firmest and most steadfast,
Unfaltering brilliance radiates outward.

Afar it sends, afar it sends,
Reflecting light to distant horizons.

Nine-four’s cold wind like an arrow,
Its might pervades all with ease.
Chasing these demons in flight,
Praise the auspicious one who sees them fall.

Worthy of envy, worthy of envy,
Hidden yet revealed—one radiant expanse.

Nine-five’s Heavenly Pool fully unfrozen,
The gentle scene now inviting.
Observe the ridge-top plum blossoms,
Warming, already luxuriant.

Incense table, incense table,
Monopolizing true yang’s half.

Nine-six’s *qi* expands and clarifies,
Ascending and descending, harmonizing.
Flowing universally, it now reveals,
The Daoist Sage’s virtue and noble worth.

Patterns and threads, patterns and threads,
Ready to unfurl jade petals, precious blooms.

Nine-seven’s gates open to eight veins,
Piercing through forever, no separation.
Like exhaling misty vapors,
Revolving ceaselessly in pristine whiteness—
Unfathomable, unfathomable,
One point at the center, terrifying.

Nine-eight’s harmony is complete,
All things now aligned and balanced.
Light shines everywhere,
Dazzling, ever more brilliant—
Connecting, connecting,
Lengthening into jade branches, jade leaves.

Nine-nine’s eightfold seal is locked,
Gathering light like fire.
Flames form crimson clouds,
Enveloping the face—heaven’s flowers are perfect.
Completed, completed,
One luminous pearl, radiant.

Nine-nine’s words now perfected,
Who else but Wang Zhi, named Zhe?
The refined name knows its brilliance,
The Daoist title *Chongyang* is distinct.

Joyous, joyous,
One grain of golden elixir forever sealed.

---

**West River Moon (西江月) – Four Falsehoods (四假)**

Worthy of lament: fire-wind, earth-water,
For them, form is forged.
They teach humans suffering through daily scriptures,
Plunging them into perfumed visions and sounds.
Only I shake my head, unmoved,
Morning after morning, dwelling in the Yellow Court.
Naturally silent and serene, the true spirit gathers.
Five-colored clouds of light enfold and settle.

---

**Four Falsehoods (四民)**

Worthy of lament: farmers, artisans, merchants, laborers,
Each boasts skill in their own trade.
Within, clever schemes multiply,
Yet still they vie in empty strife.
Only I shake my head, unmoved,
Clinging to simplicity and plainness.
Clear as still water, firm as ice,
Their own fruit of perfection is assured.

---

**Four Falsehoods (四害)**

Worthy of lament: lust, greed, wealth, *qi*,
The world is long ensnared by these.
All seek them like roasted fowl,
Their minds clouded, their wisdom lost.
Only I shake my head, unmoved,
Content to endure solitude and sorrow.
In coarse robes, plain food, and yellow pickled greens,
I cultivate the embryo of the transcendent.

---

**Four Falsehoods (四方)**

Worthy of lament: east, west, south, north,
Misguided travelers suffer.
Come and go as they will in red dust,
Drawn only by fame and gain.
Only I shake my head, unmoved,
Within stillness, my essence is fixed and true.
Refined and gathered, *qi* and spirit harmonize,
Forever joyous in the natural and unadorned.

---

**Four Falsehoods (四时)**

Worthy of lament: spring, winter, autumn, summer,
Strange flowers and plants vie to bloom.
The passing years unnoticed, urging on,
What use is regret when it’s too late?
Only I shake my head, unmoved,
Chasing inner virtues, ever near.
Green, red, yellow, white, black—pure and bright,
The true gold is forged, resounding.

---

**Four Falsehoods (四宝)**

Worthy of lament: brush, inkstone, paper, ink,
Binding fate with rules and schemes.
Ordinary scribbles always become texts,
Called the "literary quarters" with annotations.
Only I shake my head, unmoved,
Commanding the Great Record to trace its origins.
One spark of spirit unfurls at will,
Returning to true suchness, gazing back.

---

**Four Falsehoods (四物)**

Worthy of lament: chess, calligraphy, music, painting,
Empty pleasures to delight the eye and soothe the heart.
Within, these numinous things are scorned,
How can they ever grasp life’s true meaning?
Only I shake my head, unmoved,
With fate, I sift out the nameless.
On the path of eternal life, perfection is proven,
Beyond the void, spirit-light subtly glows.

---

**Four Falsehoods (四景)**

Worthy of lament: wind, flowers, snow, moon,
The world’s affections cling to these.
Pursuing joy and admiration, when will it cease?
They fail to see the yin’s just reward.
Only I shake my head, unmoved,
Searching for mysteries profound.
Luminous, the cause is revealed,
Precisely my family’s inherent grace.

---

**Four Falsehoods (四渎)**

Worthy of lament: Yangtze, Yellow, Huai, and Ji rivers,
Endless currents deceive the foolish.
Floods and waves meet the sky’s paths,
Only flowing from west to east.
Only I shake my head, unmoved,
Rolling jade nectar, precious essence.
Three fields irrigated, forming pearls,
Seven treasures’ peak—there I reside.

---

**Four Falsehoods (四苦)**

Worthy of lament: birth, old age, sickness, death,
The world’s great afflictions, vast and dire.
Alas, the bitter and the sour only deepen,
How can one escape this fate?
Only I shake my head, unmoved,
Even now, I’ll grant them this.
Within the jade flowers’ cluster, I behold the precious science,
Five-colored clouds—there I sit, unshaken.

**Refining the Elixir**

Split and refined into purple rays of gold,
A thousand flowers bloom in myriad brocades.
Drink the clear light—smooth yet spicy,
Feast on fruit—soft, fragrant, and sweet.
Two methods daily refined and added,
Eight flavors given at their proper time.

Stroll the six streets with careless ease,
Seek the seven treasures in adorned splendor.
Three fields turn ninefold like silver rabbits,
One essence, solitary and verified.

Humans must cultivate with fierce resolve,
My heart cleansed—now nothing remains.
Do not waste vital strength in vain exertion,
Let the true and pure gradually emerge.

White snow transforms into a radiant maiden,
Yellow buds nurture the infant within.
Two signs—who can comprehend?
Awakening reveals it clearly.

Drink the clear light—smooth yet spicy,
Feast on meat—soft, fragrant, and sweet.
The world’s delusions know no end,
Each faces perilous paths ahead.
Only I, awakened, stand apart,
Leaving only regret behind.

Tenfold precepts refined, ever stricter,
No trace of *táng* remains to be refined.
Awakening reveals noble descendants,
Seizing robes and seizing feasts alike.

Laughing, rejoicing, grieving, resenting—like roaring wolves and tigers,
Yet they dwell not with me in chaos.
Turn back, and I bear you in my green embrace.
Let the cloud-steps guide you to the Three Teachings of Mao.

---

**Song of the Incense Offering (行香子)**

**First Watch—Water Phase Incense**
The drum first sounds—water’s virtue ascends.
Behold the tortoise, auspicious on the waves.
Full breath, eyes dazzlingly clear,
Diving the pure tide, riding the limpid waves,
Hidden yet the river’s form.
Black mist swirls, filling the skin-bag.
Sealed tight, yet drifting upward.
Harmonizing above and below, flowing at the edges.
Then it becomes mist, forming a canopy,
Accumulating as frost.

**Second Watch—Metal Phase Incense**
The second watch begins—gold’s virtue ascends.
The tiger cub ascends, the infant prince sits.
A white blade hangs at his waist, a green steel rod in hand.
He drives away a hundred demons,
Slays a thousand, dooms ten thousand.
Net of forests spreads wide, silver rays emitted.
The Dipper’s handle aligns, the Azure Dragon’s star ascends.
In the southwest’s place, fragrant virtue revealed.
Good roots bloom, kind roots unfold, auspicious roots flourish.

**Third Watch—Fire Phase Incense**
The third watch begins—fire’s virtue ascends.
The moon’s first phase, illuminating the heart-king.
Scarlet and radiant, dazzling and resplendent.
The original true birth, the enlightened spirit, the supreme true guide.
Threefold balance, one path of ease.
Gazing at the azure sky, auspicious mists unfurl.
Spread horizontally and vertically, encompassing round and square.
Early he plays with the jade ring,
Holding the jade tablet, grasping the jade blade.

**Fourth Watch—Wood Phase Incense**
The fourth watch begins—wood’s virtue ascends.
The Azure Dragon ascends, a graceful maiden sits.
Her breath emits crimson qi, her robe is scarlet.
She wears jade flowers, feasts on jade petals,
Drinks jade nectar.
Coming and going in harmonious delight,
Yin and yang reversed.
The *Mao* stem opens, the sun’s brilliance shines.
The great pearl dims, the luminous flame passes through the Hall of Light.

**Fifth Watch—Earth Phase Incine**
The fifth watch completes—earth’s virtue ascends.
It gathers the four symbols within itself.
Now fully revealed, centered in the middle.
White returns to green, red to black—none to yellow.
Vacuity proven, then it flees from Kunlun’s peak.
The Golden Boy arrives, secret teachings proclaimed.
The Heavenly Sovereign decrees, granting wind’s madness.
Ever in leisure, ever serene, ever cool.

---

**Self-Composed Verse**
There was a King San, wind-mad and deranged.
Abandoning honor, begging first for alms.
Mountains of kindness, seas of love—all fiercely discarded.
No flowers planted, no medicines brewed, no fields tilled.
Fallen yet obsessed, sleeping wherever he lands.
Awakening to coolness, boundless realms unfold.
Penglai’s path secure, each step in cloud and sky.
True joy within truth, truth within delight, delight within mystery.

---

**To a Disciple**
Again you seek new verses, no hidden heads to write.
Plainly stated, the reason revealed:
Gentlemen unenlightened, yet still they seek.
Lost in worldly affairs, when will it cease?
Awaken to the mystic principle, grasp the method of cultivation.
After the elixir’s completion, essence and spirit refined.
The path ahead is steady—Sanzu Islands, Ten Thousand Isles.
Turn back early, and we shall journey together.
If you wish to cultivate, follow this path:
True compassion, boundless wisdom.
Honor parents above, cherish children below.
When jade flowers bloom, their petals drift,
Drinking jade nectar.
Building a golden garden, erecting a jade hall.
This Red Youth ever burns incense in his heart.
His voice resounds, his nature chimes.
Thus attaining cool clarity, pure purity, serene coolness.

To drink the fragrant elixir, spit out all cloying thickness.
With the Flower Pool’s waters, divine essence combined,
Irrigating east and west, refining above and below.
Then the stars appear, the bright moon, the radiant sun.
Gradually entering harmony, only then does sweetness reveal.
The precious vessel forms—no need for pounding and refining.
In leisure, stillness deepens, tranquility embraces calm.
Dwelling in clear skies, beyond all things, atop the mountain’s peak.

**Obtaining the Dao**
Obtaining the Dao, obtaining the Dao—
Naturally hidden in the jade cave’s cloud-palace.
The jade precepts and spirit symbols refresh the pure qi,
The golden elixir’s medicine outshines silk robes.
Not like worldly men, light and frivolous,
Boasting of gold and silver in their chests.
My treasure, the Three Fields ever turning,
My family’s one essence, never in alarm.

January’s cold retreats gradually,
Nine-petaled spirit flowers bloom eastward.
When jade nectar flows, it benefits the vital breath,
When the precious herb is gathered, life is reborn.
Nurturing the Double-Qing’s radiant faces,
Peach-blossom cheeks smile with jade hairpins.
The seven spirits and three corpses depart with the winter solstice,
The five directions and nine turns arrive with spring.

February knows the water’s harmony,
Wind stirs the wood virtue naturally.
*Wuwu* transforms, giving birth to the inner maiden,
*Yiyi* smiles, killing the moon’s fair one.
Bright and clear, the river of the world—
I turn back, emerging from the high slope.
Thirty-six thousand deities gather,
Twelve-layered towers, ten thousand streams of essence.

---

Three months, Qingming’s clarity banishes all smoke,
A hundred flowers bloom radiant beneath the sun’s embrace.
Maiden Maqia gathers by the fresh fire’s glow,
Infant children play by the old pond’s edge.
A precious mirror hangs before my chest,
Old and young unite—auspicious bonds take root.
The Vermilion Bird ascends on clouds, distinguished among all,
The Azure Dragon rides the mist, achieving lofty ascent.

Four months, the Vermilion’s harmonious qi clears,
The heart’s seven treasures bloom ever more distinct.
When you understand, speak alone to yourself,
Do not covet the cries of a hundred birds, O Sage.
Flames stretch slender, gradually taking form,
From this point, all ten thousand trees earn their noble names.
Among the Ten Celestial Stems, I alone advance,
Within the Five Phases’ palaces, I lead the way.

Five months, the sun’s fervent qi thrives,
Now is the time to sit upright and question Nan Hua.
This one cannot praise the Liver-Wood’s excess,
That person favors planting the Heart’s flower.
All vexations vanish—no distant sighs or lamentations,
At noon’s zenith, I stand unyielding, never askew.
The Jade Hare passes, adding to the white snow,
The Golden Rooster appears, spouting yellow sprouts.

Six months, Pure Yang fully enters the domain of the Recluse,
Yin demons are driven back from the streets.
Ren-Gui’s Northern Waters nourish the Kidney’s essence,
Bing-Ding’s Southern Peak kindles the true incense.
Ghosts and fiends, all busied in their schemes,
The assembled horde cannot muster defense.
After the hour of Zi, days grow short—
Before Chen, nights stretch long.

Seven months, the sea’s depth at Geng-Xin,
A single wheel of moonlight governs the celestial heart.
When rice is cooked, know the fire must be fed,
When garments are made, the thread must follow the needle.
Crafting the Seven Treasures of Non-Action,
I command today’s essence to endure until now.
When the White Tiger roars, I seize it often,
Where the Black Tortoise treads, I turn to seek it.

Eight months, the pure dew of clear autumn,
All people at ease, nurturing their true bodies.
Obscure and distant, guests beyond the clouds,
Dim and silent, those who dwell within the moon.
Though dwelling in dust, I am unstained by it,
Nor do I harbor joy, anger, or wrath.
Having attained effortless ease, my body gleams smooth,
Naturally parting and gathering, shedding old skin.

Nine months, the crisp qi of the azure sky ascends,
Layered towers descend with a shower’s gentle rain.
The Red Dragon stirs the sea in true freedom,
Wooden Horses gallop with the wind—never empty.
Each strike in the dust forges my waist,
A six-chun robe hangs, surpassing crimson decay.
Drunk, I sprawl upon the green brocade couch,
Awake, I pluck the jade herb’s tender shoots.

Ten months, the red frost returns, ever clearer,
The Yellow Mother half-submerges in the deep abyss.
When the Celestial Stem is exhausted, only I remain vigorous,
Reborn with divine qi—who else could hear?
The warp must come before the weft,
Only then can the patterned silks be woven.
When the Fire phase departs, red peonies bloom,
When the Water phase descends, rain pours in torrents.

Eleven months, the stern wind wields its might,
The moon’s jade flees, the sun’s gold takes flight.
Binding the Three Threes into treasures,
Donning the Six Sixes’ six-chun robe.
Riding the Phoenix, clutching the Mandarin Duck, crossing mist to return,
Descending from heaven’s decree—no defiance.
With three thousand karmic ties fulfilled, all is exhausted,
Eight hundred deeds completed, dust is rare.

Twelve months, the tapestry of fortune is complete,
The four seasons’ branches and leaves wither not.
See how fire draws water within,
Naturally, water encases the furnace’s glow.
Dragon, Tiger, Tortoise, and Serpent align in breath,
All bones filled, standing in an instant.
One luminous pearl descends three times,
Three evils vanish, all at once.
Having obtained the sacred talisman, all matters are at rest,
A hundred grievances retreat—let others fret.
Drink the elixir to fill my belly’s depths,
Pour the golden marrow to crown my head.
All for the Ten Causes that led to this path,
Maqia and the infant dwell in intricate bonds.
Teach me to grasp the three straight blades,
Ask the Sage to recognize the single curved hook.
The crimson window’s distant five thousand words,
Two hundred characters—
Two kinds of hidden scriptures,
Divine and marvelous deeds.
Within the numinous, I perceive the profound,
Piercing the mystery, refining the gold elixir.
Obtaining the incandescent, all duality ceases.
In boundless ease, my vision unfolds,
Ascending beyond, forever fulfilled.
Together with the red clouds, I return with the rainbow’s hue,
Enveloped in auspicious omens.
At the fifth watch, the first watch begins,
The drum’s voice echoes—foolish and raw.

The hammer strikes—
monkey-mind and wild horses tamed.
Gently, gently—
each chime rings clear,
all at once subdued.

Ten thousand forms hang voidly suspended.
Flames blaze divine radiance,
incandescent, effulgent.
Bright light pierces
the Palace of the Precious Bottle—
the maiden blooms in tender grace.

At the second watch, the drum’s rhythm steadies,
evenly striking of its own accord.
Tiger and dragon shift in exchange,
qi, spirit, and essence
each dwelling in the Elixir Chamber—
no disorder remains.

Piercing through the layered towers,
this jade nectar, this ambrosial brew,
flows back and forth in irrigation.
Now must it
nurture forth the golden sprout,
gradually taking form in splendor.

At the third watch, the drum’s tone resounds true,
its resonant notes turning luminous.
Within, the clamor reveals the numinous root,
harmonizing with the Sage’s Dao and virtue.
Slowly circling the swift path,
the Silver Arrow’s message is strung into elegant verse.
With the arrow’s own tip—
its crimson core—
revealed in utter stillness, pure and clear.

At the fourth watch, the drum’s voice sharpens,
suddenly vibrating—
heavenly blossoms scatter.
Before me stands the True Person,
crowned with stars, draped in moon’s mantle.
This marvelous mystery brings auspicious fortune.
Gazing at the Dipper’s ladle star,
pointing true to the southwest.
Behold—
the jade blossoms gleam,
weaving auspicious omens.

At the fifth watch’s close, the drum grows leisurely,
stirred by that Person into inversion.
From the golden dish emerges the spirit-pearl,
casting myriad rays of crimson light.
Deep, dark, and truly wondrous.
From here, the path reconnects—
the primordial treasure.
Now, where shall it return?
Dwelling in the Ten Isles, the Three Isles.

*Rain of Dews* (玉楼春)
East’s *jia-yi* stems sprout green—
timely, as the seasons decree.
South Yang’s crimson flames blaze forth,
now fierce, dense, and thick.
West winds gold, rustling crisp,
brisk and drifting free.
North’s chill congeals in stern severity,
forming ice—auspicious, fortunate.

Guard the liver’s core, the lungs, the kidneys—
four gates open, luminous, all as one.
The Elixir’s axle stands beyond the void,
radiant, five lights shining forth.
Piercing the azure heights,
claiming only boundless ease, serene repose.
At this juncture, stillness is the way—
endless, unbroken, complete.

---
*From the Complete Works of Zhongyang Chongyangzi Wang Zhe, Volume 8*
#1 *This tune should be "Yulou Chun" (玉楼春).*
*Volume 9*

---

*Lyrics of the Song: The Clear and Awake Song*
The Dao of *Zhengyang* (正陽) is the lineage’s root,
*Pure Yang* (純陽) of Tang as my teacher.
*Yan Guo Hai Chan* (燕國海蟾) as my elder guide,
*Zhongnan Chongyangzi* (終南重陽) gathers disciples.

As disciples, we take refuge here,
Serving and honoring three masters, their sacred essence united.
Move, and the Four Spirits (四靈) radiant in divine hues coalesce;
Still, and the Ten Thousand Ways (萬道) shine with jade-like brilliance.

Attain boundless ease (逍遥),
True freedom (真自在),
Where the *Qingxu* (清虚) and *Xiaoxi* (消息) ever harmonize.

From the *Yuanchu* (元初) this cause began,
Since the beginningless *jie* (劫), no obstacle stands.
To call forth immortals (神仙),
Vague and mysterious, silent before.

Why not treasure this marvel as marvelous?
What else could be deemed profound?
By nature, the *Jing* (精) flows clear,
Thus enlightenment dawns—no need for talk or cultivation.

Why ponder arcane mysteries?
Why seek hidden formulas?
No increase, no decrease,
No birth, no death—no rising or falling.

Forever as companion to wind and moon,
Eternally with clouds and mists entwined.

*Song of the Bamboo Staff* (竹杖歌)
A single bamboo staff—*Wuzhuo* (無著) in name,
Each node glows with resplendent light.
Noble is its hollow core, straight and upright,
Its sheath encased with Elixir’s essence.

Unshaken, unmoved—ever at ease,
Adapting to all things with effortless grace.
Seeking friends upon the sea’s vast expanse,
Who can truly teach me refuge?

Last night in dreams I saw the *Qiu* (虬),
Within them four times leaping with vigor.
Staff raised once, foot stepped once,
A silver thread ascended from the crown.

Furrowed brows revealed, spirit invigorated,
A luminous pearl emitted, radiant and bright.
Joyous, plucked from the azure heights,
The clouds unbroken, keeping their crimson promise.

*Song of the Mysterious* (窈窈歌)
All seek only life’s embrace,
Yet *Feng* (風) demands but death.
Life means no fixed abode,
Death means a resting place.

No attachment to flesh, fat, or sinew,
No clinging to bone, marrow, or essence.
What need for brows, hair, or beard?
What need for tongue, teeth, or lips?

Why use feet, hands, or head?
Why eyes, nose, or ears?
Small intestines churn water,
Large intestines refine grain.
Water and grain—so vague,
Day and night, when shall they cease?

Pierce the illusion’s false design,
Distinguish clearly what is real.
Other dualities merge into unity,
Yet the Dao stands ever distinct.

This one here, that one there,
When you meet it, drink the *Qingliang* (清凉) water.
Only when *Zhengchunyang* (正純陽) is attained,
Shall you be called *Chongyangzi* (重陽子).

*Song of the Primordial* (元元歌)
Though they be father, though they be mother,
The bond of flesh—no words to utter.
Forged in time, yet now I bear their ancient weight.
I am not son, nor daughter,
Nor bound by marital ties.
All are foes, all are debts to settle,
Better to avoid entanglement than suffer.

Awakened, I comprehend,
Awakened, I am whole.
Summoning the *Qingjing* (清靜) Master from ages past,
To see the *Linglong* (玲瓏) hall of perfect clarity,
Open the true gate of uprightness.

Thus know the lineage, know the root,
Clear and awake, returning to the *Zifu* (紫府).
In vain the phoenix consorts with the *Beihai* (北海) tortoise,
The dragon’s scales mock the *Xishan* (西山) tiger.

Wield the *Lingdao* (靈刀),
Brandish the *Huifu* (慧斧),
Splitting the treasures of *Kunlun* (昆仑).
Crowns of jade, pearls without end,
Robes of endless splendor, gold-threaded and bright.

Primordial this, primordial that—
The light returns, revealing the Twenty-Five (五五不離二十五).
Hold fast to this path, cultivate thus,
Your name already inscribed in the *Changsheng* (長生) register.

*Song of Attainment* (得得歌)
Yin transforms to Yang—only this is true.
Ice pierces fire, yet only thus is it.
With fate, I’ve sought the Dao in past and present,
Without beginning, yet what could I call?

Call what? Summon immortals,
Vague and mysterious—no years to recall.
Meeting the *Liangyin* (良因) of Five *Jie* (劫) lineage,
Together we enter the *Daluo* (大羅) realm.

*Daluo* (大羅) realm—where marvels unfold,
Unleashing brilliance for but a moment’s span.
A single grain, plentiful as silk,
A perfect light, eternal in its glow.

Eternal, it becomes divine,
Here in *Qingliang* (清凉), beyond sight or sound.
Why need incense’s heavy fragrance?
Why boast of jingling ornaments?

Their chimes fade, their echoes cease,
Yet new splendor rises, more transcendent.
Naturally, a luminous pearl within,
Reflecting the moon beyond the heavens.

Moon beyond the heavens—
Riding the *Chan* (蟾) wheel’s course,
How could this clarity ever be priceless?

*Zhengyi* (正一) erases all traces of birth and death,
Upright and firm, the profound cause revealed.
Profound cause, true secret—
Never bound by anger, joy, or delight.

Empty space ascends to the clear void,
Words spoken yet none truly said.
None truly said, yet ever more luminous,
In this song, the Dao’s *Tang* (堂) manifests.

Eons unbroken, new elegance unfolds,
From now on, this name spreads wide.

*Song of the Clear and Awake* (惺惺歌)
Why cling to the Four Great (四大)?
Who then was immortal in that age?
Better to perfect the *Yazheng* (雅正) round,
Than feign unity for false cause.

Crimson reborn, the *Shuangguan* (雙關) treasure,
Pure white unfurled, the *Wuyelian* (五葉蓮) lotus.
First refine the *Jiuzhuan* (九轉),
Then nurture the *Yangtian* (養田) above.

Nurture the Three *Tian* (田),
For steadfast longevity,
The golden-maned lion roars in rhythm.
On the *Duandan* (端午) day, survey the *Xuanyin* (玄陰),
At midnight, divide the luminous day.

Ever consume without end—all things’ essence,
Seize the Three *Guang* (光) with divine art.
Externally, why display brilliance?
Internally, refine the form in myriad ways.

This is the *Yuanchu* (元初),
Now believe this truth exists.
First encounter the *Tachizi* (太赤祖),
Return to see the *Shuzhongzhu* (黍中珠).

Seven *Zhulu* (珠戶) gates open wide,
Six *Dao* (道) silver lights freely unfold.
Gazing upward at the *Baibao* (百寶) hall,
This meeting—truth revealed in person.

This truth—no mistake,
In boundless ease, the Elixir’s essence consumed.
Radiant, resplendent—how clear it is,
Awake and lucid, yet ever effortless.

Praised by the sun in emerald mist,
Before the wind, crimson clouds emerge.
At *Kunlun*’s peak, before the jade summit,
A single lotus flower—our vow.

*Song of the Dao’s Exhortation* (勸道歌)
Cultivate, and branches bloom,
Fail to cultivate, and labor is in vain.

The scriptures never exhaust their meaning,
Incense smoke burns in vain, a hollow show.
With weary heart and labored strength, anxiety grows,
Exhausting body and mind, leaving only pallor and decay.

Without wisdom, you frantically seek the fruit of flawlessness,
Unenlightened, you wander blindly across the bridge of fate.
Others’ teachings are endlessly recited,
Yet you dare not uphold your own ancestral Dao.

In stillness, evil thrives in demonic realms,
Clinging to the middle, you fall into the net of mundane existence.
Faithfully holding talismans and elixirs—how proper!
Yet you let food and clothing dictate your true needs.

You boast of emptiness and cold detachment,
Exalting grandeur and dazzling display.
Winds, flowers, snow, and moon—scenes of sorrow,
Alcohol, lust, wealth, and arrogance—roots of bondage.

The gate of affliction opens as you speak of awakening,
The path of contention unfolds as you preach liberation.
Morning and evening, coughs and throat ailments drain you,
Midday practices scatter like empty wind.

All these methods are useless—abandon them now.
From this day on, heed only these words.

Let true function arise naturally in serene stillness,
Trust in compassion to transcend all bounds.
Silent and tranquil, purity shines forth,
In the void’s embrace, darkness harmonizes.

Dragons and tigers must not wander the Three Realms,
Infants and maidens must not dance in vain display.
Mighty roots respond to the strike,
Lonely spirits play their bamboo flutes.

The Two Forces unite like clay molded,
The Five Desires abandoned like carved wood.
Seize the true sound echoing in emptiness,
Silence the false roars of your nature.

Two maidens cast into the gold mine,
Two boys enter the jade gourd.
Break off the wood’s tip for repeated refining,
Then open the spring’s waters for repeated rinsing.

Graceful hues defy all adornment,
Clustered forms resist all description.
Their appearance dazzles the eye,
Their radiance shines like jade and pearl.

Returned to the Dao’s hall, they earn their noble name,
Allowed only in our gate to be called *A-Jiao*.

*Obtain, obtain, obtain*—
Free to compose poetry, music, and song.

**Song of Self-Lamentation**
Ah, in my youth, my parents spared no care,
Ever thinking of filial devotion, I strove with all my might.
Yet how could I ever repay such boundless love?
Only shallow attachments accumulate in vain.

Now I refuse such weary labor,
Content in poverty and leisure, selling nothing but high truth.
Delighted in boundless ease, I nap at noon in blissful repose.
The foolish do not grasp my family’s intent,
Night and day, they scheme in vain.

Four clinging obsessions consume them—
Alcohol, lust, wealth, and arrogance.
Better to let the *Harmful Wind* strike them down,
Free from worry, far from sorrow.

Clouds and waters, green mountains await my joyous roaming,
I wish to return to the Three Isles, the Ten Directions.

Escape the mundane cage,
Enter the jade cavern—
Cease this false body’s empty play.
Then monkeys and horses will all return to nothing,
And only the bright moon remains in use.

**Secret Song of the Dao**
*Sword-Stalactite, Sword-Stalactite*—how fine!
How few can pierce the veil of delusion.
Even if you claim enlightenment, where shall you go?
How shall you bind yourself, how carry yourself?

This *Sword-Stalactite*—
It can drink, too,
Washing away the tenfold brocade within.
Ten thousand petals, a thousand flowers, ever renewed,
Five directions’ hues, each with its own rank.

The *White-Transcending Sword-Stalactite*—
Round and bright,
Emitting its own luminous light.
Dazzling yet unmatched,
Even surpassing the Purple-Gold Elixir.

This *Sword-Stalactite*—
Its blade is sharp,
Unbroken through countless kalpas.
The wise see its radiant wisdom,
The foolish grow only more confused.

This *Sword-Stalactite*—
Truly steel,
Floating in space, it emits its own light.
Only the *Harmful Wind* dares to touch it,
And even then, its essence remains pristine and cool.

This *Sword-Stalactite*—
Ancient and boundless,
Neither yin nor yang, neither earth nor dust.
Just a *lixiangluo*—
From *lixiangluo* comes the lineage’s origin.

**Song of Stability**
Cultivate, and branches bloom anew,
Yet do not chase the light winds—trust in stillness.
Ever bathed in dew and rain, it thrives in emerald green,
Soft and yielding, it fears no frost nor snow’s decay.
Thus does vitality flourish, qi harmonized.
Do not rely on scattered pills for virtue’s path,
Nor cling to talismans for transcendence’s hope.

Ancestral teachings must be penetrated,
Your own Dao must be firmly upheld.
External scenes must not intrude, external affairs must cease,
Search within for the incense of true essence.

Graceful maidens cast into the gold mine,
Handsome youths enter the jade gourd.
One plants a treasure tree in the ore,
The other nurtures the fungus in the vessel.
Their union yields three rare virtues,
Their meeting dances the Six *Mei*.

Ten slender fingers strike the drum,
Seven gates open to blow the flute.
Through raging flames they advance,
On surging waves they float.

The path of true awakening cleanses all filth,
The road of perfect fulfillment shines beyond dust.
Crimson clouds enfold the celestial blue,
Emerald mists spiral in the azure void.

Mysterious and profound, unobstructed,
Awake and lucid, forever unbound.

**Song of Boundless Ease**
*Simplified sounds, swift sounds*—
Abandon wife, forsake child, sever all ties.
Past affections—no need to lament,
The *Harmful Wind* obscures no light.
Ghostly messengers of *Dian* have turned back,
Your name erased from the Black Register’s rolls.

Speak with your mouth, act with your heart,
The path to Penglai is secure—eternal life awaits.

**Song of Profound Profoundness**
*Wūzhuō Peak* stands with its ten-thousand-foot staff,
At its tip, a child plays in joyous abandon.
Wrapped in clear winds, he leaps in wild delight,
Before the bright moon, he boasts of his skill.

Again and again, he plucks the *màtuó* elixir,
Frequently tossing the coral cauldron.
The elixir and cauldron slip—
Effort wasted in vain.

Parting the silver waves, he gazes at the jade shore,
And there he sees the golden tortoise in the jade vessel.
Qi glows like amber, eyes shine like pearls.
The child descends the staff to claim the pearl in vow,
Not letting the *Lí Dragon* hide it below,
Nor casting it into the clouds—he hurls it to the Azure Void.

Obscure and distant, time forgotten,
From this moment, he knows the effortless way.

**Song of the Reached**
Cultivate with wisdom, devise grand strategies,
Search and arrange with broad intent.
The Eight-Eight Maiden steadies her hands,
The Six-Li Gentleman applies his effort.

**Song of the Alchemical Arts**

Fair and ruddy, he knows the gold mine’s secret,
Black and lithe, he seeks the jade vessel’s treasure.
He drinks and pours himself—awake, then drunk,
To song and dance he yields, his mirth unshaken.
He smashes open the *Yáng Path* to spread the sacred gem,
Through the *Yīn Pass* he emerges, the *lùliú* wheel in hand.
Ascending *Kūn Mountain*, he presents a slice of jade,
Returning to the great sea, he plays with pearls so bright.
With every touch, he grasps the Dao’s profound essence,
Wherever he wanders, he finds paths smooth and clear.
His head brims with *Lí Dragon*’s hidden wonders,
His feet overflow with *Yáo Flower*—seizing emptiness with ease.
He teaches his face to move with boundless grace,
Nurturing his roots through breath, the art of *xīhū*.
At *Zhōu Chéng*’s dawn, the true awakening comes,
The *Dìduān*’s end reveals the great *Dà Chéngsū*.
Alone, he shines—no difference in his radiance,
Five paths’ light unified, none can surpass his splendor.
Like the *Huánghuā* poet’s single gain,
Or *Qiáo*’s red crow transforming into twin ducks.
The *Sān Dǎo* islands call him to their pure retreat,
The *Shí Zhōu* lands unite beneath his guiding step.
In stillness, he asks the clouds’ crossroads—only the *Dòngdá* knows,
Adrift and free, he joins the ranks of immortal paths.

---

**Song of the Gift to a Friend**

Who can summon the sea’s refined *qi*?
Only *Zōu Zhèngdào* in the *Nínghǎi* ranks.
Gold waves and silver tides return to their source,
To welcome *Pénglái Island*—now revealed in sight.
*Pénglái Island*, where is it found?
Obscure and distant, touching the boundless sky.
Who shares this boundless ease with me?
Only you, my friend, dwell in this cool, pure place.
This cool, pure place—truly it exists,
Where the *Qīngtóng* child presents the elixir of long life.
Let it permeate the four seasons’ spring,
A single pearl’s light roars like thunder.
Its light roars like thunder—crimson clouds it spews,
Blanketing the clear sky with marvelous splendor.
Descending the spirit waves, it stirs not a ripple,
Soaring to the celestial heights, its expanse knows no end.
Its expanse knows no end—truly it is seen,
Mysteries profound, revealed in their play.
The cloud-car enters the Azure Void once more,
On *Dàluó*’s heights, his alchemy takes form.
His alchemy takes form—*yuán gēn* obtained,
The gate of *wúwéi*’s great Dao now stands revealed.
May you turn back and grasp this truth,
Ascend the path of no leakage, beyond all speech.

---

**Song of the Iron Cauldron**

*Iron Cauldron Song*, *Iron Cauldron Song*,
From its first forging, following the golden method.
Its belly hollow, yielding wonders profound,
Who knows its secrets, its subtle messages?
*Iron Cauldron* formed, *Iron Cauldron* formed,
Frequently filled with jade nectar, brimming.
When fire refines it, snow-waves scatter,
When water clears it, blessings of peace ascend.
*Iron Cauldron* carried, *Iron Cauldron* carried,
Its ringing strikes the deaf, dispelling ignorance.
If one would hear its resonant call,
North or south, east or west—all shall know.
*Iron Cauldron* new, *Iron Cauldron* new,
Its inner light and outer glow are kin.
To add to the cauldron, one must rely on *jīnyè*’s tide,
To blend and harmonize, all depends on *qi* and spirit’s might.
*Iron Cauldron* wide, *Iron Cauldron* wide,
Where *qi* surges, snow drifts in endless tide.
