Only then does the *Hǔlóng* coil in still embrace,
Wrapping lead and mercury tight on its head.
*Iron Cauldron* deep, *Iron Cauldron* deep,
No dust or defilement can breach its keep.
Its use is fire that burns the wood above,
Its practice, gold refined within the water’s love.
*Iron Cauldron*’s light, *Iron Cauldron*’s light,
Three lights shine—auspicious signs take flight.
Each time it’s used, transformations arise,
When left to rest, it cools with tranquil skies.
*Iron Cauldron* burned, *Iron Cauldron* burned,
Last night, today, and the morn to come.
By seasonal rule, the furnace is set,
With time, the jade mushrooms grow.
*Iron Cauldron*’s power, *Iron Cauldron*’s power,
Within it, the *qi* swells like a stormy tower.
Obscure and distant, the wind is its friend,
Drowsy and silent, the moon its companion.

---

**West River Moon (Alchemical Reflections)**

Worthy of praise—this southwest land’s ease,
Burning firewood, all of it true silver.
Within the flames, two forms are seared apart,
Half of them blooming as gold flowers.
Recognizing the *jīnxīng*’s weight with precision,
At once, the merit is paid in full.
*West River Moon* wraps the spirit’s essence,
Revealing the *língtóng*’s true seal.
Worthy of praise—the water’s single flow,
Must rely on a thousand cauldron additions.
From the sea’s heart, a ten-thousand-fathom pole sways firm,
After stillness, the mushrooms sprout.
Understanding the labor, swift and sure,
One finds joy in ease, immersed in bliss.
*West River Moon* wraps the mushrooms’ tender shoots,
Carrying them to the *Shí Zhōu* and *Sān Dǎo*.
Worthy of praise—leaving home’s threshold,
Must neighbor the *Jiǎdì Gēngtú*’s sacred path.
In darkness, he claps his hands, calling in laughter,
Slowly, they blend in perfect harmony.
Locking the golden gate, the *Bái Yáng* teams form pearls,
*West River Moon* wraps the lone jade hare,
Illuminating the path of eternal life.
Worthy of praise—the clouds rise from his crown,
Soaring aloft, where wonders abound.
Mysteries profound all radiate in light,
Within the cauldron, silver waves ignite.
Ashamed to refine, he turns to gold’s face,
*Yáo Flower* blooms, dancing in grace.
*West River Moon* wraps the drink of jade nectar,
A thousand paths of crimson clouds part.
Worthy of praise—the wood and gold’s dual form,
*Jiǎfū Gēngfù* smile with joy.
Their laughter’s sweetness echoes in flowing streams,
A clear current emerges from the ravine.
Nourishing the *huángyá*’s endless growth,
They teach white snow to cycle in rebirth.
*West River Moon* wraps my climb,
Each step, the silver hare watches my path.
Worthy of praise—the day’s swift change,
Frequently wiping the spirit’s hall.
A single light dispels all dust,
Its brilliance pierces both inside and out.
Claiming adrift ease, his flute scatters cold plums,
*West River Moon* wraps the *guìhuā*’s bloom,
Its fragrance draws the clean winds to meet.
Worthy of praise—the white lotus unfurls,
Three chariots harnessed to the golden ox.
Naturally, its red splendor covers the peaks,
Not forged by labor, but by spirit’s light.
Guarded by the refined glow’s power,
The elixir’s done—its radiance lights the divine boat.
*West River Moon* wraps the sight of *Yíngzhōu*,
A single strike of the immortal song resounds.
Worthy of praise—this melody’s grace,
Moved by the *Shífù*’s stone flute’s embrace.
On mountain peaks, they speak of water’s frequent rain,
In ocean depths, they whisper of fire’s flame.
When the round brilliance shines true,
The pure wind spreads, its gusts unrivaled.
*West River Moon* wraps the eating of mushrooms’ taste,
Their flavors clear—now understood.
Worthy of praise—this single true nature,
Gained with laughter, the wise now stumble.
No incense burned, no scriptures read,
This path alone leads swift and speed.

「便把那人喝定，今朝说与叮咛。
*Now that the man is thoroughly awakened, today I speak and admonish him.*

西江月裹最分明，
*The West River Moon’s embrace reveals clarity most bright,*
堪用家风清莹。
*Worthy to employ the family’s pure and luminous *qi*.*

堪叹青霄碧汉，
*Worthy of praise—the azure sky and verdant heavens,*
高空景致尤宽。
*Their vast expanse and boundless vistas are most broad.*

今朝清爽有余欢，
*Today’s clarity and freshness bring abundant joy,*
拈出我家公案。
*I present my family’s *gōng’àn*—public truths.*

方显平生手段，
*Now I reveal my lifelong skill,*
腾身便入云端。
*And rise—entering the clouds’ heights.*

西江月裹跨祥鸾，
*Within the West River Moon’s embrace, astride the auspicious *luán*—phoenix,*
直上虚无仙馆。
*Ascend to the void’s immortal halls.*

悟真歌
*Ode to the Awakened Truth*

余当九岁方省事，
*At nine years old, I first understood the Way’s meaning.*
祖父享年八十二。
*The Grandfather lived to eighty-two.*

二十三上荣华日，
*At twenty-three, on the day of my prosperity,*
伯父享年七十七。
*The Uncle lived to seventy-seven.*

三十三上觉婪耽，
*At thirty-three, I indulged in the delusion of awakening,*
慈父享年七十三。
*The Father lived to seventy-three.*

古今百岁七旬少，
*From ancient times to now, few reach a hundred or seventy years.*
观此递减怎当甘？
*Seeing this gradual decline, how could I bear it gladly?*

三十六上寐中寐，
*At thirty-six, I slept within sleep,*
便要分他兄活计。
*And sought to divide my elder brother’s livelihood.*

豪气冲天恣意情，
*With boundless *qi* and unrestrained passion,*
朝朝日日长波醉。
*I reveled in wine day and night.*

压幼欺人度岁时，
*Oppressing the young, deceiving others, wasting years,*
诬兄骂嫂慢天地。
*Falsely accusing my brother, scolding my sister-in-law, defying heaven and earth.*

不修家业不修身，
*Neither tending my family’s affairs nor cultivating my own nature,*
只恁望他空富贵。
*Only hoping for them to gain empty wealth and rank.*

浮云之财随手过，
*The wealth of transient clouds passed freely through my hands,*
妻男怨恨天来大。
*My wife and son resented me, and the heavens grew vast with their wrath.*

产业卖得三分钱，
*My properties sold for three parts of their worth,*
二分吃着一酒课。
*Two parts consumed in wine and revelry.*

他每衣饮全不知，
*They knew nothing of clothing or sustenance,*
余还酒钱说灾祸。
*Yet I spoke of misfortune in repaying the wine debts.*

四十八上尚争强，
*At forty-eight, I still strove for dominance,*
争奈浑身做察详。
*But my body was already frail and meticulous in its decay.*

忽尔一朝便心破，
*Suddenly, one morning my heart shattered,*
变成风害任风狂。
*And I became a *fēnghài*—one afflicted by wind, surrendering to its wildness.*

不惧人人长耻笑，
*I fear not the endless scorn of others,*
一心恐昧三光照。
*But dread the obscuration of the Three Lights in my mind.*

静虑澄思省己身，
*With tranquil reflection and clear contemplation, I examined my own form,*
悟来便把妻儿掉。
*And upon awakening, I cast aside wife and children.*

好洗面兮好理头，
*I bathed my face and combed my hair,*
从人尚道骋风流。
*Following others, still preaching the Way of unrestrained *qi* and freedom.*

家财荡尽愈无愁，
*Though my family’s wealth was spent entirely, my worries only deepened,*
怕与儿孙作马牛。
*For fear that my descendants would become *mǎniú*—servants of fate.*

五十二上光阴急，
*At fifty-two, time pressed urgently,*
活到七十有几日。
*How many days would I live to seventy?*

前头路险是轮回，
*The path ahead is perilous—*samsara’s* turning wheel,*
旧业难消等闲失。
*Old karmic debts hard to erase, like careless neglect.*

一失人身万劫休，
*Once losing the human form, a million kalpas pass in vain,*
如何能得此中修？
*How could one attain cultivation hereafter?*

须知未老闻强健，
*Know this: before growing old, I heard of vigor and strength,*
弃穴趖坟云水游。
*So I abandoned my dwelling, left my grave, and wandered in clouds and waters.*

云水游兮别有乐，
*Wandering in clouds and waters has its own unique joy,*
无虑无思无做作。
*Free from worries, thoughts, and contrivance.*

一枕清风宿世因，
*A pillow of pure wind—*cause from past lives,*
一轮明月前生约。
*A single wheel of bright moon—*pledge from ages before.*

赠弟子颂
*Ode to the Disciple*

谭仙入道，
*Tan Xian entered the Dao,*
慧刀能举。
*His wisdom-sword raised the Way.*

弃妻割爱，
*He abandoned his wife and severed attachments,*
舍了男女。
*And cast aside male and female.*

却要随余，
*Yet he wished to follow me,*
余应便许。
*And I consented.*

羡公决烈，
*Xian Gong’s resolve was firm,*
羡公显露。
*Xian Gong’s virtue revealed.*

我吐真诚，
*I spoke with true sincerity,*
却有少诉。
*Yet he had slight complaints.*

入道非难，
*Entering the Dao is not easy,*
亦非易做。
*Nor is it simple to accomplish.*

苦中寻闲，
*Within suffering, one seeks leisure,*
闲中没苦。
*Within leisure, suffering vanishes.*

休觅婴姹，
*Cease seeking the *yīngchī*—youthful charm,*
莫搜龙虎。
*And do not hunt for *lónghǔ*—elixir of immortality.*

只要真清，
*Only true purity is sought,*
要识真趣。
*And one must know the true delight.*

绝尽人我，
*Sever all attachments to self and others,*
绝尽思虑。
*And exhaust all deliberation.*

或饥或饱，
*Sometimes hungry, sometimes sated,*
或寒或暑。
*Sometimes cold, sometimes scorched.*

便戴青巾，
*Then I wear the green headband,*
便衣纸布。
*And clothe myself in hemp and paper.*

决要上街，
*I resolve to go to the streets,*
觅钱乞去。
*To beg for coins and depart.*

些小绢帛，
*Some trifling silks and linens,*
些小绵絮。
*Some trifling cotton and floss.*

遮藏微体，
*To cover my humble form,*
长令淡素。
*And forever maintain simplicity.*

三人同行，
*Three men walk together,*
三人同处。
*And dwell in one place.*

常用一心，
*Always employing a single mind,*
不得二慕。
*Without dual attachments.*

只是兄弟，
*Only as brothers,*
并无师父。
*With no master between us.*

惟谈惟笑，
*Only speaking and laughing,*
共歌共舞。
*Together singing and dancing.*

落绝清闲，
*Falling into utter leisure,*
任诗任句。
*At ease with verse and prose.*

如在庖厨，
*As if in the kitchen,*
大家管顾。
*All share in the oversight.*

不可独劳，
*No one labors alone,*
也无独措。
*Nor acts alone.*

自有金乌，
*There is the Golden Rooster,*
自有玉兔。
*And the Jade Rabbit.*

认得真闲，
*Knowing true leisure,*
长生门户。
*Is the gateway to eternal life.*

自在亭颂
*Ode to the *Zìzài* Pavilion*

自在自在真自在，
*True *zìzài*—freedom, freedom, true freedom,*
不论高低及内外。
*Beyond distinctions of high or low, inner or outer.*

照见五蕴即皆空，
*Seeing the Five Aggregates as they truly are—all empty.*
咄了八方无呈碍。
*And dispelling the Eight Directions’ hindrances.*

维摩笑我因何退，
*Weimó laughed at me for why I withdrew,*
我笑维摩尚礼拜。
*And I laughed at Weimó for still bowing in reverence.*

教公认得这害风，
*Let the Master recognize this *fēnghài*—wind affliction,*
大家总赴龙华会。
*And all gather at the Dragon Flower Assembly.*

四果颂
*Ode to the Four Fruits*

果来海角天涯，
*The fruits come from distant lands and seas,*
果应师指希夷。
*As the Master’s pointing directs to the rare.*

果得前生知友，
*The fruits are gained from friends known since past lives,*
果然会我心机。
*And indeed they resonate with my deepest intentions.*

指迷颂
*Ode to the Illusion of Pointing*

无无有有有无端，
*Non-existence without existence—existence without end,*
有有无无有有攒。
*Existence without non-existence—existence in clusters.*

无有有无无有相，
*Non-existence with existence—existence without form,*
有无无有有无看。
*Existence without non-existence—existence without sight.*

剑颂
*Ode to the Sword*

这口剑，
*This sword,*
真有力，
*Truly has power,*
无始劫来人不识。
*Yet since beginningless kalpas, none have known it.*

今朝撞箸害风儿，
*Today, as I strike the chopsticks—*fēnghài’s* child,*
吐出光芒颠倒织。
*It emits radiance and reverses the weave of existence.*

两道明辉只自知，
*Two beams of light are known only to itself,*
三峰顶上呈红赩。
*And on the Three Peaks’ summit, it displays crimson brilliance.*

到斯不肯落凡来，
*Arriving here, it refuses to descend into the mundane,*
样入晴空端又直。
*Yet it enters the clear sky, upright and unyielding.*

传神颂
*Ode to the Transmission of Spirit*

灵昏性昧着凡体，
*The spirit’s dusk and delusion cling to the mortal form,*
自画自描自传起。
*Self-painted, self-drawn, and self-transmitted from the beginning.*

借他俗状做形躯，
*Borrowing their vulgar appearance to construct this body,*
攒聚火风并地水。
*It gathers fire and wind, earth and water.*

阳作骨骸阴作肤，
*The *yáng*—yang force forms the bones,*
*而* 阴 *作肤。*
*And the *yīn*—yin force forms the skin.*

眼耳鼻前安个觜，
*The eyes, ears, and nose are placed before—*zhuì*—a snout.*

四般迷执各夸强，
*The Four Delusions each boast their strength:*
浑身便用肉山垒。
*This body is built like a mountain of flesh.*

我今省悟达玄微，
*Now I awaken and comprehend the profound mysteries,*
却认初真不用你。
*And recognize the original truth—without need of you.*

若还只恁累我神，
*If you still burden my spirit thus,*
扑人坈中教见底。
*You’ll drive me into the *yǐn*—pit of existence, revealing its depths.*

来自何方，
*From whence do you come?*
去由何路，
*By what path do you depart?*
一脚不移，
*With one step unshifted,*
回头即悟。
*Turning back, one awakens.*

假合形躯诚是假，
*The false body is truly false,*
何劳更恁重描画。
*Why labor further in its detailed depiction?*

诸公莫使达人知，
*Let no one reveal this to the enlightened,*
惹得一场大笑话。
*For fear it sparks a grand jest.*」

赠道友
*To a Daoist Friend*

自然消息自然恬，
*The natural *qi* flows, serene and tranquil,*
不论金丹不论仙。
*Beyond concern for elixir or immortality.*

一气养成神愈静，
*With a single breath of *qi*, the spirit grows ever still,*
万金难买日高眠。
*And a million coins cannot purchase the bliss of lofty midday slumber.*

红红火焰三峰秀，
*The crimson flames of the Three Peaks glow bright,*
白白莲花五叶鲜。
*The white lotuses of the Five Petals bloom fresh.*

勘破行功无作用，
*Piercing through the *xínggōng*—cultivation practices,*
於斯便可认玄玄。
*Here one may recognize the profound mysteries.*

四时睡颂
*Ode to the Four Seasons’ Sleep*

子时睡，
*Sleep at the Hour of the Child,*
子时睡，
*Sleep at the Hour of the Child,*
玉绳抨下端严遂。
*The jade *shéng*—pendant of the Daoist priest strikes down, its order complete.*

一轮明月过天庭，
*A single wheel of bright moon passes through the celestial court,*
照破中宵暗昧事。
*Dispelling the obscurity of midnight.*

卯时睡，
*Sleep at the Hour of the Tiger,*
卯时睡，
*Sleep at the Hour of the Tiger,*
缘空直看真嘉致。
*By the void, one gazes straight at the true splendor.*

当中一点皎然灵，
*Within, a single point of luminous spirit,*
莹裹光明精又锐。
*Enveloped in brilliance, sharp and piercing.*»

午时睡，
*Sleep at the Hour of the Horse,*
午时睡，
*Sleep at the Hour of the Horse,*
香烟正撞於炎位。
*The incense smoke strikes the *Yánwèi*—Fiery Abode.*

「自然馥郁任拈拏，
*The Way’s essence naturally fragrant, left to the plucking and releasing—*
透入晴空传不二。
*Penetrating the clear void, conveying the undivided Path.*

酉时睡，
*Sleep at the Hour of the Rooster,*
酉时睡，
*Sleep at the Hour of the Rooster,*
恬然饮尽西江水。
*Serene, one drains the waters of the Western River.*

便令浇溉出风流，
*Thus, one irrigates the flourishing spirit—*
一朵琼花呈玉蕊。
*A single jade blossom reveals its pure essence.*

赠友入道颂
*Ode to a Friend Entering the Dao*

若是要随余去，
*If you wish to follow me away,*
绝尽平生思虑。
*Sever all earthly cares and contemplations.*

心中物物不着，
*The mind clings not to things,*
尘事般般休序。
*All worldly affairs cease in sequence.*

饥后粗细皆餐，
*After hunger, one takes both coarse and fine [food]*
寒来只消纸布。
*When cold comes, only paper and cloth suffice.*

常睡莫起忧愁，
*Ever sleep, never stir with worry,*
如行休生恐怖。
*As one walks, cease all fear.*

不得言是谈非，
*One may not say "yes" or "no,"*
不得辞辛道苦。
*Nor utter "labor" or "hardship."*

长怀平等之心，
*Ever hold the mind of perfect equality,*
人痾须要救护。
*To aid the suffering of others is essential.*

长把假身搜获，
*Ever grasp the false body to search within,*
永将内真正顾。
*And forever turn to the inner True Self.*

直待消尽旧业，
*Only when all past karmic deeds are exhausted,*
万事般般勿做。
*Should one refrain from all worldly actions.*

行功堪可证明，
*The Daoist practice may be proven through its fruits,*
有个真师来度。
*For there is a true teacher to guide.*

四不得颂
*Ode to the Four Impossibilities*

不得受人钦重，
*One may not receive others’ admiration,*
不得教人戏弄。
*Nor provoke others’ mockery.*

不得意马外游，
*The mind’s "horse of desire" may not roam outside,*
不得心猿内动。
*The "monkey of the mind" may not stir within.*

四得颂
*Ode to the Four Attainments*

得汞阴消尽，
*Attaining cinnabar, the shadow dissolves completely,*
得铅阳自团。
*Attaining lead, the luminous essence gathers of itself.*

得命颠倒至，
*Attaining the reversal of life [and death],*
得性见金丹。
*And the nature reveals the elixir.*

玉花会疏
*Essay for the Jade Blossom Assembly*

切以能全呼吸，
*Above all, mastering the complete breath—*
定喘息，
*Steadying the inhalations and exhalations,*
实非难；
*Is indeed no easy feat.*

会养气神，
*To nurture the *qi* and spirit,*
调冲和，
*And harmonize the *chōng*—vital currents,*
应甚易。
*Should be quite simple.*

性凭三曜，
*The nature relies upon the Three Illuminations,*
命变五行，
*The life transforms through the Five Phases.*
出阴阳造化之端，
*Emerging from the origins of yin-yang transformation,*
在清静虚无之上。
*Residing above the realm of tranquility and emptiness.*

要开金蕊，
*To open the golden lotus,*
须种玉花。
*One must first plant the jade blossom.*

馨香吐而透入晴空，
*Fragrance exhales, permeating the clear void,*
明艳显而朗舒碧汉。
*Luminous brilliance reveals, spreading across the azure heavens.*

得自然而轻九转，
*Attaining the natural, one transcends the Nine Rebirths with ease,*
得自然而没七还。
*Attaining the natural, one escapes the Seven Reincarnations.*

自结大丹，
*One’s own elixir is formed,*
自通玄妙。
*And the profound mysteries are self-revealed.*

既为脱壳，
*Having already shed the mortal shell,*
便是登仙。
*One ascends to transcendence.*

願露赤心，
*May one bare the crimson heart,*
請題芳號。
*And request a fragrant Daoist name.*

金莲会诗
*Poem for the Golden Lotus Assembly*

诸公须是助金莲，
*All revered ones must aid the Golden Lotus,*
願出長生分定錢。
*And contribute to the treasury of eternal life.*

逐月四文十六字，
*Each month, four coins and sixteen characters,*
好於二八结良缘。
*To form a harmonious bond at the auspicious Twenty-Eighth.*

長生永结〔金〕莲社，
*Eternal life is forever bound in the Golden Lotus Assembly,*
有始有终无谄诈。
*With beginning and end, yet no flattery or deceit.*

诸公不可半途止，
*All revered ones must not cease halfway,*
直待王风去则罢。
*Only when the *Wángfēng*—Royal Wind departs, may one rest.*

劝君莫恋有中无，
*I urge you not to cling to "having yet not having,"*
无无休失无中有。
*Nor to "not having yet not losing" the "having yet not having."*

有有养出玉花头，
*From "having having," one nurtures the jade blossom’s peak,*
头头结取金莲首。
*And each peak binds to the Golden Lotus’s origin.*

辞世颂
*Ode to Departing the World*

地肺重阳子，
*The *Dìfèi*—Earthly Lung, Master Zhòngyáng,*
呼为王害风。
*Is called the *Wánghài Fēng*—Royal Harmonic Wind.*

来时长日月，
*When it comes, the days and months extend,*
去后任西东。
*When it departs, one follows the west or east.*

作伴云和水，
*It takes the clouds and waters as companions,*
为邻虚与空。
*And the void and emptiness as neighbors.*

一灵真性在，
*The true nature of the One Spirit remains,*
不与众心同。
*Not aligned with the multitude’s minds.*

重阳全真集卷之九竟
*The Ninth Volume of the *Zhòngyáng Quánzhēn*—Complete Perfection of Master Zhòngyáng, ends here.*

重阳全真集卷之十
*The Tenth Volume of the *Zhòngyáng Quánzhēn*—Complete Perfection of Master Zhòngyáng.*

终南山重阳子王哲撰
*Composed by Master Zhòngyáng, Wáng Zhé, of Zhōngnán Mountain.*

诗
*Poem:*

赠王俊
*To Wáng Jùn.*

**Ode to Departing the World**

The Earthly Lung, Master Zhòngyáng,
Is called the Royal Harmonic Wind.
When it comes, the days and months extend,
When it departs, one follows the west or east.
It takes the clouds and waters as companions,
And the void and emptiness as neighbors.
The true nature of the One Spirit remains,
Not aligned with the multitude’s minds.

---

**Poem**

To Wáng Jùn:
*If you halt halfway, wait until the Royal Harmonic Wind departs, then cease.*
Admonish you not to cling to the "having within, lacking without"—
*Without the without, you lose the having within;*
*With the with, you nurture the jade-flower crown,*
*And from each crown, you gather the golden lotus head.*

---

**Poem**

The Royal Harmonic Wind repeatedly visits the Lotus Sect,
For the Three Teachings, only your Daoist discourse is shared.
At this moment, we meet in perfect harmony above and below,
In the midst, our gathering aligns with each’s own west or east.
Know that winter solstice yields the green and white,
And spring equinox reveals the crimson and verdant.
Swiftly, the Three Lights may be grasped if wisdom dawns,
Hastily, the Four Illusions dissolve into emptiness.
A single round and luminous essence suffuses all things,
Yet the myriad forms conceal it utterly.
The awakened nature naturally flows like water in stillness,
The enlightened mind enters the hundred-blooming flowers.
Each illusion shattered still returns to the marvelous,
Each return reveals the ultimate end.
Food and drink merely sate the hunger—two wondrous means,
Before you, the jade-like lingzong stands clear.

To the Daoist Assembly:
*All know that the long and the Dao are neighbors,*
*Seeking the profound and profound, you bind kinship.*
Do not forget the Three Teachings’ logic,
Nor abandon the eternal spring of Complete Perfection.
Nurture the Original Qi to ever fill,
Secure the Spirit Essence to never leak.
The Nineteenfold Radiance as my wish,
Dare I invite you to join in boundless joy?

**On the Celestial Realm:**
*Seizing its true essence, search ends in absolute clarity,*
*Each form dissolved, yet none intrude.*
The Jade Retreat’s depths are naturally serene,
White clouds drift without intent, their comings and goings.
The swelling moon enhances its splendor,
Fine breezes carry melodies of virtue.
With languid gaze, I observe Pan Yue’s prose,
With leisurely touch, I stroke Bo Ya’s zither.
Outside, the flowers and strolling crowds grow still,
Within, the herbs and elixirs gather close.
The Three Fields must return to their supreme treasure,
The One Nature ascends to lofty peaks.
Nurturing the phantom body as bright as light,
Dancing the prenatal sage like wind and song.
Vanished and silent in endless twilight,
Eternal stillness guards the water’s gold within.

**On the Question of Dreams:**
*Capturing the mind-monkey, taming the spirit-god,*
*There is no dream-distress when the true nature is held.*
The tail’s root remains motionless, preserving vital essence,
The kidney’s sea ever replenishes the silver waters of the Primordial.
Internally, this fosters heightened awareness,
Externally, it nourishes the body’s life.
Widely practicing rituals and incantations to save all,
You attain the carefree shore-dweller’s ease.
To Master Wáng:
*Seeking the Dao in practice requires no teacher,*
*Only self-knowledge within the heart.*
In purity, wisdom ever grows,
In seclusion, compassion naturally arises.
Carrying firewood, fetching water—only the sound matters,
Gazing at forms, pondering thoughts—each does as they will.
Reducing food to forget the self is noble generosity,
Embracing joy to take delight is true cultivation.
Healing others with medicine brings supreme merit,
Avoiding wine and meat is most fitting conduct.
Wait until the gate opens to reveal the Host’s nature,
Then follow the fateful thread to its end.

**On Internal Matters:**
*In cultivation’s logic, speak with careful emphasis,*
*Only the heart’s stillness and clarity suffice.*
When the eye’s vision ceases, the dragon rests within,
When the nostril’s block is lifted, the tiger lingers no more.
The tongue retreats from taste, the mind and spirit rejoice,
The ears release sound, the kidney’s waters grow clear.
North and south harmonize as one body,
East and west merge, extinguishing the Three Passions.
Wood and metal vie in the coiled abdomen’s realm,
The prenatal sage follows, moving freely at will.
The Golden Elixir forms at the crown’s apex,
Five radiant lights illuminate the Dao’s rainbow canopy.

**On Drinking and Gambling:**
*The heart drifts in idle amusement, lost in fleeting pleasures,*
*Unrestrained abandon leads to the brink of ruin.*
Do not let drinking sever filial piety,
Nor let gambling disrupt your household.
The Daoist path is best entered with reverence,
The royal law must be followed without extravagance.
Equality in action brings ease,
And you may join me in the misty peaks.

**To the Scholar on Learning:**
*Zài Yǔ’s midday slumber is unbearable to behold,*
*Wasting light and time in sleep and gluttony.*
Diligence in a humble dwelling brings no shame,
In a thatched hall, cultivation seeks no comfort.
Snow reflected through the window brings constant joy,
Head suspended in meditation finds its own delight.
Great ambition need not cling to a single treasure,
Sun Bin’s wisdom suits the study of Ní Kuān.

**To Master Xiǎo Dá:**
*Unlock the original essence, and clarity comes naturally,*
*Release the true light, and all attachments vanish.*
The Three Treasures must converge to perfect awareness,
The One Spirit fears no obstruction in its completion.
Mastering subtle applications requires purity and stillness,
Recognizing the profound depends on clarity and refinement.
Fit to be a carefree guest beyond the clouds,
Treading the path of longevity toward the fore.

**Self-Narrative:**
*Crimson agate hangs in the silent void,*
*Deep stillness and mystery before my eyes.*
With mother-of-pearl, I fortify the elixir chamber,
And with amber, I till the Field of Regeneration.
Four precious treasures securely gathered,
The Three Radiances transmitted with utmost care.
This method, once attained, transcends the empty world,
In the depths of the rainbow, I tread the Golden Lotus.

**On Life and Death:**
*Ever know contentment to roam freely,*
*Do not cling deeply to the fire’s pit.*
The nature above is clear—two paths divide,
Before noon, recognize the Host’s true form.
The One True Essence reveals its luminous structure,
The Seven Orifices breathe the auspicious Qi.
Palming compassion and mercy, you transcend the Dharma-realm,
On the path of cool clarity, you attain eternal life.*

**To a Friend Who Offers Wine:**
*Though the road ascends without my bidding,*
*The mist and clouds summon my nature to awaken.*
Ten thousand miles of clear wind as constant companion,
One wheel of bright moon as ever-present disciple.
Mountains green and waters blue, step by step they guide,
Wine white and barley yellow, turn by turn they beckon.
Tonight’s cup, if taken with intent,
Unleashes the red flame to illuminate the ice-cup’s depths.*

**To a Friend Seeking Quietude:**
*Black clouds disperse, the moon shines ever clearer,*
*Illuminating the dusty world, extinguishing all sentient longing.*
No more afflictions arise when perfect wisdom is held,
No more quarrels remain when the deep pit of duality is crossed.
Above the peaks, a subtle breeze arrives,
Within the heart, I welcome the light snow.
The recluse who faces the wall knows this flavor,
On the carefree path, they attain the round and perfect.

**On Transient Glory:**
*Not clinging to honor and splendor is a virtuous cause,*
*Distant and detached, your vision grows ever new.*

**On the Eight Consciousnesses and Five Gates:**
Eightfold perception penetrates the boundless night—
Fivefold luminosity shines upon eternal spring.
From this, one may transcend the Three Realms,
By this, one may emerge from the Six Dusts with divine grace.
A single golden lotus ascends to the highest realm,
Round and perfect, never to sink into the mire of delusion.

**To a Friend:**
The Dao is wordless, beyond hearing’s reach,
Zen’s boundless openness unites all beings.
Which seated practice can awaken one?
Who discerns the incense’s smoke as it divides?
Seizing the true essence of the Three Lights,
The Four Great Elements dissolve in their tumult.
A radiant cluster shines beyond the void,
Only then does one drift free like white clouds.

**A Friend’s Inquiry:**
Nature’s rhythms unfold in tranquil ease,
No need for elixirs, no need for immortals.
A single breath nurtures the spirit ever purer,
A thousand gold pieces cannot buy the bliss of high slumber.
Crimson flames pierce the three peaks,
White lotuses bloom fresh with five petals.
Piercing through the labor of practice’s path,
Here, one may recognize the profoundest mystery.

**On the Eye:**
Like sunlight, clear as crystal,
Illuminating all, ever vigilant.
Gazing only at the empty spectacle of dust,
Would you read the *Huangting* scriptures within or without?
The pupil steadied cannot see the Dao,
A child sits upright, yet does not perceive form.
If a teacher meets you with a golden needle,
He will scrape away the dust—your wisdom eye will shine bright.

**Self-Realization:**
Teeth fallen, hair gray, my aged frame remains,
Yet the original spirit clings to foolishness still.
In the market’s hustle, I earn my daily bread,
On the mountain’s heights, I bear the moon’s solitude alone.
Dispelling the waters, the fire’s essence is revealed,
Parting the smoke, I point to the ice-cup’s lake.
From this moment, my crimson clouds unfurl,
Treading upon pure yin, this wheel of darkness is shattered.

**On the Sword:**
Awakened, the treasure-sword is clearest of all,
Sharpened and polished, it stands mute before me.
Lifted high, it splits the new Dao’s eye,
A single stroke severs the old entanglements of the heart.
Dawn reveals its pristine, unstained brilliance,
Night emits its radiance with resounding clarity.
It repels demonic forces and malevolent qi,
All dissolve into formlessness beyond the void.

**Composed at Comrade Zheng’s Residence:**
Today, on this clear and bright water hall,
A dwelling place where all may dwell in perfect ease.
Children, grandchildren, wives—all rejoice in harmony,
Their virtue as fragrant as the lotus on the Dao’s path.
Retreating from self to serve others is Comrade Zheng’s way,
Resting the mind in goodness surpasses scriptural study.
When fortune arrives, we dwell beyond green mountains,
A thousand *li* of white clouds as our painted screen.
Last night, I dreamed the Eight Immortals called,
They bestowed robes of *luan* and jade embroidery.
Spread out scrolls of barbarian silk, richly embroidered,
A single elephant-tusk flute wafts clouds and mist.
I widely impart teachings to open the heart’s ground,
Writing verses and poems to sow fields of merit.
Who can fathom the secrets of celestial mechanism?
Only the *Harmful Wind* can transmit its essence alone.

**Hearing the Oriole’s Song:**
Today, the twenty-eighth of the third month,
A sudden oriole’s cry pierces my ear.
I open the Dao’s eye to behold it—
Its feathers newly brushed with gold.
It turns and sings its pure, clear notes,
Its intent, I think, aligns with my own heart.
Like a *qin* just tuned to its finest pitch,
Even the wind and moon, without sentiment, are its audience.

**Early Spring:**
The world’s net unravels—no dust to stain,
The garden blooms like a spring within a cave.
Do you still recognize the carefree traveler?
Do I not dwell in effortless ease?
Verses flow as I sit, one after another,
Drunk, I raise the wine cup again and again.
The four seasons’ flowers bloom in their own splendor,
Yet only this pure fragrance remains equal.
The mundane cage is left far behind,
Who today knows the spring beyond the world?
If one clings to the embroidered sash,
They have already become a carefree recluse.
Poetry spreads through the brush’s swift strokes,
Wine glides through the fragrant cup, ever anew.
Recognize the ancestors’ true ground,
Golden sprouts nourished throughout the garden’s expanse.

**Inscribed on a Friend’s Tower:**
Deeply I envy the child’s joy in driving the ox,
No need for adornment, no rush to comb the hair.
Leisure is the true kin of incense’s sacred flame,
Labor’s toil knows not the distant, boundless ease.
Though the *Penglai* Isles lie but a step away,
The carefree path to the Purple Palace I’ve already trod.
Letting go of the River of Love brings utmost purity,
The light carriage glides across the Ten Realms.
**To a Friend on the Snow:**
Scarlet clouds thicken, the white sand chills—
Dancing in the void, they blind the eye’s reach.
Auspicious omens fill the measure of a foot,
The six-petaled flower blooms as prophecy.
Beyond the scene, the painted image returns to the fisherman,
Within the radiance, purity belongs to the immortals.
As evening falls, the moon clears the dense mist,
A single stream of light illuminates the white clouds.

**To My Nephew:**
A new poem for my seventh brother,
My words are earnest—do not waste your days.
Uphold the nation’s laws, ponder righteousness,
Guard the military gates, protect the armor and spear.
In shared meals, let courtesy prevail,
In speech and song, let humility lead.
Prioritizing others is the wisest path,
Soon you shall return, singing triumphant songs.

**On My Elder Brother’s Birthday:**
Auspicious clouds and mists give birth to the virtuous,
At five hundred years, the third month’s encounter is most wondrous.
The eleventh day’s hour is uniquely rare,
Three thousand years have passed since the peach blossoms first bore fruit.
Do not refuse the golden *xueliang* wine—add more,
Let the jade censer’s incense burn full and bright.
I raise my cup in toast—none can compare,
Today, as your younger brother, I speak with care.
If compared to gold and jade, they may be lacking,
If compared to rivers and seas, they are not exhausted.
If compared to iron and stone, they may be shattered,
If compared to pines and cypresses, they may be bent.
Yet my brother’s longevity surpasses all—
Endless, unbroken, never to fade.
Midday has passed the radiant sun’s peak,
Tender green and delicate red mark the forbidden smoke.
The true fire of purity is now revealed,
Not lost in the murky wine—his Dao is firm.
Knowing his singular nature brings eternal life,
Why shame the mortal frame with its old rags?
The swallow’s murmurs are all enchanting,
The oriole’s trills gaze upon the virtuous child.
Who among the Three Fields recognizes the treasure within emptiness?
The Four Deceptions I alone perceive on the mountain’s heights.
If one reverses the Five Phases’ order,
Even today, one may meet the immortals.

**Reflections:**
Leisurely, leisurely, I take up the brush,
Revealing the Four Worthies within the study hall.
The inkstone boy adds water with a child’s delight,
The red-robed maiden grinds the ink with ancient skill.
The silver-haired youth transmits the script,
The green-browed maiden spreads the brocade paper.
Ninefold transformations arrange the true jade’s glow,
A single stroke completes the pearl’s perfection.
Bright light gathers in a thousand gleaming forms,
Vibrant hues cluster in five resplendent colors.

The **Celestial Master’s** lofty ascent—
Tenfold worthy to offer the Great Dao’s saints.
The Wind King’s harm retreats to distant peaks,
Trusting feet like clouds near the Ocean’s bounds.

Eight hundred deeds bear twin trees’ fruit,
Three thousand merits thunder in one voice.
No lust for steeds nor worldly cravings rise,
Nor monkey-minds to plunder mortal wealth.
Wealth and desire both may vanish clean,
Yet wealth and desire need not cling to me.
Forever banished from the Yellow Springs’ fall,
Long since turned back—now the Dao’s eye opens wide.
Wherever the Azure Mists gleam bright,
I follow wind and moon past the Jade Terrace.

---
**To Li Dao Friend**
Your leisure knows no bound, your joy unbound—
The Dao is whole, the world’s dust cast aside.
Your verses shine like banished immortals’ words,
Your spirit echoes Laozi’s ancient home.
Yet know the literary heights of Han Yu,
And the lute hall’s bond with Bo Ya’s tune.
Does Rong Qiao still walk this earth?
Let us return to Penglai, striding on clouds.

---
**Continuing the Rhyme**
From cloud-roots rise, unbound by mortal span,
Everywhere the wind and moon’s bright play.
Two cranes cross the water—mine to ride,
The Qichuan scene now mine to claim.
Clear and empty qi, by Master’s guidance,
Serene and pure—yet I fall short of Yi Ya’s grace.
Adrift in ease, I grasp true freedom’s art—
Why seek elixirs or feast on morning mist?

---
**On the Red-Eyed [Saint]**
What sound within your ears now sharpens clear?
Yet eyes like blindness, crimson and unseeing.
Like monks at first stillness, deep in dhyana’s hold,
Or the Dao’s first steps—now the work begins.
Inner thoughts dissolve, the spirit dwells serene,
No outward musings—emptiness is all.
The wild horse tamed, the mind’s monkey bound,
The Jade Path at the crown now opens wide.

---
**On the Charcoal Grinder**
The donkey’s strength too weak for the steep path’s climb,
The driver’s wrath stirs—his blows rain down.
One heart’s fury at the pace too slow,
Two hands wield the whip in ceaseless pain.
Yet why not know what’s light and what’s heavy?
More suffering comes from this blind strife.
Oh, how cruel—no mercy in his sight!
This alone proves karma’s bitter fruit.

---
**Master Shuo’an’s Transformation of Ma Yu**
A monk of nameless rank guards stillness here,
His verse proclaims:
*"Opening and closing—what cause lies deep?
Silent sitting banishes greed and wrath.*
The tower’s horn like spring’s fleeting dream,
The waves of Release now reveal true form.
When clarity dawns, the heart is clear—
When faintest ripples stir, the water’s pure.
To watch the world’s folly, bound in ignorance,
Thus I stay in the Zen hall, never leave.
The Master answers each line with three—
Eight quatrains follow, marking the Eight Consciousnesses.

*Opening and closing—what cause lies deep?
All from the eye’s realm, dust’s net undone.
White steeds pass by, too swift to stain,
Wild horses gallop free, unchecked, unbound.
Silent sitting banishes greed and wrath—
No ear for worldly clamor, no embrace.
No drum nor string, yet music lingers near,
No chord, yet harmony fills the air.
The tower’s horn like spring’s fleeting dream,
Breath alone suffices—no need for speech.
This parting bears clear fruit’s promise bright,
This life plants seeds of virtue’s worth.
The waves of Release now reveal true form—
Tongue’s five tastes never touch the lip.
Three times serene, in purity alone,
One flavor sweet—beyond all price.
When clarity dawns, the heart is clear—
A single light within the body glows.
From now, stillness and dimness intertwine,
Yet deeper shadows veil the way.
When faintest ripples stir, the water’s pure—
Desire and thought dissolve, the heart undone.
Leakless, effortless—true awakening’s rise,
Neither gain nor loss seals perfection’s close.
To watch the world’s folly, bound in ignorance,
Delusion clings—life and death ensnare.
Now light returns, the mirror’s gaze,
The heart’s true nature grasped in Dao’s embrace.
Thus I stay in the Zen hall, never leave,
No defilement clouds the mind’s pure light.
Unfulfilled still is my vow to save all beings,
Yet Dao’s deep talk I’ll now unfold.

---
**To the Monk Named Nameless**
The Master now has coolness, pure and bright,
One nature shines with fortune’s golden light.
Yet ‘Nameless’ suits him best—where does the Buddha dwell?
Where is the Sage who first set foot on earth?

---
**A Friend’s Inquiry**
Spring’s youth is best for study’s embrace,
Truth’s logic clear—no need for forced chase.
If exams call, then win with might,
Yet honor’s mark already gleams in sight.
Yan the Scholar pens four lines—twelve more follow:

*"How does the wheel of birth and death unfold?
Recognize the primal face, unchanging, old.
Three treasures, five colors gathered near,
The path to longevity gleams with misty light.
To love or crave—what law can sever ties?
True purity lies in steadfast will.
All things, all forms—no grasp, no cling,
One round light on jade pools’ surface shine.
Time’s fleeting as the wind—how long has passed?
Yet none but fools mistake the way.
In leisure, seek the truth’s true face,
Then joy in freedom, unbound, embrace.
Though years may age this worn-out frame,
The True Person within knows no decay.
Do not cling to outward guise or show,
The child’s pure face reveals no shift or sway."*

---
**To the Fisherman**
This fish now dances, wild and free,
Scaled in gold, it leaps the spring’s clear stream.
Three casts with golden hook—it swallows bait,
One tug brings saints to feast at table’s edge.

---
**To the Novice in Practice**
White robes, green sash—fated ties from old,
By chance you met me, crossed the mist’s deep flood.
Though Dao’s depths still veil your path,
You’re now a little wayfarer of Penglai’s hall.

---
**To a Practicing Friend**
Leap past Yin-Yang’s forge of fate’s design,
One heart for the Dao—turn not back again.
Purity itself is the path to saints,
Only in stillness nurture inner light.

---
**On the Paper Flag**
If wind’s favor brings good fortune’s hand,
Each dawn I win the sun’s high rest.
Hungry, I beg the streets for coins to spend—
Yet only those who give are truly blessed.

---
**Echoing a Dao Friend’s Verse**
Seize the true form—no need to ask your years,
Five thousand words of incense fill the air.
Lofty ease, like swallows in repose,
I laugh at spirits bright in jade halls’ glow.

---
**To Liu the Fourth Friend**
Ever distinguish the mirror’s face,
Lest dust obscures the pearl’s bright grace.
With fate’s new thread, your form takes shape,
Yet formless body sheds the old.
In dreams you met me, speechless, deep in sleep,
Yet know I came to seek the Wind King’s keep.
Still you crave talk—let’s meet in ice’s chill,
Where warmth and cold in stillness dwell.

**On Fate’s Shallow Fortune and Laborious Days**
Fate bestows but little fortune, scarce the causes arise,
Only the toils of life’s path drag me through the years.
If you wish to dwell in ease and leisure,
Let your heart remain ever clean—no cares, no restless strife.

Leave but a few words for my ears to hear,
Wait till your life holds nothing left to do.
Then we may together roam in carefree bliss,
Meeting immortals in talk of the Unutterable.

A single finger points the way to Eternal Life,
Yet your nature’s fate still binds you tight.
From the first breath, the truth is clear to see,
Why fear the future when you’ve already touched the Way?

Reflect now on my words—if fate denies,
In you alone, let steadfast resolve arise.
With honest heart and simple truth untarnished,
Though no god nor sage, you’ll walk the path of Virtue.

To ponder chance encounters, fleeting yet fortunate,
How could such leisure ever truly be?
Man finds no joy in burdens—only ease,
Then let us rise together, hearts aligned in grace.

Better than not seeing your face at all,
Is your virtue everlasting, pure and bright.
Auspicious signs cling close, like pearls untold,
One clear gem shines—your mind’s true light.

To meet my teacher in dreams is but a sleeping sage,
Yet through you, I’ve known this fateful thread.
If you still walk this path as I’ve described,
No need for fear—just rest in boundless ease.

**The Blossom of the Third Month**
At this fair time, the third month’s flower blooms,
Like sandalwood in heart, like jade in cheek.
Pluck one branch to crown my head and wear,
And follow me to Penglai’s halls of air.

**On the Paper Skull to Warn Ma Yi**
Ah, lament the world where all are bound in sorrow’s net!
I must now paint a skull to wake the foolish man.
In life, he clings to wrongs and bitter deeds,
Till he meets this fate—then he’ll cease his strife.

To be a man, one must perceive the dust of toil,
A pure mind is treasure none can spoil.
Snatch the pearl from the Lipu Dragon’s maw,
And enter Kunlun’s caves to live in flawless law.

**Ode to the Moon**
The waxing moon is gold, the waning silver bright,
Each half a measure, gold and silver in the night.
I’ve bound them both to sixteen *liang*—
How then do stars divide their weight?

**Ode to the Dwarf Sophora**
The Boundless Sage planted dwarf sophora here,
Its cool shade spreads wide—who else might share?
Today, I rejoice beneath its branches green,
Remembering well when first I planted them.

**Visiting the White Deer Hermitage**
This hermitage is named for chill and purity’s call,
Where white deer once ascended to the Heavens’ hall.
Do not mock me for coming here, my friend,
For I’ve already found my rest in clouds beyond.

**On the Sudden Change in Weather**
The Ho family’s words run deep and wide,
Yesterday’s sun, today’s gloom and pride.
If Heaven’s will could be counted by man’s hand,
It would be neither high nor broad—just like a mortal’s mind.

When neither cold nor heat the wind does blow,
Round golden cakes reflect the light on my robe.
The Martial Constellation now guards the Literary,
At the Upper Elemental Festival, brighter than its contrary.

**On a Friend’s Pond**
Naosun’s pond mirrors Han’s ancient marshes,
Before its waves, all sound is hushed and stilled.
Yet turn your gaze to where the water murmurs,
And see the wheel of life’s unjust, unending wheel.

**Hearing Cicadas in the Sixth Month**
The cicada sheds its black robe, feels its body light,
And becomes a golden one, perched high to sing its might.
It’s found true companionship in breezes clear,
Who else today would hear this voice so new and rare?

The black cicada’s shell now cast aside,
Its body rises, lighter by the tide.
In tall sophora’s shade, it sits with grace,
And sings in freedom, soft yet full of place.

**Ode to the Mid-Autumn Moon**
Strange how the sky now presses cold on man,
Yet rises up a golden plate from mist’s remains.
Not like the usual three-five nights of old,
I urge you now—do not dismiss this sight, so bold.

**On the Tea Whisk**
Light and slender, yet its purpose burns so near,
Long immersed in oil, its truth grows dim and drear.
Though I love to stir the tea’s bright glow,
How could I know the flame would turn and sear my soul?

**Ode to Bamboo**
When moonlight shines, its nodes are gold like scattered flakes,
When breezes touch, its leaves are jade—so crisp, so frail.
Through winter’s chill, it stands with virtue’s mark,
Not like the common grass that bows and falls apart.

**Ode to Tea**
Once I saw it at Zhao’s old abode,
Now Lu Quan serves it in seven cups of joy.
After brewing, where does it go?
The wind carries me to Penglai’s shore.

**Giving a Fan to My Nephew to Ward Off Dust**
You wash away wine and wool with care,
I give this frost-laden fan to little Seventh Brother.
To clear the dust and open the eyes of the Dao,
And grant my child forevermore this breeze of Virtue.

**On the Fifteenth Night Moon**
As twilight fades and clouds withdraw,
The moon’s cold wheel still shines where night withdraws.
This light tonight is clear and bright—distinct,
Do not compare it to the common sight.

**On the Tea House**
I’ve feasted on coiled peaches, better than mere fruit,
This flavor’s taste belongs to me—my suit.
To trade the false for truth, my nature’s call,
Point the way to Penglai, where rainbows span the hall.

**Lamenting the World**
Ah, lament the world where name and gain are sought,
Morning’s greed and evening’s love—no end in sight.
To see it clearly is like watching chess,
When lost, the pieces scatter, and the game is done, no less.

Hurry, hurry now, to cultivate and rise,
I’ll paint this skull to mark the path you’ll choose.
From ancient times, men chase what’s vain and bright,
Till now, they’ve not yet learned to cease their fight.

**When My Eastward Journey Was Delayed by a Friend’s Deception**
Who held my feet? I’ll slowly gather them,
Yet now I see—no need for such a scheme.
Today I’ve found the road ahead,
And now my carefree vessel sails to shore with speed.

Your feet you’ll hold, but I’ll detect your truth,
The True Wind’s path will search you out.
You know full well the ties that bind,
To cultivate and follow the land’s true law you’ll find.

**Leisurely Thoughts**
One wheel of moon, one breath of wind,
Within and without, they dance and blend.
Rolling from Kunlun’s peak so high,
Their light and breeze are clear—nature’s majesty.

**Gazing in the Mirror**
Who knows that in the mirror’s strange embrace,
I’ve split the south and north in two with grace?
I lift my spirit-mind to view its light,
No need to seek another’s face so bright.

**Self-Composed Verse**
From this, I’ll tear apart the net of iron true,
Today I leap from dust’s confining cage anew.
Now take the moon and play it with my hands,
And scatter idle clouds to seek the Wind King’s lands.

**On a Caged Parrot**
Painted as a parrot, yet it does not chirp,
Freed from its cage, it leaves life’s grip.
Tell the butterfly not to mock its flight,
For now it soars beyond this narrow sight.

**On Parting from Kin**
With heart and mind pure, no need for hair’s deceit,
The water-clouds are my path, my fate.
No need for mourners when my body’s gone,
But take this chance—now leave the bonds of life’s old sun.

**On the First Day of the Fifth Month**
I honor those who gather in the White Lotus Society,
Where guests and moon unite—this chance is rare and free.
If all would wake to eat the food of Ling Mountain’s height,
They’d trade their lives for immortality in silent night.

**On the Fifteenth Day of the Fifth Month**
May the household first know peace and auspicious fortune,
Then kindle the fire within your heart.
Burn away to see the original true face,
Gazing with joy upon the reunion’s embrace.

**On the Jade Flower Golden Lotus Society**
I urge you not to cling to *having* within *not-having*,
Nor lose *not-having* by grasping *having* within *not-having*.
*Nurture having* to bloom the Jade Flower head,
And *each head* will bear the Golden Lotus crown.

**To the Fishing Hermit**
After casting your line, you see the tortoise again,
Knowing your fate lies among the ranks of immortals.
The *wūláng* calls out—it knows my intent—
Leaping from the surging waves a thousand feet high.

**To Cui the Thousand-Household Officer Seeking Wisdom**
Refined essence seeks clarity,
Within, pure nature’s virtue stands firm.
Naturally, wisdom unfolds,
Surely revealing brilliance’s birth.
To teach you shared sorrow’s weight,
May years extend like Pengzu’s span.
Uniting the Three Teachings’ truths,
Far off, the path’s true measure is gained.

**For Hao Shenghua After Smashing the Jar**
Shattering the true ash jar,
Now the Wind King’s sight is revealed.
True remnants await awakening—
Each soul calls out to the one.
To keep the heart unshaken,
Break each illusion clean.
At *zi-wu-ma-you* hours,
Observe the skull’s hollow stare.

**Leisurely Verse**
Laughing at this wild Dao,
Why now delight in borrowed light?
Follow fate to dissolve old karma,
No longer crafting fresh misfortune.
Tame the mind-horse with firm reins,
Restrain the heart-monkey tight.
Cultivate the Way with urgency,
Each day drawing fragrant virtue’s breath.

**On Skulls**
This is King Zhao’s hollow frame,
In life, his nature was weak.
Strip away your skull’s disguise—
Now the Mid-Autumn moon shines clear.

**On Coolness**
Coolness—what does it resemble?
Not the same as bitter cold’s harshness.
Midnight moon over still waters,
Early autumn breeze after rain.

**To Fan Caifu**
My nephew, called Fifth Brother Wang,
His wife, they call my niece.
The two have forged a blessed bond—
May neither suffer ruin’s pain.
If you seek the *mercury-lead* path,
Nurture the True Dragon and Tiger.
The True Dragon and Tiger—
Most do not recognize—
One each beside Red Phoenix Peak.
Guarding their nests, they intertwine,
Exchanging east and west in trade.
This trade, when rightly done,
Slays the Three Pengs in the Dan Field.
None grasp the double meaning’s depth,
Yet a spirit boy strikes the fifth watch.
Striking the fifth watch, news spreads—
A pure spring’s perfect accord.
Like ambrosia poured upon the crown,
Only I know its true essence.
Know it well—rest, rest, rest,
Niece, nephew, hasten your practice.
If you refuse my words,
In the wilderness, two skulls you’ll be.

**Proclamation for the Golden Lotus Society**
By the eternal light of wisdom’s lamp,
We rely on the Jade Bud’s radiance.
The nature-torch burns eternally,
Unveiling the Golden Lotus’s glow.
Bathing in the Three Lights’ brilliance,
Dissolving the Four False names.
Treading the void, probing the profound,
Searching for marvels rare.
Washed clean in purity’s realm,
Moving through fragrant paths.
Each holds pearls and jade,
Together presenting crystal and gem.
Displaying the vital essence,
Nurture the qi with care.
Slightly mastering this key,
Hang the fragrant title high.

**Proclamation for the Jade Flower Society**
The transformation of jade is the essence of *qi*,
The Golden Lotus is the ancestor of spirit.
When *qi* and spirit intertwine,
They become immortals.
*The Yinshu Jing* annotates:
*"Spirit is the child of qi, qi the mother of spirit.
When mother and child unite,
Immortal birth is achieved."*

Establishing the Jade Flower Golden Lotus Society
In these two prefectures,
All must recognize true nature.
Unaware of the true source,
Many study minor side paths—
Merely methods to foster blessings and life,
Not the Dao’s true cultivation.
In matters of life and nature,
Even slight error veers from humanity.

If you seek true practice,
When hungry, eat;
When tired, sleep—
No need to sit in meditation,
No need to study the Way.
Only screen out worldly entanglements,
Only seek the two characters: *heart-clear*.
The rest is not cultivation.

Each holds wisdom—
Daily in the hall of abstinence,
Reflect deeply,
Lest you stray to other doors.

True function has its own true function and true practice.
The True Person of Jin said:
*"To achieve true function,
One must purify the heart, settle the mind,
Calm the spirit and emotions,
Neither moving nor acting,
Truly clear and pure,
Embrace the Original, preserve the One,
Nurture the spirit, stabilize the qi—
This is true function.*

*To achieve true practice,
One must cultivate virtue and power,
Relieve poverty and ease suffering,
Seeing others in distress,
Always harboring a heart of rescue,
Or transform and guide the virtuous
To enter the Way and practice.
In all actions,
Prioritize others over self,
Unselfish toward all beings—
This is true practice."*

May all honorably heed these words.
The *Complete Authentic Collection of Chongyang* ends here, Volume Ten.

**Volume Eleven of the Complete Authentic Collection of Chongyang**
*Composed by Master Zhongyang of Zhongnan Mountain, Wang Zhe*

---
**Song: *Zhuiyan Xiang* (醴醾香)**
At ease with fate’s unfolding,
Trusting steps without thought or reckoning.
A crisp breeze calls the moon as companion,
Together, boundless and free.

Along the long road, joyful and singing,
Lips hum, tongues pluck the air’s melody.
Suddenly passing through the immortal’s halls,
Mountain peaks—worth lingering to admire.

Just as blessings multiply and gather,
Strange fruits and flowers scatter sweetness and fragrance.
Though fine weather and beauty may tempt,
Let water and clouds guide my path—
To the farthest shores, the distant horizon.

Then I meet the pure spirit-vessel,
Ferrying me beyond this shore.
This time, I’ve become a true Daoist wind-han.
*Hechuang Tian* (鹤冲天)

Delusions vanish, the path is clear—
Now I may truly cultivate and refine.
Stillness is the root, the true gateway.
Do not seek elsewhere, lest you stray from the Dao’s path,
And miss the way to the immortals.

In leisure’s deepest quiet,
The primal root and luminous essence unfold,
Layer by layer, ever more awakened.
When virtue and practice are complete,
Only crimson clouds remain.

Once, I met my master in person,
Who taught me the secret of eternal life,
Again and again, with tender care.
Now I know I’ve been saved.

I vow to follow, hand in hand,
Through endless clouds, forevermore.

---
**Song: *Wang Yuanxing* (望远行)**
Under the sun’s bright gaze,
The moon pours silver, stars gleam clear.
Where the Three Lights converge,
Five colors rise in stillness—
A silent witness to true cultivation,
Where qi and spirit gather.
Now I may tread the hidden path.

This fullness of virtue and practice is certain.
With uprightness, I must refine and polish,
Revealing the original true nature—
Every leaf luminous, every branch refined,
Pure and everlasting.

Beyond the clouds, the Green Boy holds the decree,
Passing down the Celestial Emperor’s command.
I thank the Ten Isles of Master Shizhou—
The immortals have summoned me.

---
**Song: *Yong Xue* (咏雪)**
Blessings spread like jade and pearls,
Cut by wind into delicate flakes,
Scattered across the void,
Falling like powder on eaves and tiles.
Locking gardens in silence,
Dotting paths with fleeting marks—
Truly a scene fit for brush and ink.

Even treasures of jade and pearl cannot compare
To this harvest’s bounty.
Pure and fresh, its brilliance shimmers,
Its crispness ever refreshing.

Valleys flatten, mountains blend into one,
Near and far, no boundary remains.
Just like my home—
Celestial landscapes, clear and boundless,
Glowing like Penglai’s pavilions,
Bathed in eternal light.

---
**Song: *Manting Fang* (满庭芳)**
Selecting rare seeds, planting in season,
Nurtured by wind and rain,
Branches stretch, leaves unfurl.
Only when fully grown may they be harvested—
The pond’s edges turn green with new shoots.
How others envy their freshness and purity,
Their tender, plump skins.

Let them be spun into fine threads,
Woven into dense cloth,
Pounded until soft.
Then, cut and stitched into immortal robes—
Who else could wear them but me?

When virtue and practice are complete,
Six *qian* of silk are exchanged—
Now your merit truly shines.

---
**Song: *For Master Lü’s Ritual Invitation to Friends from Jingyang***
Long have I opened my heart,
Today’s ritual brings fresh delight.
Among friends, there is pure joy.
Wind-companions and cloud-friends gather,
All ascending to refine the elixir.
Only my old Jingyang brothers remain,
Their vision clear and boundless.

I invite all masters and sages,
Wishing to ascend the immortal stage.
Together, we uphold the Dao—
No need for incense or sandalwood,
Only heart-incense burning.
The saints have come to observe.

When virtue and practice are complete,
We shall surely meet in the clouds.
Tonight’s true work brings joy—
All will ride the cranes home.

---
**Song: *For Master Zhan’s Inquiry***
With lofty spirit, heart unbound,
Let no worries or entanglements disturb you.
Cultivate the self, nurture the nature—
Find joy in what fate offers.
This is to uphold the true Dao,
Kindling eternal spirit within.
Embrace leisure’s taste,
And you shall dwell in lasting years.

Thus, you must clearly understand:
Refine suffering into elixir,
Passing it down.
Then you may wander freely, ever fresh.
Wait until the primal root shines bright—
Then virtue and practice will be complete.

Do you not see?
The path to Penglai is secure—
There, you’ll meet both immortals and humans.

---
**Song: *Gift to a Friend with Doubts***
The courtyard lies in disrepair,
Trees sway in the wind—
The walls are crumbling.
You say your wife has passed,
Father and son—what can be done?
Wang Zhe laughed and said,
*"Your fate is to find joy in solitude.
You still do not see—
In the fire-pit, seek not the red furnace.
Cut away all clinging desires,
Sever them utterly.
Walk with the moon as your neighbor—
This is my disciple’s way.
Follow the steady path to Penglai,
Transcending birth and death,
Never falling into the Three Realms.
In the depths of white clouds,
There lies another heaven."*

---
**Song: *Gift to My Nephew***
Not born with talent, yet burdened by karma—
Why strive to emulate my ways?
Reflecting on yourself,
You’ve never truly excelled.
Most painful is your shallow learning,
Students crowding, trembling in fear.
When you ask for advice,
Your heart feels like walking on thin ice.
Could you ever be a model?
If so, you’d surely die—
Yet you earn only hatred.

Another chain binds you—
Soon you’ll rise above.
Turning to the Dao, I wave farewell,
Seeking friends among clouds and mists.
The true news is this:
The Penglai path is secure—
Come, let us ascend together.

---
**Song: *Huanghe Qing* (黄河清)**
The root is deep, the source pure and sealed,
Guarded in profound stillness.
Warmth grows within,
All cold and rigidity banished.
A different elegance emerges—
Now I know I’ve risen beyond control.
Naturally, eternal life is met,
The alchemical flower ready to pluck.

From the beginning, true spirit exists—
This time, I’ve found the lead and mercury.

The moment it congeals,
A single grain of *jindan* is ready to offer.

Auspicious radiance shines forth,
Now coming and going with *luan* leading *feng*.
The Ten Isles and Three Mountains—
Divine immortals rejoice, welcoming us to feast.

Again, according to the count of **one hundred and eight**—
Nine *ju* of the Yellow River, nine transformations,
Turbid waves and great billows now pure and still.
The Nine Rivers converge,
All returning to the Right Way.

In the Nine Cauldrons, it manifests,
The Nine Palaces unfold—
Flows and currents now fixed.
Jade overflows, gold cascades—
Where the nine luminosities bloom,
The nine glories unfold their shadows.
Nine heavens of emerald green align,
Nine marshes where cranes call—
Welcoming the luminous essence.

Nine lights pierce the void,
Reflecting the sacred glow.
Nine curves—divine pearls leap,
Nine immortals arrive—
Just as they swim.

Deep and clear, now complete,
The Nine Heavens’ path to holiness is open.

---
**Song: *Hanyong Chun* (汉宫春)**
Just the time to cultivate,
Deep and secret, profound and subtle.
The pivot lies here—
With this, the gate is sealed.

Awake and clear,
Now fashioned—
Elegant and true.

From ancient times, the essence has gathered—
Thus, its radiance shines.
The Three Lights shine from the start,
Now recognized—
The original tone resounds.
Pure sound permeates, echoing through the seven orifices.
From Kunlun, a *qingtong* summons me,
To fish with golden thread for the luminous mind,
Receiving the celestial scroll and purple edict.

---
**Song: *Xia Yun Feng* (夏云峰)**
In cultivation, no need for strict *zhuozuo* at *zi-wu*.
Lead and mercury naturally congeal—
Only true *ci* is required.
The swift path of the Mysterious—
Who understands it but me, content?
Secrets unfold—
Leisurely, vast and unbounded,
Subtly shifting.

Gradually, the luminous radiance emits wonders,
Changing into clouds of glory—
Light and color follow.
Truly, it was once fitting.
In the depths of white clouds,
The true teacher of the earth’s lungs resides.
Now permitted to ascend to the *Danxia*,
Together in *wuwei*.

Guarding the *zhulin*,
No action—
Alone, reclining on high peaks.
Stone pillow, grass robe—
Gazing far.
Water peaches, mountain plums—
Eating as fate allows,
Stealing *yang* and *yin*.
Slowly shedding,
The dusty mortal form,
Threefold the heart of the zither.

The *taixian* debates depth and shallowness—
Naturally revealed,
No need for further search.
Now comprehending the Mysterious,
Stepping into the *qionglin*.
Among the jade flowers,
Henceforth nurturing the true gold.
Glowing stillness,
With clear wind and bright moon—
Forever companions.

---
**Song: *Yaotai Yue* (瑶台月)**
Leisurely scenes,
True leisure understood—
Only clarity can be entrusted.
Originally, that which must be made firm.
Congealed into a single grain of *jindan*,
Five-colored clouds spread.
Together they guard,
Together they gather.
Returning light shines,
Reflected light gazes back.
Encountered—
Perfectly complete—
The true teacher’s guidance.
This aids the pure and unadorned,
Endlessly yearning.

It must be known that it has always existed.
Following the gleaming auspicious hues,
Jewelry and ornaments adorn the steps.
The *taixian* dances,
The path of immortals.
Golden boys lead,
Jade girls instruct.
Worthy to attend the *Yaotai*,
Moonlit feast on jade mats.

---
**Song: *Shengsheng Man* (声声慢)**
Knocking at the golden gate,
Locking the jade door—
Leisurely, yet no cultivation.
Who in the dimness understands?
Playing with an infant.
Sleeping, catching monkeys and horses,
Awakening to gather *qiongzi*.
Each moment,
This practice—
A hundred days, only the heart knows.

Free and unbounded,
Only spreading—
Crimson clouds and radiance.
Enveloping the luminous mind,
Now revealing the original true *ci*.
A single grain of divine *dan* forms,
Three flames tightly entwined.
Passing the *Yaochi*,
Piercing the green celestial peak—
*Wuwei*.

---
**Song: *Zhidu Chun* (绛都春)**
Naturally enlightened,
This encounter deepens—
Cool clarity awakens.
Within the stillness, lead and mercury congeal,
All because *ren* meets *bing*.
The original face becomes a jade neck—
Reflected light brings eternal tranquility.
Swiftly returning,
The path ahead is permitted—
Long-standing firmness.

Fine scenes,
Light spreads resplendent—
Beyond the void, ten thousand silver clouds align.
Gradually approaching,
Meeting and welcoming in an instant—
The *Penglai* path opens to the immortal realm.
A golden boy invites.
Holding the jade edict, taught in person,
The wind of harm received.

---
**Song: *Erlang Shen* (二郎神)**
Gazing at the dusty world,
All reduced to—
Empty names, refined.
This false form, unaware—
Still chasing cleverness and clumsiness.
A hundred years of prime—how few!
By seventy, escape is difficult.
Within, true guilt grows heavier,
No way to dispel it.
As if recalling—
Originally, one luminous point.
Swiftly recognize what it has always been called—
It is the perfected light and shadow.
Again, the *jindan* gleams—
Let it be the master,
Endlessly enduring.
May all mortals turn back,
Refining purity, not deceiving.

---
**Song: *Shang Ping Xi #1* (上平西#1)**
Toward Zhongnan,
An encounter—
Wild winds arise.
Now wandering the seas of auspiciousness.
Leisurely and content,
Free to compose poems and songs.
Naturally, the divine *qi* intertwines,
Recognizing the true incense of the heart.
True stillness—
Only clarity,
Still clearer—
Abiding in coolness.
Red, blue, black, white, and yellow.
Five colors now encircle the jewel-light.
This time, it must be permitted—
Above the azure void,
Brilliant without bounds.

---
**Song: *Qitian Le* (齐天乐)**
To cultivate, know the swift path—
How to arrange the furnace and kiln?
Take the *dantian* as treasure,
All phenomena in the *baobei* forest—
All gathered here,
Before the *Ruizhu Gong*,
Fully instructed.
Emerging with the luminous mind,
A single divine pearl—
Tumbling.
Bright and clear above the sky,
The Jade Emperor’s edict,
The green boy solemnly presenting the golden decree.

「This is the conjunction of merit and practice,
Both fully paired and matched—auspicious signs abound.
Endless and eternal,
Within the Great Luo Heaven,
Holding and carrying elixir herbs.

Clear and profound,
Suddenly transcending the Three Isles of Non-Doing.
Ascending the Celestial Gate—
Return, return, return to the Original Source.
The two mortal counties,
Now have no sight of me.

Enveloped by the Pure Wind and White Clouds,
Everlastingly summoned.
The King of Harmful Winds,
This time departs from me.
I urge all gentlemen,
To seek the Mysterious and Marvelous,
No more deliberation.

Look upon this false body,
Better than none at all.
Only now have I crossed the Other Shore,
I know it well.

To see again,
This time is difficult.
Drunk on Penglai’s splendor,
At sixty-three years of age,
In the fine season of the third month,
On the eleventh day of celebration.

Auspicious *qi* and blessed clouds,
Fragrant incense smoke sealing the divine radiance.
At this moment, the lofty vault,
Chooses to descend celestial messengers,
And the flowers of heaven scatter in disarray.
Ice and jade in form,
Divine beings in stature—
Who can truly know this?

I solemnly inform my wise elder brother,
Now, for the present moment,
Name and fame, honor and wealth—
Like fire within stone.
Swiftly escaping the mortal net,
Suddenly understanding the removal of self and others.
Free and unbounded,
The True One’s true joy—
Holding the void.

Feasting on the Shattered Peaches of Penglai,
The old path of Penglai,
Together we shall walk.

*Rain in the Flower* (花慢)
Gold chrysanthemum just blooming,
Silver hare gradually emerging,
New medicine’s radiant hue as its companion.
Unfolding in the fragrant void,
The Pure Moon of deep autumn.
Then, in accordance with the Central Harmony,
It must be the night of the full moon’s cycle.
Worthy of my family’s appreciation,
Just as it should be—
Inviting branches, welcoming the luminous pavilion.
Capable of savoring refined beauty,
Delicate hues spread out,
Illuminating shadows—
Both harmoniously paired.

Suddenly recalling the Luminous Spirit,
The Moon Hare’s origin.
Perfumed and rich, overflowing,
Graceful and luminous, boundless.
On the Seventh and Eighth of the Double Ninth,
Fragrance spreads through the Three Isles,
Light fills the Ten Lands.

*Turning the Celestial Dipper* (斗鹌鹑)
A single luminous mind—
The material for an immortal maiden.
Echoing through the Jade Palace,
The Golden Petals open by themselves.
For the sake of the Linglong’s purity,
Emerging from Penglai,
Descending here.

Exiled to the mortal realm,
Taking birth in a vulgar form.
Only fearing this body,
Wine and lust, wealth and gain.
Mingling once more in worldly pleasures,
This heart will turn to ashes.

Reawakening to the Original Truth,
The Wheel of Rebirth turns—
No calamity at all.
Gazing again,
Ascending once more to the Jade Terrace.

*Flower Along the Path* (满路花)
From the beginning, the Great Dao,
Meeting with principle to form one’s path.
Residing in the company of wind and moon,
Abandoning honor and wealth.
Abundant pure *qi*,
Swirling red clouds.
Five hues of true brilliance,
Piercing through the perfect roundness—
Within, the narrow yellow sprout emerges.

Three thousand and eight hundred,
Counted fully, with no discrepancy.
Along the path, adding elegance,
The Golden Flowers bloom.
Branch by branch, refined and graceful,
Petal by petal, gathering rare blossoms.
In the dim and murky beyond,
A sudden strike of clear sky—
Strange fragrance ascends to the elixir field.

*Mountain Stream* (蓦山溪)
Observing your form and bearing,
Your vigor and refinement are exceptional.
Bold and magnanimous,
Yet you would rescue my leisurely solitude.
Only knowing of name and fame,
Honor and wealth along the way,
Discussing literature,
Speaking of good fortune—
Purple robes adorned with golden sashes.

If you would come with me,
Hear my early planting of merit.
Cease chasing the waves’ flow.
Only if you return,
Abandoning infatuation and love of wine.

Slightly knowing the Mysterious and Marvelous,
Grasping the essence of unbounded freedom,
Under the moonlight,
Playing with the Pure Wind,
Together we shall walk to Penglai’s island.

All fail to comprehend,
Each day’s light and time fleeting.
The path is the cycle of rebirth,
The future’s affairs—
Dark as lacquer in the unseen.

Observing your bearing and demeanor,
Your youthful spirit is most refined,
With much purity,
Little greed,
Good deeds not lost.

Hollow emotions and delicate postures,
Just like bees gathering honey.
Day and night, busy plucking flowers,
Mixing and blending—
Who will taste the nectar?

If you awaken to this,
Turn back immediately.
The path to Penglai,
Where the colored clouds end,
Has a share for those who follow.

One luminous true nature,
Two substances contained within.
Three inches of the master’s body,
Four directions of wandering—
Each invites and requests.

The Five Emotions and Six Desires,
All Seven Orifices connected,
Eight Mountains towering,
Nine Palaces deep,
How to attain the Ten Realms?

Tenfold cultivation and refinement,
Nine transformations to reach sagehood.
Eight paths surge with ambrosial nectar,
Seven Gates open—
Caverns communicating with purity.
Six streets in five colors,
Four Symbols fully devoted,
Three Lights shining,
Two Nights following,
One luminous pearl gleaming.

Aspiring to Dao and cultivating immortality,
Why do all bear burdens?
Falsely coveting the boundless void,
All from indulging in external pleasures.
Inner treasures,
Unrecognized as Non-Doing—
Only boasting of strength,
Then boasting of ability,
Boasting until it all dissolves.

Not knowing how to begin,
How can one firmly establish the foundation?
Each merely endures hunger and cold,
Better to master the interplay of yin and yang.

White as pure jade, red as brilliant flame,
Light and color dazzlingly distinct—
One roundness, ten directions of clarity,
Only then does the true elixir appear.

You seek to master it,
Recognizing the Black and the White Hare.
Above and below must harmonize,
Left and right—
The Dragon and Tiger must intermingle.

Passing down the Great Elixir,
It must enter the Red Furnace,
Refined and transmuted,
Turning into Silver Frost,
One Golden Flower gathered.

Fragrance drifts far and wide,
Piercing through Kunlun’s peaks.
Wafting up to the Azure Void,
Forming clusters of light—
Illuminating and worthy of beholding.

Within the Jade Hall,
Consorting with the Great Luo Immortals,
Self-content and joyful,
Obtaining eternal spring,
Now on the path of unbounded freedom.

Pen, ink, and paper,
The inkstone as the matter.
The first and second hexagrams,
One missing—
Difficult to use.

In leisure, sitting quietly,
Counting on fingers and pondering carefully,
If one must write,
Not thinking of it in time,
Must use the Pure Spring’s water.

Just like the four seasons—
Spring, summer, autumn, and winter.
Warmth and cold, heat and chill,
Combining to form—
What year is to be considered?

Originally, it ascends,
With mysteries beyond measure.
In accordance with the True and Mysterious,
Aligning with Heaven’s mechanism,
The intercalary month completes the year.

Concentrating the spirit and meditating afar,
Only then does the snow within lead solidify.»

Nurture the yellow sprout,
So the Golden Crow may climb toward the bright moon.
The Yellow Mother’s match—
A different household’s wind,
With dragons roaring and tigers snarling—
Who could distinguish them?

Humans still cling to desire,
Acid and spice must be savored in moderation.
To taste flavors truly,
Let the Five Agents of the Pure and Empty
Rejoice in their harmony.

Guard the Original Intestine steadfastly,
Nourish the spirit to its divine essence—
When virtue is perfected,
Ascend to the Celestial Gathering,
Dwelling in the world without rest.

The mortal frame’s four illusions—
Now is the time to examine them thoroughly.
Limitation arises from cause and condition—
Why not practice earnestly and early?

Unsoiled by dusty toil,
Displaying another household’s wind,
Unentangled, unhampered—
For oneself, all vexations are removed.

Slightly enlightened, one resists not
The allure of wealth and beauty.

Cultivate the Original Spirit—
This true principle, this true essence,
Rests upon it.

On Kunlun’s peak,
A single spot of unbounded freedom—
Facing the red haze,
Achieving self-mastery,
The crane leads, bearing the mushroom of immortality.

Dissolving the red [passion],
Sighing at the floating world,
Driven by glory and wealth,
Chased by fame and gain—
All vie in deceitful schemes,
Jealousy ever growing,
Cunning multiplying in imitation.

All are greedy—
When does it ever cease?
Each boasts of daughters and sons to serve them.
More lost in wine and song,
Hoping for endless fulfillment—
Yet who knows seventy years may not be granted?

Even if a hundred years are allotted,
There is no escape.
Awaken early—
The path ahead is not as desired.
Turn back swiftly,
And only then may one escape birth and death.

Seek the Mysterious, investigate the subtle,
Search the profound and fathom the hidden.
Take naturally the dual completeness of spirit and qi,
Revealing clearly—
The Original Beginning’s true, round nature,
Thus it is:
Jade features, jade complexion, strange and wondrous.
Glowing with gemstone radiance,
Pearlescent hues emitting auspicious omens.
The Golden Elixir formed in empty space,
Dwelling in purity,
Ascending to the Great Luo’s celestial rank.

Frozen clouds congeal.
Accumulated pearls and jade—
Auspicious omens meet in kind.
Lightly cast and dancing,
The wind’s blade shears in swirling patterns.
In an instant, spread across—
Fields, rivers, and mountain streams.
Including the Yang Valley,
Lonely bridges and fords—
All are visible.

Facing this evening scene,
Worthy of painting by the riverbank.
Three or four fishermen laugh at each other,
Cloaked and hooded, their songs ringing.
Pointing to tavern flags, they gather to drink.
Wide locks of hair adorned,
Gardens and paths of the woodcutter—
Even more bewitching,
Distant flocks of egrets and herons.
Outshining the white crane,
Worthy of the white pheasant’s elegance.

After the evening mist clears,
The slanted sun glows with silvered clouds.
The gate welcomes its light,
As if a jade palace of immortals.
A natural Zhurong arrives,
Radiant and resplendent.
Piercing the void beyond,
Kunlun’s gems are arrayed.

When night is still and the clear sky gleams,
A single wheel of bright moon ascends,
Its light intermingling.

**Tail Note:**
The world is entirely deluded,
Clinging to wealth and beauty,
None escape error.

One with sincere elixir-making,
Seizing the moment of ease—
The Four Seasons ever pursue pleasure,
Ever more frequent in their folly,
Like moths drawn to flame,
Ever seeking refuge in the light.
Only then do they awaken—
How can they undo their burned bodies?

Regret comes too late—
Already scorched by suffering.
Avoiding harm now,
How can one escape future calamity?
Preserving the body intact,
How can one endure the searing?

Look within—
Bound only by fame, wealth, and glory.

**Dissolving Sorrow:**
Worthy of lament—
The world’s confusion grows ever deeper,
How can one escape its snares?
All are equal in their praise,
Gathering and dispersing in turn.
Endless scheming,
A hundredfold entanglements.
These demonic messengers
Calculate your fate in secret.
Wait until it’s too late to see.

Foolish mortals.

The reckless race—
Clever, nimble, bold,
Unchecked in arrogance.
They meet the Sage with deceit,
Ignoring the divine, playing with the numinous.
This is but the karmic thread they weave—
How can they evade it?
Even escape is futile.
See the summons—
Each adds to their torment and woe.
All judgments are sealed by the underworld’s decree.

The green-headed duck#2 sighs at life’s fleeting light,
Chasing glory with swift haste.
Let not fame and name ensnare you—
No need for ceaseless toil.
This splendor, when it appears,
Is like a candle flame—
Never lasting, never firm.
Time presses like jade wheels turning,
Gold flees like swift winds,
While sorrow clings, relentless and tight.

Behold the transient world—
Pushed along through borrowed time,
As seasons shift and years flow.
All must abandon, all must let go—
Better to plant good roots,
To bind fate with virtuous ties.

The wisdom-blade swings—
Severing fierce return,
The keen intellect strikes—
Piercing through the virtuous and the wise.
One’s own voice can refine elegance,
Old melodies resonate—
Worthy to answer this string.

Recognize the primal source,
Seek the essence ever-present,
Subtle, profound—all merge into the Mysterious.
Attaining Oneness,
Eternal spring’s radiance remains,
As it ever was.
No coming, no going—
Within Penglai’s isle,
A Daoist immortal.

Lament the Yellow Flower—
The Great Sage often comes to save.
Yet as a mortal, I speak of the lineage.
A thunderclap beneath the earth,
Shakes rain from the mountain peaks.
Who knows the iron ox plows the soil?
Kan and Li, Zi and Wu—
Seizing dragons, capturing tigers.
Such deeds—none are truly yours,
For fate’s design prevails.
Outwit the clever traps,
But the limit’s number will claim you.
See which gate you enter.

Mortals must awaken,
Mortals must see.
If they fail to wake, fail to know—
The clever traps ensnare them still.
When Yama learns of it,
He sends a sly messenger.
To the underworld’s peaks,
They rush in their going.
Midway, tears flow endlessly.
They tell the ghostly attendants,
“Pause here for now.”
A small ghost shouts,
“Do not bury your wrongs.”
Before the judge,
Speak your full account.
The master dwells in the crimson palace,
Performing daily rites,
Locking doors, sealing homes.
Inside, gold is sown—
Each coin is yours to claim.
Good fortune regards—
Awaken now.
Reach the cool retreat,
Where thought dissolves entirely.
Wondrous within wonders,
Secretly revealing the Mysterious Speech.
Coming and returning,
Going and returning—
Never again tread the Penglai path.

**Again, the Ninth Day:**
A million reds wither,
Autumn’s edge sharp and lone.
A different hue—
Central splendor, uniquely bright.
Spare the Yellow Flower,
As the Ninth aligns with Heaven’s will.
Piercing thick frost,
Unfurling golden blossoms.
Beside the fence, Yuanming rejoices,
White-clad, he arrives.
Suddenly—
A Revere-the-Aged child emerges.
Seizing the pure fragrance,
Recognizing the auspicious sign.
Three branches plucked—
A Penglai drunkenness.
This Revere-the-Aged one,
Now born in this life.
Let go of strife,
Banish sorrow—
Adrift in ease.
A single incense suffices—
No need for three prostrations.
Nor the Daoist’s hollow rites.
Laugh at the sly messengers,
Laugh at the clever ones.
Laugh at those who vie—
Officials, merchants, farmers, scholars.
Only I, serene in stillness,
Only I, unbound in leisure.
Wherever I tread—
Clouds part beneath my feet.
The flower’s heart stirs.

The eastern dawn gradually ascends,
As harmonious brilliance meets refined clarity.

Little by little, the seasons shift—
Southern lands radiant with fiery sun,
Scorching heat, dazzling light.
Gradually, the western realm gathers golden splendor,
While the northern wheel congeals in dense purity.
